201 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Russ v. State


No. SC09-923


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


73 So. 3d 178; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2256; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 527



September 22, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Russ v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 2452 (Fla., Nov. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Marlene M. Alva, Judge - Case No. 2007CF2377A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida) to first-degree murder. Prior to the penalty phase, defendant waived his right to present mitigation and waived his right to a penalty phase jury. The trial court accepted his waiver and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered the victim after a several-days-long crack cocaine binge. After escaping from police, he climbed to the roof of a house and observed the victim leaving for work. He decided to kill her when she returned. He entered her house, ate her food, did laundry, and collected items to steal from her. When she returned home, he tied her up and killed her by strangling her, stabbing her, and striking her in the head with a blunt object as she lay facedown on her bathroom floor. He then left in her car with the stolen items, pawning them to obtain more crack. The court found that the trial court complied with the three-part procedure outlined in Koon v. Dugger for considering mitigation evidence, although defendant waived the presentation of mitigation evidence. The court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court failed to consider mental mitigation because the presentence investigation report did not alert the trial court to the probability of significant mental mitigation. The findings that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) and especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel (HAC), § 921.141(5)(i), Fla. Stat., were amply supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence.

Valle v. State

203 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Valle v. State


No. SC11-1387


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


70 So. 3d 530; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1951; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 461



August 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by, Motion granted by Valle v. Fla., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5211 (U.S., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County. Case No. F78-5281A. Jacqueline Hogan Scola, Judge.
Valle v. State, 70 So. 3d 525, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1841 (Fla., July 25, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which denied his amended successive motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, a prisoner under sentence of death, appealed the denial of his amended successive motion for postconviction relief. The supreme court affirmed, stating that he failed to satisfy the heavy burden that Florida's current lethal injection procedures were constitutionally defective in violation of U.S. Const. ament. VIII. The circuit court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion to strike the State's witnesses because the State's witnesses did not become irrelevant after the exclusion of the two reporters' affidavits; instead, their testimony served to rebut a doctor's account of the execution. The inmate's contention that because he was a Cuban national, that the State's failure to advise him of the right to notify his consulate of his arrest and to consult with that consulate or a diplomatic officer without delay under the Vienna Convention on Consular Relations entitled him to relief was both barred and without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

204 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Whiley v. Scott


No. SC11-592


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


79 So. 3d 702; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1900; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 451



August 16, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Whiley v. Scott, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1441 (Fla., June 17, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen brought a petition against respondent governor, seeking a writ of quo warranto directing the governor to demonstrate that he had not exceeded his authority, in part, by suspending agency rulemaking through Executive Order 11-01 and Executive Order 11-72.


OVERVIEW: The executive orders suspended and terminated rulemaking by precluding notice publication and other compliance with ch. 120, Fla. Stat. absent prior approval from the Office of Fiscal Accountability and Regulatory Reform (OFARR). The court found that to this extent, the executive orders, contrary to the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), infringed upon the process of rulemaking and encroached upon the legislature's delegation of its rulemaking power, and that the governor exceeded his constitutional authority. Separation of powers was recognized by Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const. Pursuant to §§ 120.52, 120.536(1), Fla. Stat. (2010), rulemaking was a derivative of lawmaking and was a legislative function. Pursuant to the APA, under § 120.54(3)(a)(1), Fla. Stat. (2010), agencies were required to provide notice prior to the adoption, amendment, or repeal of any rule (other than an emergency rule). Executive Order 11-72 mandated that agencies receive OFARR approval before taking any of the three rulemaking actions. The executive orders supplanted legislative delegations by redefining the terms of those delegations through binding directives to state agencies.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, but issuance of the writ of quo warranto was withheld.

 

205 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Am. Optical Corp. v. Spiewak


Nos. SC08-1616 & SC08-1640, Nos. SC08-1617 & SC08-1639


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


73 So. 3d 120; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1594; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P18,703; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 435



July 8, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Appeals from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. And two Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Palm Beach County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D07-405 and 4D07-407.
Williams v. Am. Optical Corp., 985 So. 2d 23, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 7532 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee claimants sued appellant companies for damages due to asbestos exposure. The trial court dismissed the suits for failing to meet the requirements of the Florida Asbestos and Silica Compensation Fairness Act (Act), tit. 45, ch. 774, pt. II, Fla. Stat. (2007). The Court of Appeal of Florida, Fourth District, found the Act unconstitutional as applied to the claimants, reversed, and certified a conflict. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether retroactive application of the Act to the claimants was permissible. The appellate court found that it was not. The claimants possessed a vested property interest in their right to pursue an action based on asbestos-related injuries. Prior to the Act, the development of particular impairment symptoms as described in the Act was never the legal factor in determining "manifestation" or accrual under Florida law. If there was proof of injury, there was no requirement of any particular level of impairment to bring a suit. Medical and X-ray reports confirmed that the claimants suffered from actual lung injuries that were consistent with asbestos-related disease. The claimants thus had an accrued cause of action, which constituted a property interest under Art. I, § 2, Fla. Const. Application of the Act to the claimants would have destroyed their vested rights in accrued causes of action for asbestos-related injury. The Act could not have been constitutionally applied to the claimants. The appellate court disapproved the decision of the Court of Appeal of Florida, Third District in DaimlerChrysler Corporation v. Hurst, 949 So. 2d 279 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2007).


OUTCOME: The holding of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

 

206 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Wyatt v. State


No. SC08-655, No. SC09-556


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


71 So. 3d 86; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1582; 92 A.L.R.6th 725; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 417



July 8, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 15, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Wyatt v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2223 (Fla., Sept. 15, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Wyatt v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2227 (Fla., Sept. 15, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Wyatt v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2259 (Fla., Sept. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Lisa Davidson, Judge -- Case No. 88-748CF(CTS 1-3).
Wyatt v. State, 641 So. 2d 1336, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1358 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Indian River County (Florida) denied an inmate's motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed and simultaneously petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was subject to a death sentence for three murders at a restaurant 15 years earlier. Defendant argued that a 2008 letter issued by the FBI was newly discovered evidence. The letter stated that the comparative bullet lead analysis (CBLA) conducted by the FBI on bullets used in the crime was flawed and that the science did not support the testimony of the State's witness. The court agreed that the letter was newly discovered evidence, although it was not in existence at the time of the inmate's trial but held that it would not have resulted in an acquittal given DNA and other evidence linking the inmate to the murders. The court rejected the inmate's claim that because the FBI had knowledge of the flaws in CBLA at the time of trial, the State's knowing presentation of the FBI agent's false testimony violated Giglio, because the State was unaware at that time of the flaws in CBLA. Similarly, the State's failure to disclose that the agent's testimony was unscientific and unsound did not violate Brady because the State was unaware of these facts. Also, defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the CBLA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the postconviction court's denial of relief and denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus.


 

207 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mendoza v. State


No. SC09-774


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


87 So. 3d 644; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1581; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 427



July 8, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 7, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Mendoza v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 914 (Fla., May 7, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Dava J. Tunis, Judge -- Case No. F92-994C.
Mendoza v. State, 700 So. 2d 670, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1530 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) convicted appellant inmate of, among other things, first-degree felony murder. The inmate was sentenced to death. The inmate then filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion for post conviction relief against appellee State, which the trial court denied. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: During a robbery committed by the inmate and two others, the victim was shot and killed. The inmate argued that he received ineffective assistance of trial counsel in both the guilt and penalty phases. The appellate court found that, while counsel's closing argument as to who fired the gun differed from that made during his opening statement, there was evidence supporting the defense theory that someone other than the inmate, either of his accomplices, committed the murder. The jury convicted the inmate of first-degree felony murder, and thus, the identity of the shooter in this case was not material. The inmate failed to show that the rationale in which counsel believed he decided not to call one of the accomplices was not supported by competent, substantial evidence or that counsel's strategy was unreasonable. Moreover, the inmate failed to demonstrate that the accomplice was an available witness at the time of trial. The inmate failed to demonstrate prejudice based upon counsel's failure to recognize different times that residue swabbings were done because, as the jury convicted the inmate of felony murder, the identity of the perpetrator who fired the gun was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

208 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


D.J. v. State


No. SC10-1852


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


67 So. 3d 1029; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1572; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 363



July 7, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Third District - Case No. 3D09-1965. (Dade County).
D.J. v. State, 43 So. 3d 176, 2010 Fla. App. LEXIS 13382 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a juvenile, was convicted for trespassing upon the grounds of a school facility in violation of § 810.097(2), Fla. Stat. (2009). The Court of Appeal of Florida, Third District, affirmed. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: At a bench trial, a security guard testified that she told petitioner that he would have to leave the school grounds. The next day, the witness again observed petitioner on school grounds. She notified the school's police officer, who arrested petitioner for trespassing. The appellate court held, however, that to prove that a defendant committed the first-degree misdemeanor set out in § 810.097(2), the State had to present evidence that the defendant was (1) warned to leave the premises by a specific person, and (2) that that person was either the principal of the school or one who had received authorization from the principal to restrict access to the property. The State presented no evidence that the school's security guard was a designee of the school's principal for the purposes of the trespass statute, or that the guard was in any way vested with authority to restrict access to the school's property. Further, the State cited no rule or statute indicating that a school security guard, by virtue of his or her title, would possess such authority as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The conviction was vacated and the case was remanded.

 

209 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



McCray v. State


No. SC08-2434


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


71 So. 3d 848; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1565; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 383



July 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 21, 2011.
Rehearing denied by McCray v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2257 (Fla., Sept. 21, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McCray v. Fla., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2188 (U.S., Mar. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Clay County, William Arthur Wilkes, Judge -- Case No. 04-1149-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Clay County (Florida) of four counts of first-degree murder. Following the penalty-phase proceeding, the jury unanimously recommended sentences of death for each of the four counts of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to death on each count, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant, a drug dealer, shot the victims because he believed they had contributed to his prior arrest for drug dealing. Defendant refused to cooperate with doctors appointed to evaluate his competency to stand trial. The trial court properly ruled from its own observations of defendant and from the opinion of one expert that defendant was competent. The other two experts could not rule out that defendant was malingering. The trial court did not err in refusing to allow defendant to represent himself because some of his requests for self-representation were equivocal, and when he was allowed to represent himself, he had to be removed from the courtroom for disruptive and obstreperous behavior. The State proved beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of two weighty statutory aggravating circumstances: that defendant was previously convicted of a capital felony, and that the crimes were committed in a cold and calculated and premeditated manner. Defendant presented no mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences of death.


 

210 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. State


No. SC09-549


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


71 So. 3d 802; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1568; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 395



July 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 21, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Baker v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2258 (Fla., Sept. 21, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Baker v. Florida, 565 U.S. 1237, 132 S. Ct. 1639, 182 L. Ed. 2d 238, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1801 (2012)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by, Writ of habeas corpus denied Baker v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 647 (Fla., Mar. 23, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Flagler County, Kim Crane Hammond, Judge -- Case No. 2007-00033-CFFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Flagler County (Florida) for murder, home invasion robbery with a firearm, kidnapping, and aggravated fleeing and eluding a law enforcement officer. The trial court determined that the aggravating circumstances far outweighed the mitigating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death for the charge of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forced his way into the victim's home, shot the victim in the head, then held the family at gunpoint for several hours. He then kidnapped the victim, stealing her car and attempting to steal money from her bank account. Finally, he drove the victim to a wooded area where he killed her by shooting her in the forehead at close range. The court held that defendant's confession, which he offered in exchange for getting to see his girlfriend, was not the product of improper coercion. This was not a quid pro quo offer not to prosecute, defendant was not threatened, and defendant himself proposed the deal. The court upheld the trial court's finding of aggravating factors that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated and that it was heinous, atrocious, and cruel under § 921.141(5), Fla. Stat. (2006). The trial court did not err in admitting victim impact statements from the victim's mother and four children pursuant to § 921.141(7), Fla. Stat. (2006).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and his sentence of death, as well as his additional convictions and sentences.

 

211 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Devon Neighborhood Ass'n


No. SC10-347


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


67 So. 3d 187; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1526; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 311



June 30, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fourth District - Case No. 4D09-377. (Broward County).
Fla. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Devon Neighborhood Ass'n, 33 So. 3d 48, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 18423 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent insured sued petitioner Florida Insurance Guaranty Association (FIGA), seeking payment on a property damage claim. The trial court denied the FIGA's motion to compel an appraisal. The Court of Appeal of Florida, Fourth District, affirmed. The FIGA appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court ruled that § 627.7015, Fla. Stat., as amended in 2005, applied retroactively to the 2004 commercial residential insurance policy issued by the original insurer and that the FIGA was bound by original insurer's failure to give the notice required in the amended statute. The appellate court agreed with the FIGA that a two-prong test for retroactivity analysis was proper and that the intermediate appellate court misapplied precedent in analyzing the question of retroactivity based solely on the second prong of the test. The intermediate appellate court did not inquire into whether there existed clear legislative intent for retroactive application of the 2005 amendments to § 627.7015. The enacting law specifically stated that the amendments were to be effective July 1, 2005, and there was no "clearly expressed legislative intent" to apply the amendments retroactively. Thus, the 2005 amendments did not apply retroactively to the 2004 insurance policy to bar FIGA's right to enforce the appraisal provision in that contract.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was quashed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

212 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Barwick v. State


No. SC07-1831, No. SC08-1377


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


88 So. 3d 85; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1518; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 347



June 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 7, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Barwick v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 909 (Fla., May 7, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Don T. Sirmons, Judge -- Case No. 86-940. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Barwick v. State, 660 So. 2d 685, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1151 (Fla., 1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida), which denied his motion to vacate his conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He further petitioned the supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed the denial of his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, and petitioned the supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus. The supreme court affirmed the judgment and denied the petition. At trial, counsel presented the testimony of family members as lay witnesses to establish the violent childhood experienced by the inmate and expert testimony to explain the effect of that environment on him. The fact that some of the testimony proved to be unfavorable to the inmate did not undermine the supreme court's confidence in the verdict; the inmate's own expert testified to many of the same prejudicial facts. The denial of habeas corpus petition was proper, in part because a jury instruction on the "avoid arrest" aggravator was properly given and appellate counsel could not be held ineffective for failing to raise a nonmeritorious issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

213 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Ballard v. State


No. SC08-2041


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


66 So. 3d 912; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1521; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 314



June 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by Ballard v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 923 (Fla., May 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Donald G. Jacobsen, Judge -- Case No. CF06-007863-XX.
State v. Ballard, 956 So. 2d 470, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 2610 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death; the supreme court reversed the death sentence, but affirmed his conviction. The victim was defendant's stepdaughter and after the investigation of her disappearance, authorities became convinced that defendant had killed her in order to gain custody of the victim's minor daughter and continue his sexual relationship with her. Although defendant claimed that the evidence relating to his sexual relationship with the victim's daughter was overly prejudicial and required a new trial, the supreme court disagreed, stating that the collateral crime evidence that defendant was engaged in an illegal sexual relationship with the daughter was relevant to establish motive and inextricably intertwined with the testimony of the chain of events. Additionally, the trial court did not err in finding under § 921.141(5)(i), Fla. Stat. (2009) that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated. However, the imposition of the death penalty in the case was disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the conviction but vacated and death sentence and reduced defendant's sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


 

214 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Lukehart v. State


Nos. SC09-961 & SC09-1788


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


70 So. 3d 503; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1425; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 297



June 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2011.
Motion denied by Lukehart v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2173 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, William Arthur Wilkes, Judge -- Case No. 16-1996-CF-2645AX.
Lukehart v. State, 776 So. 2d 906, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1903 (Fla., Sept. 28, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which denied his amended motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed the order denying his amended motion for postconviction relief. Through his postconviction motion, the inmate challenged his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. The supreme court affirmed and denied habeas relief, stating that the inmate failed to show that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel because trial counsel testified that there was no basis to set aside the plea and counsel had an ethical obligation not to file a frivolous motion. Further, to the extent that the inmate was really raising a residual or lingering doubt claim, Florida did not recognize residual doubt, much less residual doubt as to the aggravators. Counsel could not be ineffective for failing to pursue a meritless claim. Because the exclusionary rule was not a remedy for a violation of § 394.453, Fla. Stat. (1995) unless a constitutional violation had also occurred, even if trial counsel had raised that argument in the inmate's motion to suppress, the motion still would have been denied and its denial affirmed on appeal on that basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and habeas relief was denied.


 

215 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Pham v. State


No. SC08-2355


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


70 So. 3d 485; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1346; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 259



June 16, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 9, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Pham v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2185 (Fla., Sept. 9, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pham v. Florida, 132 S. Ct. 1752, 182 L. Ed. 2d 541, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2278 (U.S., 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Pham v. State, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 2475 (Fla., Nov. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Marlene M. Alva, Judge - Case No. 2005CF4717A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree murder (§ 782.04, Fla. Stat. (2005)) and his death sentence on direct appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found competent, substantial evidence to support defendant's conviction of first-degree murder of his estranged wife, under theories of premeditated or felony murder, as defendant entered her apartment without permission intending to kill her, and once inside he dragged his stepdaughter by the hair into her bedroom and bound her to keep her from escaping or warning the victim. He then waited for approximately one hour for the victim to return home and stabbed the victim repeatedly without provocation. The stepdaughter testified to observing defendant strike the victim with one of the knives he had brought. Defendant claimed that jurors were not willing to accept his mitigation based on his upbringing and societal differences in Vietnam, but the juror comments in question did not rise to the level of ethnic bias. The statements made were not open appeals to the bias in others. The victim was conscious during at least part of her attack and was stabbed at least six times. The attack was unprovoked and witnessed by her daughter. Accordingly, there was competent, substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding of the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

216 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Rigterink v. State


No. SC05-2162


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


66 So. 3d 866; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1343; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 273



June 16, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Rigterink v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 835 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Dale Durrance, Judge - Case No. CF03-006982-XX.
Rigterink v. State, 2 So. 3d 221, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 151 (Fla., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Polk county (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after he was convicted and sentenced for first-degree murder, but the supreme court affirmed, stating that the Miranda warnings administered to him by the police were sufficient under Miranda and its progeny because they reasonably conveyed defendant's right to counsel both before and during a custodial interrogation. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding testimony under § 90.405(1), Fla. Stat. because the testimony concerning an individual who had provided an alibi appeared to have been based on mere personal opinion, fleeting encounters, or rumor, which was insufficient to satisfy § 90.405(1)'s admissibility predicate. The evidence was sufficient because defendant's bloody fingerprints were found at the scene, and the police found DNA under the fingernails of one of the victims that was consistent with defendant's DNA. Further, police found blood in defendant's truck that was genetically consistent with that of one of the victims. There was also eyewitness descriptions of two men in an altercation outside the warehouse where the bodies were found that were consistent with the physical appearances of defendant and one of the victims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

217 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Hernandez


No. SC08-2330, No. SC08-2394


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


74 So. 3d 1070; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1282; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 243



June 9, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised November 10, 2011
Motion denied by Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Hernandez, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2695 (Fla., Nov. 10, 2011)
On remand at, Writ of certiorari granted, Remanded by McLaughlin v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2012 Fla. App. LEXIS 3776 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Duval County). First District - Case No. 1D08-1424.

Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Polk County). Second District - Case No. 2D07-4891.
Hernandez v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 995 So. 2d 1077, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17595 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)
McLaughlin v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 9898 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 2, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In combined cases, petitioner department suspended the driver's licenses of respondent licensees based on refusals to take breath tests, and the licensees sought review. The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, found that a suspension was proper only if the refusal was incident to a lawful arrest. However, the Court of Appeal of Florida, Second District, reached an opposite conclusion and upheld the suspension. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first rephrased certified question asked if the department was allowed to suspend a license under § 322.2615, Fla. Stat. for refusal to submit to a breath test if the refusal was not incident to a lawful arrest. The second certified question asked if the issue of whether the refusal was incident to a lawful arrest was within the allowable scope of review of a department hearing officer in a proceeding to determine if sufficient cause existed to sustain a suspension under § 322.2615 for refusal to submit. The appellate court found that § 322.2615 authorized the department to suspend the driver's license of a person who refused to submit to a "lawful" breath test. The only definition of a lawful breath test under § 322.2615 was found in § 316.1932(1)(a), Fla. Stat. The statutes were read in pari materia. A "lawful test" under § 322.2615 was one that was requested incident to a lawful arrest, as specified in § 316.1932. Further, the only reading that avoided an unreasonable and unconstitutional result was to construe §§ 322.2615, 316.1932, in pari materia and allow the hearing officer to review whether a breath test was administered incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court answered the first rephrased certified question in the negative and the second question in the affirmative. The decision of the Court of Appeal of Florida, Second District, was quashed. The decision of the Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, was approved.

Coleman v. State


No. SC04-1520, No. SC09-92


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


64 So. 3d 1210; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1251; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 227



June 2, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Nicholas P. Geeker, Judge -- Case No. 8901139C-CF.
Coleman v. State, 610 So. 2d 1283, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2146 (Fla., 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which denied his motion to vacate his convictions for first-degree murder and sentences of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He also filed petitions for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed an order denying his motion to vacate his convictions of first-degree murder and sentences of death and petitioned the supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus. The supreme court reversed the denial of postconviction relief as it pertained to the inmate's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase because counsel rendered ineffective assistance during the penalty phase when counsel failed to investigate, develop, and present available mitigating evidence that would have legally precluded an override of the jury's life recommendation. Therefore, his death sentences were vacated and the supreme court remanded for the imposition of life instead. The inmate's petition for habeas corpus was denied. The inmate's trial counsel failed to conduct any investigation into possible mitigation. A reasonable investigation would have revealed substantial mitigation. Further, the record did not reflect that, at any time, the inmate actively concealed mitigating factors or that he instructed counsel not to pursue an investigation of mitigation.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the denial of relief as it pertained to the inmate's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase, vacated the death sentences, and remanded for the imposition of life sentences instead. His petition for habeas corpus was denied.

Hildwin v. State


No. SC09-1417


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


84 So. 3d 180; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1254; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 234



June 2, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 28, 2011.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County. Case No. 85-499-CF. Richard Tombrink, Jr., Judge.
Hildwin v. State, 727 So. 2d 193, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1678 (Fla., 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief attacking his death sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief but the supreme court affirmed. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

220 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Harris v. State


No. SC08-1871


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


71 So. 3d 756; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 953; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 163



April 21, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 22, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Harris v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2253 (Fla., Sept. 22, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Florida v. Harris, 132 S. Ct. 1796, 182 L. Ed. 2d 615, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2335 (U.S., 2012)
Reversed by Florida v. Harris, 133 S. Ct. 1050, 185 L. Ed. 2d 61, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 1121 (U.S., 2013)
Opinion withdrawn by Harris v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2140 (Fla., Oct. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Liberty County). First District - Case No. 1D06-6497.
Harris v. State, 989 So. 2d 1214, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 13719 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after his motion to suppress was denied, entered a plea of no contest in the trial court to possession of the listed chemical pseudoephedrine with intent to use it to manufacture methamphetamine, in violation of § 893.149(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2006). Defendant reserved the right to appeal the denial of the suppression motion. The trial court imposed a sentence. The First District of Appeals of Florida affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether probable cause existed for the warrantless search of defendant's vehicle, following a traffic stop, based on a drug-detection dog's alert to the vehicle. On appeal, the court found that the State of Florida failed to present sufficient evidence to meet its burden to establish probable cause to have conducted the warrantless search of defendant's truck. The State did not meet its burden in demonstrating that a police officer had a reasonable basis for believing that the dog was reliable at the time of the search and, thus, that the dog's alert, the lynch-pin of the probable cause analysis in the case, indicated a fair probability that drugs were to be found in defendant's vehicle. In the absence of a reliable alert, the other factors considered in the totality of circumstances analysis -- defendant's expired car license tag; defendant's shaking, breathing rapidly, and inability to sit still; and defendant's open beer can -- did not rise to the level of probable cause that there were illegal drugs inside the vehicle. Accordingly, the search of defendant's vehicle violated the Fourth Amendment's prohibition on unreasonable searches and seizures.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion to suppress was reversed. The case was remanded for proceedings.


 

221 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Bar v. Adorno


No. SC09-1012


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


60 So. 3d 1016; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 952; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 174



April 21, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Fla. Bar v. Adorno, 48 So. 3d 837, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1818 (Fla., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant, the Florida Bar, brought a disciplinary action against respondent attorney. A referee recommended that the attorney was to be found guilty of violating R. Regulating Fla. Bar 4-1.7, 4-1.5, and 4-8.4. The referee recommended that the attorney was to receive a public reprimand. The Florida Bar petitioned for review of the recommended sanction. The attorney filed a cross-petition for review of the recommendations of guilt.


OVERVIEW: The disciplinary case arose from an underlying civil case seeking class certification for alleged improper assessment fees imposed by a city on property owners. The attorney represented clients in the class action. The referee found that the attorney took an excessive fee when he settled with individual plaintiffs to the detriment of the putative class. The referee concluded that the attorney breached a fiduciary duty owed to the putative class and prejudiced that class when he settled on behalf of individual plaintiffs to the detriment of the putative class. The state supreme court found that the attorney's actions regarding the disproportionate settlement amount, as well as the terms of the settlement, created a conflict of interest that prejudiced the remaining class members. Further, the attorney abandoned the putative class via his settlement negotiations, hid the terms of the settlement agreement from the class through a nondisclosure agreement, and stopped litigating on behalf of the class as a result of the standstill agreement. The attorney's actions violated the Rules Regulating the Florida Bar which the referee cited. However, a more substantial sanction was warranted.


OUTCOME: The referee's findings of fact, recommendations of guilt, and award of costs were approved. The referee's recommendation of a public reprimand was disapproved, and the attorney was suspended from the practice of law for three years.


 

222 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Silvia v. State


No. SC09-220


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


60 So. 3d 959; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 779; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 138



April 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Silvia v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1995 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Donna L. McIntosh, Judge -- Case No. 2006CF4522A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida), which convicted him of the first-degree murder of his estranged wife and the attempted first-degree murder of her mother. He appealed his conviction and death sentence for the first-degree murder of his estranged wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence for the first-degree murder of his estranged wife, but the supreme court affirmed, stating that the State presented evidence that he confessed to the officer transporting him to jail that he shot his wife because she spent all of their money and then started dating her ex-husband. That constituted direct evidence of defendant's guilt. Moreover, several witnesses testified that defendant was firing a shotgun near the carport of the home of the victim's mother on the night in question, resulting in the victim's death. Evidence also established that shells collected at the crime scene were fired from the shotgun found in defendant's motel room. The cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravating factor was properly applied because, although defendant and the victim had recently separated, the record lacked evidence showing the type of an ongoing, highly emotional dispute needed to refute a finding of cool and calm reflection. Further, when compared with other capital cases, the death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johnston v. State


No. SC09-780, No. SC10-75


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


63 So. 3d 730; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 671; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 122



March 24, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Johnston v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1287 (Fla., June 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Rex Martin Barbas, Judge - Case No. CR07-13379C And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Johnston v. State, 841 So. 2d 349, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2576 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Florida, that denied his postconviction motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and the sentence of death imposed. Petitioner also applied for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court rejected petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel as a basis for relief. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the issue of juror misconduct after it was discovered that the jury foreperson had been charged with and pled nolo contendere to a charge of civil contempt because there was nothing about the nonviolent offense that suggested that the juror would be biased against a defendant pleading not guilty in a death penalty case. Further, defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to move to suppress defendant's statement to the police because counsel's decision was a reasonable and strategic choice in that, short of calling defendant to testify, there was no available evidence aside from that statement that could explain defendant's possession and use of the victim's ATM card. Further, counsel could not be deemed ineffective because any motion to suppress would have been meritless. The record established that defendant's initial statement was voluntary; as such, no Miranda warnings were required until defendant was formally arrested.


OUTCOME: The order denying postconviction relief was affirmed, and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences of death, but the supreme court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient. The State introduced circumstantial evidence of an elaborate plan to establish an alibi, a plan that defendant had developed and begun to implement ahead of time. That victim was personally known to defendant and he speculated that the victim was not the target of the crime, but rather a witness who had to be eliminated. The supreme court had also found that the death penalty was proportionate in cases where the totality of the circumstances was similar to the totality of the current circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dufour v. State

69 So. 3d 235; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 289; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 57

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Dufour v. Fla., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 936 (U.S., Jan. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Lawrence Kirkwood, Judge -- Case No. 82-5467.
Dufour v. State, 495 So. 2d 154, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2617 (Fla., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which, in ruling on the inmate's petition for postconviction relief from a capital conviction, concluded that the inmate was not mentally retarded pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203 and 3.851.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that the circuit court erred in determining that he was not mentally retarded in accordance with the definition set forth in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203 and § 921.137(1), Fla. Stat. (2005). The court concluded that the circuit court incorrectly applied the standard error of measurement to the IQ score reached by one of the three experts in the case. There was some reasonable possibility that the error affected the circuit court's determination of the inmate's intellectual functioning. However, the inmate could not establish all three prongs of the applicable test to be excluded from the death penalty based on mental retardation as he failed to establish that he demonstrated deficient adaptive functioning. The inmate's handling of the leasing of his apartment, his administration of household chores, his daily maintenance of personal hygiene, his work to secure a GED diploma, and his serving as an aide in an engine repair class in addition to organizing and developing lesson plans for a motorcycle repair shop showed that he had the ability to live independently in society. Finally, the circuit court did not commit prejudicial error in its admission of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court.

State v. Fleming


No. SC06-1173


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


61 So. 3d 399; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 331; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 50



February 3, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Clarified by State v. Fleming, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 995 (Fla., Apr. 28, 2011)
On remand at Fleming v. State, 2012 Fla. App. LEXIS 5817 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 17, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Columbia County). First District - Case No. 1D05-3411.
Fleming v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5735 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 21, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, aggravated battery with great bodily harm, permanent disability, or permanent disfigurement, and was sentenced. Following an earlier appeal and remand, defendant was resentenced. The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, reversed the sentence, holding that, among other things, the trial court's finding of upward departure grounds on resentencing violated Apprendi and Blakely. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether, in cases in which the convictions were final before Apprendi issued, Apprendi and Blakely applied to resentencings held after Apprendi issued where the resentencing was not final when Blakely issued. The intermediate appellate court held that Apprendi and Blakely applied in such cases. The appellate court agreed. Where a sentence was reversed or vacated, the resentencings were de novo in nature, and the full panoply of due process considerations attached. Applying Apprendi and Blakely to such a resentencing did not constitute retroactive application. Here, defendant's his pre-Apprendi sentence was vacated because it was illegal. As a result, defendant was resentenced in a de novo proceeding, and Apprendi and Blakely were applicable. Galindez v. State, 910 So. 2d 284 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2005), Cutts v. State, 940 So. 2d 1246 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2006), quashed on other grounds, 976 So. 2d 579 (Fla. 2008), Lester v. State, 923 So. 2d 596 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2006), quashed on other grounds, 976 So. 2d 577 (Fla. 2008), and Hamilton v. State, 914 So. 2d 993 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2005), quashed on other grounds, 976 So. 2d 575, 576 (Fla. 2008) were overruled.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

228 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Franqui v. State


No. SC05-830


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


59 So. 3d 82; 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1; 36 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



January 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 11, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Franqui v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 875 (Fla., Apr. 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Paul Lawrence Backman, Judge ??Case No. 92-6089-B&C CF06.
Franqui v. State, 14 So. 3d 238, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1121 (Fla., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The inmate then filed a motion against appellee State, seeking to vacate the conviction and the sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) denied the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate initially argued that the trial court's interpretation of mental retardation, mandating a cut-off IQ score of 70 or below to meet the first prong of the test for mental retardation in capital sentencing, was contrary to case law and the Eighth Amendment. The appellate court found that there was competent, substantial evidence that the inmate was not mentally retarded. The language of § 921.137(1), Fla. Stat. was clear and unambiguous in mandating a strict cut-off IQ score of two standard deviations from the mean score, which was exactly 70. The inmate also alleged that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to comments made by the prosecutor in both the guilt and the penalty phase. These claims were without merit. The inmate's motion failed to establish how these alleged instances of ineffective assistance of counsel prejudiced him. In addition, the majority of the prosecutorial argument alleged to be improper was fair comment on the evidence or inferences arising from the evidence, or was proper response to argument of defense counsel. Counsel's decision not to present the testimony of a specific psychologist might have been sound trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed the order denying his postconviction motion to vacate his convictions of first-degree murder and sentences of death. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his first-degree murder conviction and death sentenced entered by the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Fla.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the strangulation murder of a woman. Defendant was also indicted on five other counts of first degree murder. PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Terry David Terrell, Judge -- Case No. 2003-CF5683A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the trial court's finding that the evidence established that he did not experience concurrent deficits in adaptive behavior for purposes of § 921.137, Fla. Stat. and Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203. The appellate court found that the trial court's findings on this issue were supported by competent, substantial evidence. Among other things, several witnesses testified about defendant's daily living and other capabilities, experts opined about defendant's adaptive functioning, and the trial court made lengthy findings based on the evidence presented. Defendant functioned well at home and was capable of traveling independently to and from work and appointments with his parole officer and from Ohio to Alabama and Florida. The planning of the murder and the cover-up also supported the trial court's findings. The collateral crime evidence showing that defendant committed a separate murder did not become a feature of the trial and was not improper. The evidence was sufficient to find defendant guilty of first-degree murder both on the theory of premeditated murder and on the theory of felony murder.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.


 

233 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Greenfield v. Daniels


No. SC09-1675, No. SC09-1676


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


51 So. 3d 421; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 2012; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 685



November 24, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fourth District - Case No. 4D08-3612. (Palm Beach County).
Daniels v. Greenfield, 15 So. 3d 908, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 10724 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent representative of a decedent's estate sued appellants doctor and medical center, alleging wrongful death. The complaint sought, inter alia, relief for a child alleged to be the decedent's biological son. The trial court entered summary judgment for the doctor and the medical center on the child's claims. The Court of Appeal of Florida, Fourth District reversed and certified a conflict. The doctor and the medical center appealed.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother was married to someone other than the decedent when the child was conceived and born, the mother's husband's paternal rights had not been divested, and the husband was not a party to this suit. The doctor and the medical center argued that the reference to "father" in § 768.18(1), Fla. Stat. (2005) meant the legal father, defined as the husband of the woman who gave birth, if the woman was in fact married at the time. However, the appellate court found that § 768.18(1) did not require a legal determination of paternity, but merely required recognition by the biological father of a responsibility of support. A formal adjudication of a legal relationship between the child and the decedent under ch. 742, Fla. Stat. was not a prerequisite for the child to bring a claim under ch. 768, Fla. Stat. If it was proven that the child was the decedent's biological child for whom the decedent recognized a responsibility for support, the child's survivor's claim vested at the decedent's death, without the need for a formal adjudication of a legal relationship being made before his death. Achumba v. Neustein, 793 So. 2d 1013 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2001) was disapproved.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

234 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Kilgore v. State


No. SC09-257, No. SC09-1552


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


55 So. 3d 487; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1976; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 665



November 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Kilgore v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 438 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Joseph Rogers Padgett, Judge. Case No. CF89-0686A1-XX.
Kilgore v. State, 688 So. 2d 895, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1425 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) denying his amended motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 38.50, challenging his capital murder conviction and sentence of death, pursuant to § 921.141, Fla. Stat. (1995). Defendant also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: First, on his motion for postconviction relief, defendant failed to demonstrate ineffective assistance of counsel due to counsel's failure to adequately investigate and prepare the defense. Defendant failed under the second prong of Strickland to allege how he was prejudiced by counsel's alleged failures. Second, trial counsel made a reasonable strategic decision not to request individual voir dire with regard to issues of race and homosexuality. Third, no Brady violation occurred. Fourth, competent, substantial evidence clearly supported the postconviction court's finding that defendant was not mentally retarded. Although defendant scored 67 on one IQ test, evidence revealed that the score was unreliable. Three scores of 74, 75, and 76 appeared to be the scores most representative as to whether defendant possessed subaverage general intellectual functioning. Fifth, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203, which specified the procedure for raising mental retardation as a bar to a death sentence, was constitutional. Finally, defendant failed to meet his burden on any of his claims of ineffective assistance of counsel in his habeas petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion for postconviction relief. It denied relief on defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus.

McGirth v. State


No. SC08-976


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


48 So. 3d 777; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1935; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 651



November 10, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McGirth v. Florida, 563 U.S. 940, 131 S. Ct. 2100, 179 L. Ed. 2d 898, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3133 (2011)
Related proceeding at, Writ denied by, Stay denied by McGirth v. State, 145 So. 3d 826, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1702 (Fla., 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by McGirth v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 195 (Fla., Jan. 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Brian Lambert, Judge - Case No. 2006-CF-2999-A-W.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder with a firearm, robbery with a firearm, and fleeing or eluding a law enforcement officer, and sentencing him, pursuant to § 921.141, Fla. Stat., to death.


OVERVIEW: Competent, substantial evidence existed to support each of defendant's convictions where he participated in the armed robber of two victims, shot one victim in the chest, and then approximately fifteen to thirty minutes later returned to the home and shot both victims in the backs of their heads. Further, defendant fled to elude police and led them on a high-speed vehicular chase. Defendant was 18 years old at the time of the murder. Evidence that defendant had a drug-based relationship with the victim's daughter was not similar fact evidence and, thus, was not irrelevant Williams rule evidence subject to the requirements of § 90.404, Fla. Stat. (2006), but rather was relevant pursuant to § 90.402, Fla. Stat. (2006), to establish the context in which the charged criminal acts occurred. Next, the trial court did not err in the penalty phase in admitting victim impact evidence or in finding the following aggravators: avoid arrest; cold, calculated, and premeditated; and heinous, atrocious, or cruel. Further, § 921.141, Fla. Stat. did not violate Ring or related cases. Lastly, the death sentence was proportionate and not in violation of Art. I, § 17, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

236 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Crist v. Ervin


No. SC10-1317, No. SC10-1319


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


56 So. 3d 745; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1858; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 637



November 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 4, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Crist v. Ervin, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 135 (Fla., Jan. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified Judgments of Trial Courts in and for Leon County - Frank Elwyn Sheffield, Judge, Case No. 2009-CA-001386 - An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D10-2972.
Crist v. Ervin, 38 So. 3d 770, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1264 (Fla., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees brought an action against appellant State, challenging statutes directing portions of civil filing fees to the general revenue fund. The trial court entered summary judgment declaring unconstitutional and void §§ 28.241(1)(a)(1)(a), 28.241(1)(a)(2)(d), 28.241(2), 34.041(1)(b), 28.2455, Fla. Stat. (2009). The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, certified that the judgment was of great public importance. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the statutes imposed an unconstitutional tax because filing fees were sent to the general revenue fund to be spent on unrelated government activities, and denied access to courts. The State asserted that the statutes were facially constitutional because the legislature appropriated more to the costs of the administration of justice than the amount of civil filing fees deposited into the general revenue fund. The appellate court held that there was no requirement in the Florida Constitution that the very money paid for filing fees be used to fund the administration of justice. Thus, the statutes, on their face, were not an unconstitutional tax. Further, because the legislature appropriated more to support the administration of justice than the amount of civil fees deposited into the general fund, the statutes were applied in a constitutional manner and were not operating as an unconstitutional tax. The filing fee statutes at issue were not contrary to Art. V, § 14, Fla. Const. There was not competent substantial evidence to support the trial court's determination that Florida courts were inadequately funded.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the injunction was lifted.

Jones v. Fla. Parole Comm'n

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought a habeas corpus petition against respondent commission. The trial court dismissed the petition. Const. granted the Supreme Court of Florida the exclusive authority to set deadlines for postconviction motions.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was quashed and the decisions of the Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, and Court of Appeal of Florida, Second District, were approved.

Everett v. State


No. SC08-1636, No. SC09-646


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


54 So. 3d 464; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1731; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 587



October 14, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Everett v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 335 (Fla., Feb. 10, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Don T. Sirmons, Judge -- Case No. 01-2956C.
Everett v. State, 893 So. 2d 1278, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2119 (Fla., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida), which denied his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed an order of the circuit court denying his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. The supreme court affirmed and denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus. It was impossible for an assistant public defender to have been representing the inmate at the time that he made the statements at issue in Alabama. Because the public defender was not yet representing the inmate as defined by Florida Law, the public defender was not yet responsible for advising the inmate. Based on the factual circumstances of the crimes that the inmate clearly recollected, the aggravation and mitigation found by the sentencing court, and precedent, the additional evidence of the inmate's substance abuse and paranoia presented at the postconviction evidentiary hearing did not undermine confidence in his sentence. He failed to prove the ineffective assistance of counsel, in part because a lieutenant's testimony would not have been favorable. Thus, the inmate could not possibly have been prejudiced by the public defender's failure to secure that testimony.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the order and denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Abdool v. State


No. SC08-944


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


53 So. 3d 208; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1637; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 571



October 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Abdool v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 224 (Fla., Jan. 25, 2011)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Lisa T. Munyon, Judge -- Case No. 48-2006-CF-002848-O.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder and his resulting death sentence, but the supreme court affirmed, stating that there was substantial evidence to have inferred premeditation by defendant. Three witnesses testified that defendant spoke of killing the victim or her baby several months before the actual killing took place, and on the night of the crime, while the victim waited in his car, defendant stopped at a convenience store and purchased duct tape, a gas can, and gasoline, which were the tools that he eventually used to kill her. Testimony by the victim's father was proper under § 90.401, Fla. Stat. and § 90.402, Fla. Stat. (2009). His testimony that the victim was not allowed to date was relevant to the fact that she snuck out of her bedroom window to meet defendant and the father's testimony that he searched for the victim for six days was helpful in providing the jury with a context of the timeline involved in the investigation surrounding her disappearance. Further, the death sentence was appropriate because it was proportionate and because the murder was heinous, atrocious or cruel and was committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Geralds v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


111 So. 3d 778; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1540; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 503



September 16, 2010, Decided

Rehearing denied by Geralds v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 239 (Fla., Feb. 2, 2012)
Rehearing denied by Geralds v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 616 (Fla., Apr. 8, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Don T. Sirmons, Judge - Case No. 89-495. And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Geralds v. State, 674 So. 2d 96, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 141 (Fla., Feb. 22, 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder. After an earlier appeal and remand, and a new penalty phase hearing, the jury unanimously recommended death. The Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida) sentenced the inmate to death. Later, the trial court denied the inmate's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 postconviction motion. The inmate appealed. The inmate also filed a habeas corpus petition.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued, among other things, that the trial court erred in denying his claim that the State violated Brady when it failed to disclose various reports and information. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's finding that the inmate failed to establish that certain items were not produced, including list of jewelry missing from the victim's home, a laboratory report, and a photo of a photo of a shoe print. As to any criminal charges against a pawnbroker, the inmate failed to establish that there were any deals between the State and the pawnbroker, and further, even if this evidence should have been disclosed, there was no prejudice because the pawnbroker's testimony did not contradict the inmate's theory of the case. The inmate also failed to establish his Giglio claims and his habeas corpus claims.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's postconviction motions was affirmed. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

242 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Dep't of State v. Mangat


No. SC10-1527


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


43 So. 3d 642; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1451; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 463



August 31, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified Judgments of Trial Courts in and for Leon County -- James Oliver Shelfer, Judge, Case No. 2010-CA-002202 -- An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D10-4067.
Fla. Dep't of State v. Mangat, 39 So. 3d 320, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1331 (Fla., Aug. 4, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Secretary of State appealed an order by the Second Judicial Circuit Court (Florida) that determined a ballot summary for a proposed constitutional amendment was misleading and should be removed from the ballot of the general election; the secretary of state asked that the text of the proposed amendment be substituted for the misleading ballot summary.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found, and the secretary of state agreed, that the introduction of the ballot summary was misleading in that it mentioned waiting lists for doctors and doctor-patient confidentiality, while the amendment itself said nothing about them. In addition, neither the summary nor the amendment explained what mandates were at issue, why they did not work, or for whom the mandates did not work. The state supreme court found, inter alia, that the ballot summary did not comply with the requirements for accuracy in § 101.161(1), Fla. Stat. (2009) and Art. XI, § 5, Fla. Const. Because the Legislature did not resolve to place the entire text of the proposed amendment on the ballot, the remedy of substitution was not available. Accordingly, the only remedy was to strike the proposal from the ballot, thereby removing it from a vote of the electorate.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Schoenwetter v. State


No. SC08-2271, No. SC09-955


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


46 So. 3d 535; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1051; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 409



July 1, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Schoenwetter v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1729 (Fla., Oct. 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, John M. Griesbaum, Judge -- Case No. 05-2000-CF-041829-AX. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Schoenwetter v. State, 931 So. 2d 857, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 668 (Fla., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which denied his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 to vacate his convictions for first-degree murder and sentences for death. Defendant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his counsel was ineffective by failing to move to exclude from the penalty phase certain statements made at a hearing and a plea colloquy. The court held that the statements made at the hearing were admissible as party admissions under § 90.803(18), Fla. Stat., and the statements were not made in connection with an offer to plead guilty. The statements made at the plea colloquy were made in open court, before a judge, after defense counsel advised defendant on the record to maintain his silence. Because Miranda warnings were only necessary prior to a custodial police interrogation, the absence of such warnings could not provide defense counsel with grounds for an objection. In his petition for writ of habeas corpus, defendant asserted that his sentence of death was unconstitutional due to evolving standards of decency. The court noted that the claims were procedurally barred as they could have been raised in his motion filed under Rule 3.851. Defendant made no assertion that he suffered from mental retardation, rather he only claimed diagnoses of Asperger's Syndrome, ADHD and frontal lobe damage, and mental illness did not serve as a bar to execution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Fla.) that denied his successive postconviction motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851.

245 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Bar v. Behm


No. SC07-661


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


41 So. 3d 136; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1044; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 419



July 1, 2010, Decided


NOTICE:

THE FILING OF A MOTION FOR REHEARING SHALL NOT ALTER THE EFFECTIVE DATE OF THIS DISBARMENT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Fla. Bar v. Behm, 918 So. 2d 293, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2515 (Fla., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant state bar brought a disciplinary action against respondent attorney alleging professional misconduct. The referee recommended that the attorney be found guilty of professional misconduct related to trust account violations and failure to file income tax returns since the time he became a lawyer. The referee also recommended that the attorney be suspended from the practice of law for six months.


OVERVIEW: The bar alleged that the attorney failed to prepare and maintain certain required trust account records and failed to file federal income tax returns and to pay federal income taxes from 1999 to 2006, despite having taxable income exceeding the threshold amount triggering the legal obligation to file. The referee found that the facts had been proven by clear and convincing evidence. The supreme court found that there was competent, substantial record evidence that the attorney was required to file federal income tax returns and that he had taxable income for the tax years 1999 to 2006. There was no support for the attorney's time-as-life-capital argument and this argument had been expressly rejected and labeled frivolous by the federal courts. As such, the attorney did not have a good faith belief that he was not obligated to file federal tax returns. The attorney should be permanently disbarred because he engaged in a lengthy course of conduct to impede and obstruct the collection of income taxes on his own income, for his own personal gain and declared his intention to persist in refusing to file income tax returns.


OUTCOME: The court approved the referee's findings of fact and recommendations of guilt, but disapproved the recommendations of sanction and, instead, permanently disbarred the attorney from the practice of law in Florida.

Turner v. State


No. SC08-975


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


37 So. 3d 212; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 800; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 281



May 20, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turner v. Fla., 131 S. Ct. 426, 178 L. Ed. 2d 332, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8242 (U.S., Oct. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Jones County, Wendy Williams Berger, Judge - Case No. 2005-01954-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for St. Jones County (Florida), which, after a second trial, convicted him of first-degree murder and which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his double jeopardy rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and art. I, § 9, Fla. Const., were violated. He also claimed that his crime was not cold, calculated, and premeditated. Upon review, the court held that because defendant, after consideration discussion with his counsel, chose to ask for a mistrial and there was no goading by the prosecution, the State was not barred from proceeding to a subsequent trial. Furthermore, one of the jurors suffered a seizure during deliberations which was an event that would qualify as an illness of a juror. In addition, the court found that defendant was fully cognizant of his actions, even exchanging pleasantries with a housekeeper. After his attack, defendant was able to locate the keys of the victim's truck, proceed directly to the truck, and drive away. Later he made a conscious decision to ram a police vehicle and attempt to elude capture. Finally, the court found that the death penalty was proportionate for the crime and that the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Rodriguez v. State
