CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which denied his petition for postconviction relief. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed the circuit court's order denying his motion to vacate his convictions of first-degree murder and sentences of death, and he also petitioned the supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus. The supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and also denied habeas relief. The inmate argued a Brady violation because the State failed to disclose two letters that a jail inmate wrote to the prosecutor, prior to trial, alleging that the brother of the inmate's girlfriend would lie. Although the supreme court agreed that the letters should have been disclosed, the inmate failed to establish prejudice. The jury was aware that the brother had entered a plea in order to avoid the death penalty. Accordingly, the defense was unable to show how the inmate was prejudiced by the failure to turn over the letters. Because there was competent evidence supporting the finding that no evidence was introduced to show that the brother's brother was threatened or promised favors in exchange for his cooperation, defense counsel could not have been considered ineffective for failing to impeach on evidence that did not exist.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of relief on the motion for postconviction relief and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

248 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Clark v. State


No. SC07-2318


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


35 So. 3d 880; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 648; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 230



April 29, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, David Cary Wiggins, Judge -- Case No. 90-10067-CF-CRB.
Clark v. State, 613 So. 2d 412, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2109 (Fla., 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which denied a motion to vacate a judgment of conviction of first-degree murder and a sentence of death under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851.


OVERVIEW: In his motion for postconviction relief, the inmate asserted that his counsel was ineffective. Upon review, the court found that counsel could not be ineffective for failing to investigate and present evidence that another defendant was the shooter because no such evidence existed. The inmate's claim that counsel was ineffective for failing to present mitigation at the penalty phase of his trial was procedurally barred because it was found to be without merit on direct appeal. Because counsel did not fail to investigate mitigation and the inmate was found competent, counsel could not be found deficient for his strategy. Further, the inmate failed to establish prejudice. Accordingly, the inmate failed to establish that his trial counsel was ineffective. In addition, the inmate claimed that there was newly discovered evidence. However because the inmate failed to raise the claim within one year of discovering it as required under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851(d)(2)(A), it was properly denied by the lower court as procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying relief.

Nelson v. State


Nos. SC08-589 & SC08-1965


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


43 So. 3d 20; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 647; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 225



April 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 23, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Nelson v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1972 (Fla., Aug. 23, 2010)
Request denied by State v. Nelson, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1121 (Fla., May 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Michael Hunter, Judge - Case No. CF97-06806A-XX And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Nelson v. State, 850 So. 2d 514, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1170 (Fla., July 10, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) which denied his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The inmate also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In his motion for postconviction relief, the inmate asserted that his counsel was ineffective. Upon review, the court found that the inmate failed to show that trial counsel's performance was deficient based on counsel's failure to move for a competency determination, based on counsel's failure to call the doctor who diagnosed the inmate with schizoaffective disorder as a witness, based on counsel's failure to call a witness to evaluate another doctor's reports, or based on counsel's failure to request the trial court to instruct the jury on statutory mitigation in the sentencing phase. In addition, the inmate was not denied substantive due process based on his being tried while mentally incompetent because the issue was procedurally barred as it was not raised on direct appeal and the record showed that the inmate was competent at the time of trial. Finally, the inmate was not entitled to habeas relief as he failed to establish that appellate counsel was ineffective because appellate counsel did raise the issue that the inmate asserted and the appellate court rejected it as procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order and denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

250 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Menendez v. Progressive Express Ins. Co.


No. SC08-789


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


35 So. 3d 873; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 581; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 222



April 22, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case No. 3D06-2570. (Monroe County).
Menendez v. Progressive Express Ins. Co., 2010 Fla. LEXIS 171 (Fla., Feb. 4, 2010)
Progressive Express Ins. Co. v. Menendez, 979 So. 2d 324, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3892 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insured sued respondent insurer for failing to pay personal injury protection (PIP) benefits after she was injured in an automobile collision. The Third District Court of Appeals (Florida) reversed a judgment in favor of the insured primarily due to her failure to comply with the pre-suit provision of Fla. Stat. § 627.736(11)(a) (2001), which was enacted after the accident, and which imposed additional requirements for PIP benefits.


OVERVIEW: The pre-suit notice provisions instituted several amendments to the PIP law. It required an insured to provide a pre-suit notice of intent to initiate litigation and provided an insurer additional time to pay an overdue claim. The amendment also mandated that the payment from the insurer include interest and penalties not exceeding $ 250. If an insurer paid within the additional time provided by the statute, the payment precluded an insured from bringing suit for late payment or nonpayment and shielded the insurer from a claim for attorneys' fees. Further, the amendment tolled the applicable statute of limitations. On appeal, the court held that the pre-suit notice provision of § 627.736(11)(a) could not be applied retroactively because it constituted a substantive change to the statute. In particular, the court found that the pre-suit notice provision was substantive, and not procedural, because it imposed a penalty, implicated attorneys' fees, granted an insurer additional time to pay benefits, and delayed an insured's right to file suit. Accordingly, the court found that the appellate court erred in its conclusion that § 627.736 was procedural and given retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case with directions to reinstate the trial court's final judgment, including the award of attorneys' fees. The court also instructed the appellate court to enter an order awarding attorneys' fees and to remand the issue to the trial court for a determination of the amount of fees for the proceedings at the appellate court and before the state supreme court.


 

251 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



McWatters v. State


No. SC07-51


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


36 So. 3d 613; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 406; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 169



March 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McWatters v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 871 (Fla., June 2, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McWatters v. Florida, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8656 (U.S., Nov. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, Lawrence Steven Schack, Judge -- Case Nos. 43-2004-CF000957-A, 43-2004-CF000959-A, and 43-2004-CF000961-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court in and for Martin County (Florida), appellant was convicted of three counts of first-degree murder and three counts of sexual battery with great force arising from the 2004 strangulation murders of three victims. Appellant was sentenced to death for each murder. Appellant sought review of the convictions and death sentences.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in finding the police officers were not obligated to readvise appellant of his rights immediately before the interview nor abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of the first victim's homicide after finding it was substantially similar to the other two homicides. The collateral crime evidence was relevant to the issues of lack of consent, premeditation, intent, and absence of mistake. Given the circumstantial evidence of premeditation, appellant's admission that he killed the women, and the testimony of witnesses who saw appellant with the victims shortly before their disappearances, the evidence was sufficient to support the first-degree murder convictions on the theory of premeditated murder. The fact that each woman was killed during sexual intercourse--which was based on appellant's admission--was evidence supporting the finding that at some point, the sexual activity became nonconsensual. When the weighty aggravating factors were compared to no significant mitigation, there was no reasonable possibility the trial court would have imposed a different sentence had it not considered cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator as to one victim.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Zommer v. State


No. SC08-494


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


31 So. 3d 733; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 358; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 159



March 11, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Zommer v. Florida, 562 U.S. 878, 131 S. Ct. 192, 178 L. Ed. 2d 115, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 7038 (Oct. 4, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Zommer v. State, 160 So. 3d 368, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 69 (Fla., Jan. 15, 2015)
Request denied by State v. Zommer, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1142 (Fla., May 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County, Jon Berkley Morgan, Judge -- Case No. 2005-CF-1200.
Zommer v. State, 995 So. 2d 981, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 19496 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 18, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the finding of the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) aggravating circumstance by the trial court. Defendant also claimed that the trial court improperly found that the murder was heinous, atrocious, and cruel (HAC). On appeal, the court concluded that there was competent, substantial evidence to support the finding of the CCP aggravating circumstance including that defendant admitted that he was having homicidal thoughts, that defendant did not fly into a rage and attack his victim, but rather left to later return with the intent to kill her, and that he carefully formulated his plan. There was competent, substantial evidence supporting the HAC aggravating circumstance including that the victim struggled, that the victim was scratching and fighting defendant, and that the victim attempted to block defendant from strangling her. Finally, after reviewing the totality of the circumstances, the court determined that the death sentence was proportionate because the significant aggravators established in connection with the disturbing and brutal murder of the victim far outweighed the mitigating factors found by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Cole v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


36 So. 3d 597; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 359; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 153



March 11, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Cole v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 868 (Fla., June 1, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cole v. Florida, 562 U.S. 940, 131 S. Ct. 353, 178 L. Ed. 2d 229, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 7238 (Oct. 4, 2010)
Review denied by Cole v. State, 118 So. 3d 219, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1190 (Fla., June 13, 2013)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Cole v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1429 (Fla., June 29, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Michael R. Weatherby, Judge -- Case No. 16-2005-CF-010263-DX.
Jackson v. State, 18 So. 3d 1016, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1578 (Fla., Sept. 24, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted her of two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, and two counts of robbery, and which sentenced her to death for each murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly admonished defense counsel when defense counsel asked a codefendant during cross-examination if his plea agreement allowed the trial court to impose a sentence of less than 52 years. Upon review, the court concluded that even if the trial court's comment was error, it was not fundamental error because the trial court allowed defense counsel to question the codefendant again on the terms of his plea agreement, which enabled defense counsel to dispel any confusion or prejudice that the jury otherwise would have had toward the defense as a result of the trial court's comment. Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred in admitting certain photographs. The court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the admission of the photographs because they were relevant to the jury's full understanding of the events surrounding the crimes and enabled the jury to see the relationship that defendant had with her codefendants and defendant's potential motive for planning and participating in the crimes. Finally, the court concluded that defendant was not entitled to penalty-phase relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Browning v. Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc.


No. SC08-884


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


29 So. 3d 1053; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 217; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 120



February 18, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 1D07-6024. (Leon County).
Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc. PAC v. Browning, 980 So. 2d 547, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 6286 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Florida Secretary of State and the Florida Department of State (State), Division of Elections, sought review of a decision from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that the signature-revocation provisions of § 100.371, Fla. Stat. (2007), and associated implementing regulations, Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 1S-2.0091 and 1S-2.0095, were unconstitutional in violation of art. XI, § 3, Fla. Const.


OVERVIEW: In response to these efforts to alter the initiative-circulation process, appellees, a political action committee and its president, filed an action against the State seeking a declaration that ch. 2007-30, § 25, Laws of Fla., and its implementing administrative rules represented an unconstitutional alteration of the initiative process in violation of art. XI, §§ 3 and 5, Fla. Const. Upon review, the court found that alteration of the initiative process through measures that were not expressly or implicitly contemplated by art. XI, §§ 3 and 5, Fla. Const., and were not necessary to ensure ballot integrity, had to be accomplished through constitutional amendment. Furthermore, the court determined that signature revocation was neither contemplated by the self-executing plain text of art. XI, Fla. Const., nor was it necessary to ensure ballot integrity and a valid election process. Accordingly, the signature-revocation provisions provided in § 100.371, Fla. Stat. (2007), and Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 1S-2.0091 and 1S-2.0095 violated the Florida Constitution and were void and without effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

Inquiry Concerning a Judge (Eriksson)


No. SC07-1648


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


36 So. 3d 580; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 178; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 111



February 11, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Inquiry Concerning a Judge v. Eriksson, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 869 (Fla., June 2, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court for review were the recommendations from the Judicial Qualifications Commission (JQC) that a judge be publicly reprimanded and charged the costs of proceedings based upon findings that he violated the code of judicial conduct.


OVERVIEW: The judge was accused of improperly retaliating against a defendant who wished to file a motion to recuse and employed an over-technical and rigid approach in conducting the proceedings for pro se applicant who sought domestic violence injunctions. The court found that the doctrine of judicial independence did not preclude the JQC from proceeding with the specific charges against the judge. The hearing panel was authorized to consider the testimony of the judge that was presented during the investigative proceeding before the filing of the notice of formal charges. The judge's testimony before the investigatory panel indicated a clear intent to retaliate against the defendant for filing a motion to recuse. The judge refused to insert himself into the controversy when petitioners did not know they had a right to testify on their behalf, but had no problem with rejecting potential hearsay evidence sua sponte. The courtroom was not the proper venue for the judge to express his disagreement with what he perceived to be a serious flaw with the system. A public reprimand was warranted under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The recommendations were approved.

 

256 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Sarasota Alliance for Fair Elections, Inc. v. Browning


No. SC07-2074


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


28 So. 3d 880; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 218; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 101



February 11, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Sarasota County). Second District - Case No. 2D06-4339.
Browning v. Sarasota Alliance for Fair Elections, Inc., 968 So. 2d 637, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 17235 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political action committee sought review of a decision from the Second District Court of Appeals, by means of a certified question, which found that the Florida Election Code impliedly preempted a county charter amendment in its entirety, that the provisions of the charter amendment also directly conflicted with the Election Code, and that they were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The committee sponsored an amendment to a county's charter which would impact the county's election procedures. Upon review, the court found that the Florida Legislature clearly did not deprive local governments of all local power in regard to elections and the Election Code did not impliedly preempt the field of election laws. In addition, the court found no conflict between § 6.2A of the proposed amendment and the Election Code as the minimum requirement for voting machines would simply be expanded by the amendment. Section 6.2B of the proposed amendment also did not conflict with the Election Code as the Election Code did not establish any procedures for audits nor did it preclude a county from conducting its own audit of its voting system. However, § 6.2C did conflict with the Election Code as it provided for an independent auditing firm to complete the required audits before the election results could be certified. Thus, it was unconstitutional. Finally, the court concluded that § 6.2C could be severed from the rest of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the part of the decision finding preemption, quashed the part of the decision finding that §§ 6.2A and 6.2B of the proposed amendment conflicted with the Election Code, approved the part of the decision finding that § 6.2C conflicted with the Election Code, and answered the certified question in the negative.


 

257 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Menendez v. Progressive Express Ins. Co.


No. SC08-789


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2010 Fla. LEXIS 171; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 81



February 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Clarified by, Opinion withdrawn by Menendez v. Progressive Express Ins. Co., 2010 Fla. LEXIS 580 (Fla., Apr. 22, 2010)
Substituted opinion at Menendez v. Progressive Express Ins. Co., 2010 Fla. LEXIS 581 (Fla., Apr. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Monroe County). Third District - Case No. 3D06-2570.
Progressive Express Ins. Co. v. Menendez, 979 So. 2d 324, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3892 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sued defendant insurer for failure to pay personal injury protection (PIP) benefits. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the insured but the Third District Court of Appeal (Fla.) reversed the judgment on multiple grounds. The insured filed an application of review of the appellate court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The insurer failed to pay personal injury protection (PIP) benefits to the insured after she was injured in an automobile accident. Because the insurer did not pay the benefits, the insured sued for overdue benefits. The insured was successful in her claim in the trial court, which eventually entered a judgment in her favor. On appeal, the appellate court reversed the judgment on multiple grounds, including the insured's failure to comply with a statute enacted after the date of the automobile accident (referred to as the statutory pre-suit provision) that placed additional requirements on an injured person seeking to recover PIP benefits before filing suit. The supreme court found that the 2001 statutory amendment could not be applied retroactively because it allowed an insurer to avoid an award of attorneys' fees, which constituted a substantive change to the statute in effect at the time the insureds' insurance policy was issued. Under the statute in effect at the time the policy was issued, the insurer was obligated to pay a claim within 30 days after receiving notice of loss. Moreover, the insured had the right to bring suit for an overdue claim once the 30 days had expired.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision was quashed and the action was remanded with directions to reinstate the stipulated final judgment and to award attorney's fees.


 

258 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Johnston v. State


No. SC09-839


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


27 So. 3d 11; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 62; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 64



January 21, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnston v. Florida, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 7932 (U.S., Oct. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Bob Wattles, Judge -- Case No. CR83-5401.
Johnston v. State, 497 So. 2d 863, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2828 (Fla., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Fla.) denied his fourth and fifth successive motions for postconviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of the brutal murder of an 84 year old woman. The supreme court found that the trial court did reach the merits of the newly discovered evidence claim and did apply the correct test, considering all the admissible evidence in the case to determine the merits of the claim. The inmate had not shown that the trial court abused its discretion in denying production for additional testing or that any of the testing would probably result in his acquittal. No specific procedures were mandated in the clemency process and the inmate had been provided with the clemency proceedings to which he was entitled. The inmate's claim of mental illness as a bar to execution was procedurally barred because it had not been raised on direct appeal on in any of the other postconviction proceedings. Mental illness was not a per se bar to execution. The inmate could not contend that his punishment had been illegally prolonged when the delay in carrying out his sentence was largely due to his own actions challenging his conviction and sentence. The trial court took reasonable steps to ensure that the shackles would not be visible to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ferrell v. State


No. SC07-92, No. SC07-1447


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


29 So. 3d 959; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 42; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 53



January 14, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 1, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Charles W. Arnold, Jr., Judge - Case No. 91-8142CFA And an Original Proceeding ? Habeas Corpus.
Ferrell v. State, 686 So. 2d 1324, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1627 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery and armed kidnapping. He was sentenced to death. The inmate filed a motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 to vacate his convictions and sentence. The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Fla.) denied the guilt-phase claims but granted the inmate a new penalty phase. Both sides appealed. The inmate also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the inmate failed to show prejudice resulting from trial counsel's decision not to depose certain individuals who testified against him at trial. The inmate did not established any specific information that trial counsel would have learned from attending the depositions of the witnesses that could have been used to impeach them at trial. The inmate could not demonstrate that trial counsel was deficient in his cross-examination of the witnesses. The inmate did not allege, or introduce any evidence to show, that he was absent from a pretrial hearing where evidence was adduced or where his consultation was required. The inmate failed to show that the state knew or suspected that certain witness testimony was false. When viewed in conjunction with the failures of trial counsel regarding the lack of investigation into mitigation, the failure of trial counsel to object to even one of the clearly improper remarks left the state's case virtually untested.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The habeas petition was denied.

Bradley v. State


Nos. SC07-1964 & SC08-1813


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


33 So. 3d 664; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 3; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 23



January 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised May 10, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Bradley v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 579 (Fla., Apr. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Clay County, Peter Lennings Dearing, Judge -- Case No. 10-1996-CF-1277-AXXX.
Bradley v. State, 787 So. 2d 732, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 404 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Clay County (Florida), which denied his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his counsel was ineffective. Upon review, the court determined that contrary to defendant's assertions, trial counsel did not fail to investigate certain duct tape evidence and was not unaware that the victim moved about the house before the police arrived. While counsel did not choose the independent act theory as his primary defense, he did make that argument as a fall back defense. Thus, counsel could not be deemed deficient for failing to investigate the duct tape evidence because competent, substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding that trial counsel did investigate and utilize it at trial. Moreover, the court concluded that counsel's decision to pursue an alibi defense as the primary defense strategy was reasonable under the circumstances. Furthermore, even if counsel's actions could be considered deficient, defendant failed to establish that such deficiency resulted in prejudice to him. Finally, defendant failed to present a legally sufficient claim for habeas relief because his presentation of the issues was legally insufficient and thus, his claims were waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order denying the motion for postconviction relief and denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus.

No. SC07-1622

42 So. 3d 177; 2010 Fla. LEXIS 4; 35 Fla. L. Weekly S 13

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 9, 2010.

Post-conviction relief denied at Twilegar v. State, 175 So. 3d 242, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1174 (Fla., May 28, 2015)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County, James R. Thompson, Judge -- Case No. 03-002151CF JRT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in concluding that the evidence was sufficient to show that he killed the victim or to support premeditation, and in denying his motion to suppress the evidence seized at a campground. The court found that a rational trier of fact could find that the elements of the crime were established beyond a reasonable doubt as defendant was with the victim on the day before the date the victim was last seen, defendant was seen digging a hole on the next day, the victim told his girlfriend he was going to see defendant, and the victim was shot and buried alive near to the spot where defendant was digging. Substantial evidence supported the finding of premeditation including defendant's digging the hole, the victim's meeting defendant, and the victim being hot in the upper back at close range near the grave site where defendant was seen digging. The court held that there was no Fourth Amendment violation in the initial seizure of the property as it was removed for safekeeping purposes. Further, to the extent police retained possession of the property, there was no illegal seizure because at such point defendant had abandoned the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Smith v. State


No. SC06-747


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


28 So. 3d 838; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 2067; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 681



December 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Florida, 131 S. Ct. 3087, 180 L. Ed. 2d 912, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5006 (U.S., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Smith v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2754 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Andrew Douglas Owens, Jr., Judge -- Case No. 2004-CF-2129.
State v. Smith, 919 So. 2d 449, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 21189 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him first-degree murder, kidnapping, and capital sexual battery, and which sentenced him to death. The State filed a cross-appeal with regard to the denial of its pretrial motion regarding defendant's prior aggravated battery charge.


OVERVIEW: The State claimed that defendant's prior aggravated battery charge should be used to establish a prior violent felony conviction aggravating circumstance. The court did not agree as since § 921.0021, Fla. Stat., was limited to noncapital felonies, it was not intended for a broader definition of the word conviction to apply to the prior violent felony aggravating circumstance in capital cases. The court also found that the State did not violate the Confrontation Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VI when it failed to present the biologists who performed the DNA tests on a known sample taken from defendant and an unknown semen sample taken from the victim's shirt because the Confrontation Clause did not require the expert to have performed the actual laboratory work to permissibly testify with regard to the conclusions he drew from the results. In addition, the trial court did not err when it refused to suppress statements made by defendant's brother relating to comments made by defendant with regard to the sexual battery and murder of the victim. Finally, trial court did not err by admitting certain photographs although gruesome as they were relevant to a doctor's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, affirmed the sentences, and affirmed the denial of the motion.


 

264 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Victorino v. State


No. SC06-2090


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


23 So. 3d 87; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1954; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 645



November 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Writ denied by Victorino v. State, 39 So. 3d 1266, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 563 (Fla., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Victorino v. State, 127 So. 3d 478, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2198 (Fla., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, William A. Parsons, Judge -- Case No. 04-1378-CFAWS.
Hunter v. State, 8 So. 3d 1052, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1615 (Fla., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of six counts of first-degree murder, abuse of a dead human body, armed burglary of a dwelling, conspiracy (to commit aggravated battery, murder, armed burglary of a dwelling, and tampering with physical evidence), and cruelty to an animal. The Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Fla.) sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convinced that one of the victims had stolen some of his belongings. Defendant planned and executed a break in of the house where the victims were staying and he and the other co-defendants beat to death the victims with baseball bats. Defendant brutalized the death body of one of the victims and killed her dog. The court found that defendant freely and voluntarily consented to providing DNA samples and fingernail scrapings. Under the totality of the circumstances the improper use of "and/or" in the felony murder, cruelty to animals, and principals instructions did not constitute fundamental error. Application of the heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC) aggravator was appropriate because the victims were acutely aware of their impending deaths and the murders were both conscienceless or pitiless and unnecessarily torturous. Application of the cold, calculating and premeditated (CCP) aggravator was appropriate because defendant planned the murders, directed where each co-defendant should go once inside and gave each co-defendant a bat. The totality of the circumstances showed that death was an appropriate penalty.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.


 

265 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Orme v. State


No. SC08-182


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


25 So. 3d 536; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1950; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 638



November 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Orme v. Florida, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 4596 (U.S., June 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Judy P.M. Pittman, Judge -- Case No. 92-442CFMA.
Orme v. State, 896 So. 2d 725, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 360 (Fla., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, sexual battery and robbery and was sentenced to death. His convictions and sentence were affirmed on appeal. In a post-conviction proceeding his death sentence was reversed and a new penalty phase was ordered. In the new penalty phase, a jury recommended a death sentence and the Circuit Court in and for Bay County sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had an extensive history of substance abuse. He lapsed after about a year after treatment at a center. He appeared at the center and tested positive for cocaine and he was showing signs of acute cocaine withdrawal. He was cold, his face was flushed, and he was exhibiting symptoms like delirium tremens. Defendant told people at the treatment center to check a certain motel room. When they called the motel the owner went to check the room and found a woman badly beaten to death. Defendant had know the woman who was a nurse for sometime and called her because he was having a bad high. Defendant raped and severely beat the woman to death. Stole her money and car and went out on the town after the crime. The court found that even if the nonstatutory mitigator of remorse had been considered, the mitigating evidence would not have outweighed the aggravators. The trial court did not err in failing to strike the venire. Defendant was not eligible to receive the sentencing option of a life sentence without the possibility of parole. Defendant's sentence was proportional in relation to other death sentences.


OUTCOME: Defendant's death sentence was affirmed.


 

266 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Pagan v. State


No. SC06-378, No. SC07-1327


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


29 So. 3d 938; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1665; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 561



October 1, 2009, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Susan Lebow, Judge -- Case No. 93-3648-CF-10B. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Pagan v. State, 830 So. 2d 792, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 549 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, and armed burglary, and sentenced to death. He filed a motion in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) to vacate his convictions of first-degree murder and sentences of death under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The trial court denied the motion to vacate, and petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus from the court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner and others committed a home invasion robbery during which petitioner shot and killed two victims and attempted to kill two others, believing they had seen his face. Petitioner argued that the State had withheld evidence regarding a potential suspect who had the same first name as he. The court rejected this claim because there was ample evidence that this person was known to and even investigated by petitioner's attorney. The attorney even used the information to argue various motions to the trial court. Evidence known to the defense could not constitute Brady material. The court also rejected petitioner's argument that his sentencing counsel was ineffective for failing to present certain mitigating factors, such as a mental evaluation performed on petitioner. Sentencing counsel reviewed all the relevant records, obtained school records and jail records, interviewed petitioner and his family and friends, and obtained the appointment of the doctor who performed the evaluation. Much of the evidence was presented, and the evidence that was not presented was left out for strategic reasons. The State did not withhold evidence regarding a plea agreement with its main witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and denied the petition for habeas relief.

Jackson v. State


No. SC07-2008


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


18 So. 3d 1016; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1578; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 547



September 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jackson v. Florida, 558 U.S. 1151, 130 S. Ct. 1144, 175 L. Ed. 2d 979, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 714 (2010)
Related proceeding at Cole v. State, 36 So. 3d 597, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 359 (Fla., 2010)
Related proceeding at Wade v. State, 41 So. 3d 857, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 687 (Fla., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Jackson v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2017 (Fla., Sept. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Michael R. Weatherby, Judge -- Case No. 16-2005-CF-01263-CX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him and sentenced him to death for the first-degree murder of two victims. Defendant also had concurrent sentences for two counts of robbery and two counts of kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the judgments of conviction and sentences of death entered for the first-degree murders of the victims along with his concurrent sentences for two counts of robbery and two counts of kidnapping. The supreme court affirmed, stating that the evidence supported the jury's conclusion that defendant was guilty of the murders and that the murders were not the independent act of his codefendants. Foremost, defendant admitted that he was a willing perpetrator of the underlying felony, which was the robbery of the victims, that set in motion the kidnapping and murders. The kidnapping did not terminate prior to the death of the victims because liberty was never restored to them and they were never in a place of safety once the robbery commenced. It was also important to note that there was evidence that defendant planned the robbery and stated that he would murder the victims. The trial court's denial of the motion to suppress the contents of a motel room safe was based on the correct legal conclusion that the safe was encompassed in the search warrant and that law enforcement was not required to obtain a second warrant to access the contents of the safe.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

268 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Hurst v. State


No. SC07-1798


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


18 So. 3d 975; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1558; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 525



September 17, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Linda Lee Nobles, Judge - Case No. 1998-CF-001795-A.
Hurst v. State, 819 So. 2d 689, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 784 (Fla., Apr. 18, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which denied his motions under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 to vacate his judgment of conviction for first-degree murder and his sentence of death. Defendant argued, among other things, that the State withheld favorable, material evidence in violation of Brady and that his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that additional information a witness provided did not demonstrate a Brady violation because it was not exculpatory or impeaching and was of questionable relevance. Defendant failed to show that a new trial was required based on newly discovered evidence. The case against him would not have been weakened to such an extent that he probably would have been acquitted even if the jury heard the recantation of a witness's testimony. The first two Brady prongs were established as to the State's failure to disclose a witness's statements, but even if a further evidentiary hearing was held to explore an investigator's notes, the third prong of Brady, prejudice, was not demonstrated. Trial counsel was ineffective in failing to investigate and present evidence of mental mitigation during the penalty phase. The evidence presented at the evidentiary hearing established that significant mental mitigation was available and could have been presented if defendant had been examined by a mental health expert. Failure to present the mental mitigation that was available had an identifiable detrimental effect on the process of weighing the aggravation and mitigation in the case.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's order denying relief as to the guilt phase claims defendant raised. It reversed the trial court's order denying relief as to defendant's penalty phase claim of ineffective assistance of counsel in investigation and presentation of mental mitigation, vacated his sentence of death, and remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding before a jury, which could consider evidence of aggravation and mitigation.

270 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Winkles v. State


No. SC08-941


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


21 So. 3d 19; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1414; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 521



September 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 27, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Winkles v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1846 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Richard A. Luce, Judge -- Case No. CRC99-05593CFANO-M.
Winkles v. State, 894 So. 2d 842, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 8 (Fla., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first degree murder and was sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate filed a post-conviction motion for relief which the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: While serving a life sentence for another crime, the inmate confessed to the murder of two women. The inmate pled guilty to two counts of first-degree murder and waived his right to a jury for the penalty phase. The circuit court concluded that the aggravating circumstances far outweighed the mitigating circumstances and sentenced the inmate to death on both counts. The inmate asserted ineffective assistance of counsel. The supreme court found that competent, substantial evidence supported the postconviction court's finding that the defense made a reasonable strategic decision to waive a penalty-phase jury based on the belief that the sentencing judge would be more receptive to the available mitigation than a jury would be. Trial counsel reasonably feared that testimony from a mental health expert would be more harmful than helpful. Given the substantial aggravation and the minimal mitigating value of the proposed mitigating evidence, there was no reasonable probability that the balance of aggravating and mitigating circumstances would have been different had evidence of the inmate's mental health and history of sexual abuse been presented.


OUTCOME: The denial of the postconviction motion for relief was affirmed.


 

271 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Wright v. State


No. SC05-2212


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


19 So. 3d 277; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1416; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 497



September 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Wright v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 2565 (Fla., Nov. 23, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Richard George Prince, Judge - Case No. CF00-2727A-XX.
State v. Pitts, 936 So. 2d 1111, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13036 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murders of two victims, carjacking with a firearm, and armed kidnapping with a firearm. The Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) sentenced defendant to death for the murder convictions and concurrent sentences the other convictions. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant along with a co-defendant carjacked, kidnapped, robbed, and murdered the victims while engaged in a three-day crime spree that spanned several areas in Central Florida. The supreme court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of the inextricably intertwined collateral crimes because the carjacking and drive-by shooting were integral threads to weaving a complete story of the murders. Defendant's strategic decision to present the penalty phase of the case to the trial court instead of a jury constitutes a knowing, intelligent, and voluntary waiver and a conscious abandonment of any challenges to the constitutionality of Florida's capital-sentencing scheme. Defendant did not act out of frenzy, panic, or rage; he obtained a firearm in advance; he abducted and forced the victims to drive to a remote area where there would be no witnesses; and he shot the victims multiple times execution-style. The dominant or sole motive of these murders was witness elimination. Defendant's death sentences were not disproportionate when compared to the life sentences received by the codefendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Hayward v. State


No. SC07-1234


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


24 So. 3d 17; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1381; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 486



August 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication, December 10, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Hayward v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 2063 (Fla., Dec. 10, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hayward v. Florida, 559 U.S. 1097, 130 S. Ct. 2385, 176 L. Ed. 2d 777, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 3508 (Apr. 26, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Hayward v. State, 183 So. 3d 286, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1386 (Fla., June 25, 2015)
Dismissed by State v. Hayward, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1208 (Fla., May 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County, James Walter McCann, Judge -- Case No. 562005CF000463A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County (Florida) on charges of first-degree murder, robbery with a deadly weapon, burglary of a conveyance while armed, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. He appealed his conviction for first degree murder and the sentence of death. He raised ten issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The statement of the murder victim to police describing his attacker qualified as an excited utterance but not as a dying declaration. However, admission of the statement violated the Confrontation Clause as it was testimonial. Given the strength and nature of the other evidence connecting defendant to the crime, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The introduction of defendant's statements to police at the rooming house and their observations while did not violate his Fourth Amendment rights. While defendant was in custody when he made statements at the police station, he had been advised of his Miranda rights. The police had probable cause to detain or arrest him. The recorded conversations defendant had with his girlfriend from jail were not improperly admitted into evidence; they were not more prejudicial than probative. While the prosecutor's comparison of the choices made by the victim and defendant was improper, it was not fundamental error. Defendant's challenge to constitutional of Florida's death sentencing scheme failed. The evidence as to identification, premeditation, and whether a robbery was accomplished was sufficient.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, robbery with a deadly weapon, burglary of a conveyance while armed, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon were affirmed, and his sentence of death was affirmed.


 

273 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Children & Family Servs. v. P.E.


No. SC09-169


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


14 So. 3d 228; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1124; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 449



July 16, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. Second District - Case No. 2D07-4605. (Hillsborough County).
P.E. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs. (In the Interest of H.E.), 3 So. 3d 341, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18072 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) filed a petition to terminate respondent mother's parental rights. Because the mother failed to appear at the adjudicatory hearing, the trial court terminated her parental rights pursuant to § 39.801(3)(d), Fla. Stat. (2007), and denied her motion for a rehearing. She appealed; the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The mother appeared at the advisory hearing where the trial court informed her of the date, time, and location of the adjudicatory hearing, that her presence was necessary, and that she could lose her parental rights if she failed to appear. She also received written notice of these facts pursuant to § 39.801(a). The intermediate appellate court held that, despite the mother's claims to the contrary, her implied consent to termination under § 39.801(3)(d) relieved DCFS of the obligation to present evidence to support any of the statutory grounds for termination alleged in the petition. The high court agreed. To the extent S.S. v. State Department of Children and Family Services, 976 So. 2d 41 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2008), R.H. v. Department of Children and Family Services, 860 So. 2d 986 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2003), and Department of Children and Families v. A.S., 927 So. 2d 204 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2006), held otherwise, they were rejected. However, the intermediate appellate court erred by reversing the termination judgment on grounds the trial court had not heard evidence as to the best interests of the child, as it took testimony from the child's guardian ad litem on this issue.


OUTCOME: To the extent the intermediate appellate court's opinion stated that the mother's constructive consent relieved DCFS of the obligation to prove statutory grounds for termination, it was approved. However, its decision to reverse the trial court was quashed.

 

274 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Marek v. State


No. SC09-1080


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


14 So. 3d 985; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1125; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 461



July 16, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Jeffrey R. Levenson, Judge -- Case No. 83-7088-CF-10B.
Marek v. State, 11 So. 3d 355, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 814 (Fla., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and other crimes and was sentenced to death. The Broward County Circuit Court (Florida) denied his third and fourth successive motions for postconviction relief (PCR), which were filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. It also denied the inmate's motions to correct the transcript. He appealed; appellee State opposed the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Co-defendant and the inmate were convicted of murder. The inmate argued that affidavits from co-defendant's fellow prisoners stating that he confessed to strangling the victim entitled the inmate to a new trial. The high court disagreed. The alleged statements were inconsistent and most of the witnesses did not believe them. This hearsay would not have been admissible during the guilt phase, and had it been admitted in the penalty phase under 921.141(1), Fla. Stat. (2008), the sentence would not likely have been less severe. None of the aggravators rested on the inmate's being the killer, and none were undermined by the newly discovered evidence. As the fourth successive postconviction motion was facially insufficient and meritless, any error in not holding a case management conference was harmless. Counsel's testimony that his performance during the penalty phase was deficient did not establish ineffective assistance. Any error in denying the motion to correct the transcript was harmless. As there was no legal issue requiring the resolution of a fact question, there was no basis for the inmate's request that the high court relinquish jurisdiction to conduct an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the PCR court's orders denying the inmate relief and his motion to correct the transcript, and denied his motion to relinquish jurisdiction.

Mosley v. State


No. SC06-1408


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


46 So. 3d 510; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1122



July 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 23, 2009.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mosley v. Florida, 562 U.S. 887, 131 S. Ct. 219, 178 L. Ed. 2d 132, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 6906 (2010)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Mosley v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 2721 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Michael R. Weatherby, Judge -- Case No. 16-2004-CF-6675-AXXX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder for killing a woman and her infant son. It then sentenced defendant for both murders, including the imposition of a death sentence for the killing of the infant son. Defendant appealed the convictions and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: A woman to whom defendant was not married gave birth to their son. Defendant was ordered to pay child support. The woman and child then disappeared. An accomplice established that defendant, on a pretext, took them to a remote area where he strangled the woman and suffocated the child. A jury found him guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. He was then sentenced to death for the child's killing and given a life sentence for the woman's murder. The state supreme court found that (1) he did not show that fundamental error occurred regarding alleged improper remarks by the prosecutor; (2) admission of an incriminating recorded collect call between him calling from jail and his wife did not violate the § 90.504, Fla. Stat. (2008) spousal privilege as defendant pursuant to § 90.507, Fla. Stat. (2008) waived that privilege because a prerecorded warning at the start of the call stated that the call was subject to monitoring and recording, which forfeited any expectation of privacy; (3) sufficient evidence supported a denial of defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial; and (4) the death sentence was not a disproportionate penalty under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the judgments of conviction and sentence of death.


 

276 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Lindsey v. State


No. SC07-1167


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


14 So. 3d 211; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1012; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 399



July 9, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Eileen M. O'Connor, Judge -- Case No. 06004260CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder. He appealed, arguing in part that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of shooting a pawnshop clerk in the head. The court stated that the circumstantial evidence, while perhaps sufficient to create some suspicion, was not sufficient to support a conviction The entire case against defendant consisted of the following evidence: a bag containing jewelry was taken during the robbery; (2) defendant's ex-wife found a bag of the same type containing jewelry in a closet of an apartment where she sometimes stayed with defendant and several other individuals, including another suspect; (2) defendant eventually sold the jewelry from the bag in the closet at a flea market; (3) defendant told a second person that the second person should always kill witnesses to crimes and that defendant had to do that. No evidence showed that the bag of jewelry the ex-wife found was the same bag of jewelry that was missing from the pawn shop safe. Even if the bags were the same, the other suspect as well as several other people had access to the closet where the bag was discovered, and defendant admitted that he sometimes helped the other suspect get rid of stolen merchandise. The evidence was equally consistent with a reasonable hypothesis of innocence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the conviction and sentence. It remanded the case with directions that a judgment of acquittal be entered.

Gill v. State


No. SC06-1572


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


14 So. 3d 946; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1016; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 414



July 9, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Gill v. State, 107 So. 3d 326, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 1863 (Fla., 2012)
Related proceeding at, Writ of mandamus denied Gill v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Jan. 23, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Union County, Robert P. Cates, Judge -- Case No. 63-2002-CF-28-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Union County (Florida) entered a final judgment finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder and sentencing defendant to death after defendant pled guilty to that offense, and waived a penalty-phase jury and presentation of mitigation of evidence at the penalty phase. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to life in prison and incarcerated for the murder of a person. In that case, he had pled guilty to first-degree murder and had requested that the trial court impose a death sentence because he did not want to spend the rest of his life in prison. Just days after he was incarcerated, he strangled his cellmate. Regarding the most recent murder, defendant after being found competent pled guilty to first-degree murder, and waived a penalty-phase jury and presentation of mitigation at the penalty phase. After considering aggravation and mitigation evidence in the record, the trial court determined pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.172 that there was a factual basis for the plea and sentenced him to death. The state supreme court found that defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily pled guilty. It then found that the fact that he had mental disabilities did not prohibit a finding that he committed the most recent murder in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner. It further found that the death penalty was not a disproportionate sentence and that Ring did not apply because he waived a jury trial by pleading guilty to the offense.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence of death.

Beasley v. State


No. SC06-2375


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


18 So. 3d 473; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1023; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 439



July 9, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 23, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Beasley v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1660 (Fla., Sept. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Cecilia M. Moore, Judge -- Case No. CF95-4842A1-XX.
Beasley v. State, 774 So. 2d 649, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2042 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an amended motion to vacate a judgment of conviction of first-degree murder and a sentence of death under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) denied the motion. Defendant appealed, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: The court held that counsel had not been ineffective for failing to present the testimony of experts in the areas of forensic crime scene investigation or blood spatter. The strategy was to use effective cross-examination to challenge the legitimacy of the theory that defendant placed a bloody shirt under a bed. Furthermore, defendant had not shown prejudice because there was no evidence that an expert would have provided different information. Next, counsel reasonably investigated all leads provided by defendant, including questioning for additional information when encountering a dead end, only to be met with defendant's reluctance to provide anything more than vague details. Next, after defendant made a last-minute decision not to testify, he declined the opportunity for more time with counsel. This, combined with the representation that counsel spent five hours with defendant the night before in preparation for his testimony, supported the finding that trial counsel was not deficient in preparing defendant to testify. Finally, counsel provided reasonable, strategic explanations for not presenting an alternative suspect as a witness or further implicating him in the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the motion.

Chavez v. State


No. SC07-952, No. SC08-970


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


12 So. 3d 199; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 977; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 383



June 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Chavez v. Florida, 558 U.S. 996, 130 S. Ct. 501, 175 L. Ed. 2d 356, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7722 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Marc Schumacher, Judge -- Case No. 95-37867. And an Original Proceedings -- Habeas Corpus.
Chavez v. State, 832 So. 2d 730, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2452 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 postconviction relief motion filed in an attempt to vacate a judgment of conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. Defendant appealed. He also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus in the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of the first-degree murder, kidnapping, and sexual battery of a nine-year-old boy. The jury then recommended a death sentence, which the trial court imposed. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Thereafter, the trial court summarily denied several Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 postconviction relief motion claims and denied other claims after a hearing. The state supreme court found that (1) the trial court properly ruled that defendant's proposed expert witness should not be permitted pursuant to § 90.702, Fla. Stat. (2007) to testify about a comparison between the criminal justice systems of defendant's native Cuba and the United States regarding whether a waiver of his Miranda rights was voluntary since the proposed expert lacked adequate experience to render such an opinion; (2) not presenting certain mental health mitigation evidence through the testimony of a psychologist was a reasonable strategic decision to avoid alienating the penalty-phase jury; (3) defendant did not establish per se ineffective assistance of counsel; and (4) he did not establish entitlement to habeas corpus relief he had also sought.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment and also denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus.


 

281 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



McNeil v. Canty


No. SC08-2369


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


12 So. 3d 215; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 975; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 381



June 25, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D08-452.
Canty v. McNeil, 995 So. 2d 998, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 16211 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent inmate brought an action against petitioner, challenging the calculation of his new release date made by the Department of Corrections (DOC). The trial court denied the inmate's requested relief. The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District granted the inmate's petition and certified a question. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate was returned to custody after a supervision violation, the DOC declared a forfeiture of previously accrued gain time on his three conditional release eligible offenses. Then, the DOC determined the inmate's new release date by using the forfeited gain time on the conditional release eligible sentence that had accrued the greatest amount of gain time. The certified question asked whether, on revocation of conditional release, the DOC was allowed to calculate a new release date by using gain time forfeited on the release eligible sentence with the most accrued gain time, even if this method required incarceration beyond the concurrent sentences imposed by the trial judge. The appellate court answered the question in the negative. If the forfeited gain time on the inmate's sentence with the most accrued gain time was applied to make his new tentative release date proportionately later, he would have been required to serve more incarceration time than originally imposed by the sentencing judge. Sentencing was a power of the courts, not the DOC, and the DOC was not permitted to require an inmate to serve more incarceration time than imposed by the court.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the negative, and the decision of the intermediate appellate court was approved.


 

282 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Counsel v. Fla. Bar Bd. of Governors


No. SC09-363


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


12 So. 3d 183; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 862; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 347



June 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Liberty Counsel v. Fla. Bar Bd. of Governors, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7360 (U.S., Oct. 13, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a nonprofit public interest law firm and two members of the Florida Bar, sought to enjoin respondent, the Florida Bar, from permitting the Family Law Section (FLS) of the Bar to file an amicus brief in support of a trial court ruling that held a law prohibiting homosexuals from adopting children unconstitutional. The injunction was sought pursuant to authority under Art. V, § 15, Fla. Const.


OVERVIEW: The FLS was established pursuant to the authority vested in the Bar under R. Regulating Fla. Bar 1-4.5, and it was a voluntary section. The FLS was granted permission, by a unanimous vote of the Board of Governors of the Bar, to file the amicus brief in the matter. Petitioners opposed the filing and sought injunctive relief. The court held that the filing of the brief by the FLS did not violate petitioners' rights under U.S. Const. amend. I because membership in the FLS was voluntary and the advocacy was not funded by compulsory Bar dues. There was no violation of the Standing Board Policy Fla. Bar 8.10(a)(3), as the restrictions therein pertained to the Bar and not the voluntary sections thereof. Similarly, while the sections of the Bar were an integral part thereof under R. Regulating Fla. Bar 1-4.5 and 2-7.2, the standards and restrictions were not applicable to voluntary sections of the Bar. Further, the actions of the Bar did not constitute an ultra vires act because it had authority under R. Regulating Fla. Bar 2-9.2 to waive any of its standing policies. There was no cause for the court, in the exercise of its supervisory authority over the Bar, to grant an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for injunctive relief.

Eaglin v. State


No. SC06-760


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


19 So. 3d 935; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 859; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 352



June 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Eaglin v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1717 (Fla., Oct. 8, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Eaglin v. State, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1384 (Fla., June 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from Circuit Court in and for Charlotte County, William L. Blackwell, Senior Judge -- Case No. 03-001525CF WLB.
Smith v. State, 998 So. 2d 516, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1639 (Fla., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Charlotte County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and imposed sentences of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a life sentence for murder. He tried to escape by jumping a fence, but was subdued. Prior thereto, he had killed an inmate and a corrections officer, and he injured another inmate. After a jury trial, defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's refusal to allow impeachment of a state witness with his prior correctional facility disciplinary report, as it was not a conviction under § 90.610(1), Fla. Stat. (2006), and was not adequately explained. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. There was no evidentiary error in the penalty phase of the trial. A claim that counsel was ineffective was not reviewable where it was not apparent from the face of the record. Further, there was no error in consideration by the trial court of mitigating evidence. Although the trial court erred by addressing the issue of remorse, such error was harmless. The CCP aggravator was supported by the evidence, and defendant failed to show that he had a pretense of justification. The death penalty statute was not violative under Apprendi and Ring, and the sentences were proportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Floyd v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 43519 (M.D. Fla., Mar. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County, William A. Parsons, Judge - Case No. 98-1315-CF-52. And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Floyd v. State, 850 So. 2d 383, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1753 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County (Florida), which denied his motion to vacate a conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. Defendant also petitioned the Court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the murder of his mother-in-law. The Court had affirmed defendant's first-degree murder conviction based on the theory of premeditated murder as well as had upheld the death sentence. On appeal, defendant asserted various claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The court held that defendant failed to establish such ineffectiveness with regard to trial counsel failing to challenge the competency of two child witnesses because a sufficient factual basis existed for trial counsel to reasonably conclude that the children were competent based on trial counsel deposing both children before trial and observing their demeanor. The court found no ineffective assistance of counsel with regard to trial counsel's failure to object to alleged hearsay testimony of one of the children identifying defendant as the murderer as the testimony qualified as an excited utterance. Defendant further failed to establish ineffective assistance of counsel based on trial counsel failing to have counseling records of the children admitted as the legal entity controlling the records had asserted the psychotherapist-patient privilege.


OUTCOME: The Court affirmed the denial of defendant's postconviction motion for relief and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Reese v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


14 So. 3d 913; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 466; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 296

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Lawrence Page Haddock, Judge. Case No. 92-4174-CF.
Reese v. State, 768 So. 2d 1057, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1682 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order by the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 postconviction motion to vacate his judgment of conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. The prisoner had argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel as, inter alia, counsel was inadequate as to the presentation of mental health mitigation in the penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner confessed to hiding in the victim's closet, raping her, an strangling her with an extension cord. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. After remand on a sentencing issue, the appellate court affirmed the sentence of death. The appellate court held that, to the extent that the prisoner argued that counsel did not present any evidence of the prisoner's mental or emotional distress at the time of the crime, the record plainly refuted the claim. The prisoner also failed to demonstrate that counsel was ineffective in failing to request a doctor conduct neuropsychological testing. Counsel stated he was not aware of any reason to request additional testing. That in hindsight the mental health expert believed he should have done the testing did not alter the appellate court's analysis. Even if he had met the first prong of Strickland, he had not established prejudice. Because the prisoner's constitutional challenges failed, he had not demonstrated trial counsel error for failing to object to valid instructions, and his ineffective assistance claim failed as well.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, O. H. Eaton, Jr., Judge. Case No. 04-2491-CFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (County) of two counts of first-degree murder and one count of burglary with an assault or battery. Following the penalty phase, the jury recommended the death sentence for both of the murders. The court then sentenced defendant to death for both of the murders, finding that the aggravators outweighed the mitigators. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bodies of two stabbing victims were found in their home. One of the victims was a partially paralyzed woman in a wheelchair. Defendant's bloody shoe prints were found in the home, while the victims' blood was found on his clothing. On appeal, the court found that (1) the trial court did not err in advising defendant of the limitations of self-representation; (2) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for new trial based on newly discovered evidence as to the palm print on the knife being inconclusive; (3) defendant did not preserve a juror challenge, and no manifest error occurred; (4) the trial court did not err in denying a judgment of acquittal on the burglary charge; (5) testimony by the victims' relative about an encounter with defendant in the victims' home was admissible; (6) the trial court did not err by instructing on the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator, or in finding the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator; (7) the evidence was sufficient to support the murder convictions; and (8) the sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.
