Fla. Ass'n of Prof'l Lobbyists, Inc. v. Div. of Legislative Info. Servs.


No. SC08-791


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


7 So. 3d 511; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 403; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 271



March 19, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 07-10435.
Fla. Ass'n of Prof'l Lobbyists Inc. v. Div. of Legislative Info. Servs., 525 F.3d 1073, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 8753 (11th Cir. Fla., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Association of Professional Lobbyists, initiated a facial challenge to a Florida Act, §§ 11.045 and 112.3215, Fla. Stat. (2008), which regulated and disciplined lobbyists. The United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit held that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague or overly broad under federal constitutional standards. However, the court certified questions of Florida law for review.


OVERVIEW: The Association argued that the Florida Legislature, in enacting the Act and thereby giving itself the power to issue advisory opinions, investigate violations, and recommend punishment for infractions of the Act that it alone could approve, had directly encroached on the powers of the judicial and executive branches. The Association also claimed that the Act was not validly enacted by the Legislature according to the procedural requirements of the Florida Constitution. The Association also argued that lobbying was part of the general practice of law and that the Act was unconstitutional because it regulated and disciplined lawyers who worked as lobbyists and thereby encroached on the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court of Florida. The court found that (1) the Act did not violate Florida's separation of powers doctrine; (2) the Act was validly enacted by the Florida Legislature under Art. III, §§ 3 and 7, Fla. Const.; (3) lobbying, as defined by the Act, did not constitute the practice of law so that the Act did not encroach on the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court. Accordingly, the Act was valid.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions and held that the Act (1) did not violate Florida's separation of powers doctrine; (2) was validly enacted by the Florida Legislature; and (3) did not infringe on the Florida Supreme Court's jurisdiction to regulate lawyers or the practice of law.

Sch. Bd. v. Survivors Charter Sch., Inc.


No. SC07-2402


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 1220; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 570; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 251



February 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Survivors Charter Schs., Inc. v. Sch. Bd., 12 So. 3d 324, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 9166 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal -- Class of Constitutional Officers. (Palm Beach County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D06-2378 and 4D06-2379.
Survivors Charter Schs., Inc. v. Sch. Bd., 968 So. 2d 39, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10702 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) entered a decision concluding that the Administrative Procedure Act had to be followed when a school board immediately terminated a charter school charter pursuant to the school charter statute, § 1002.33(8)(d), Fla. Stat. (2005), and determined "essentially" meant anything less than 90 days. The state supreme court granted petitioner school board's application for review of that decision.


OVERVIEW: Respondent charter school company operated two separate charter schools. Both charters included provisions for immediate termination after 24 hours' notice. After a meeting regarding the proposed termination of the two charters due to severe fiscal mismanagement, the school board voted for termination. A notice given to the schools stated the termination was for "good cause" because of the mismanagement, based on § 1002.33(8)(d), Fla. Stat. (2005), as well as the charter provisions, and would become effective in 24 hours. The Charter School Appeal Commission prepared written recommendations and the matter proceeded to the state education board for a final decision. The state education board voted to uphold the immediate termination of both charters. The appellate court found that the termination decision was subject to the Administrative Procedure Act (APA) and "immediate" termination in § 1002.33(8)(d), Fla. Stat. (2005) only meant something less than 90 days. The state supreme court ruled that the APA did not apply because the charter school statute provided its own procedure contemplating immediate action subject only to the charter provision requiring 24 hours of notice.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court quashed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case to the appellate court for further proceedings.

Hojan v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 1204; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 272; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 256



February 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hojan v. Florida, 558 U.S. 1052, 130 S. Ct. 741, 175 L. Ed. 2d 521, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 8710 (Nov. 30, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Hojan v. State, 180 So. 3d 964, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1843 (Fla., Sept. 3, 2015)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice Hojan v. Jones, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99244 (S.D. Fla., June 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Paul L. Backman, Judge -- Case No. 02-5900-CF10B.
Mickel v. State, 929 So. 2d 1192, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11036 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 7, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions and death sentence in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) after he was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder, one count of attempted first-degree premeditated murder, one count of attempted first-degree felony murder, three counts of armed kidnapping, and two counts of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the trial court's ruling denying defendant's motion to suppress was proper, as competent, substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant was read Miranda warnings. A detective testified at the suppression hearing that he read defendant Miranda warnings from a prepared text, and defendant expressly stated on the tape-recorded confession that he had been read Miranda rights and understood them. The evidence supported defendant's murder convictions, as a victim identified defendant as the shooter in a photo lineup at a hospital and also in court. Defendant confessed to murdering the victims, and in those confessions demonstrated an in-depth knowledge of the crime and the crime scene. A statement made by the victim identifying "the Mexican" as the shooter was harmlessly admitted as an excited utterance, as there was substantial testimony by other witnesses that duplicated the statement. Defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his right to mitigation, and thus Koon was satisfied. Based on a comparison of defendant's death sentence to other similar death sentences, the sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and death sentence were affirmed.

295 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Murray v. State


No. SC03-1241


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 1108; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 146; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 171



January 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Murray v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 388 (Fla., Feb. 26, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Murray v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1684 (Fla., Sept. 29, 2009)
Request denied by Murray v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1703 (Fla., Sept. 29, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Murray v. Fla., 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7319 (U.S., Oct. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Charles W. Arnold, Jr., Judge -- Case No. 92-3708 CFA.
Murray v. State, 838 So. 2d 1073, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1942 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, burglary with assault, and sexual battery. A death sentence was imposed.


OVERVIEW: A victim's home was burglarized and she was beaten, stabbed, and strangled to death. Defendant was linked to the murders by physical evidence at the scene, witness observations of him in the area of the crime, and his confession to a cellmate. Defendant's prior three trials either ended in a hung jury or reversals on appeal. After his fourth trial, he was found guilty of all charges. On appeal, the court found that admission of hair evidence was proper, as there was insufficient evidence of tampering and no Frye analysis required. Dismissal of the indictment was not warranted and no particularized need was shown for disclosure of grand jury testimony under § 905.27, Fla. Stat. The prosecution's use of a peremptory challenge to strike an African-American venireperson was based on a legitimate race-neutral reason. There was no juror misconduct that required a mistrial and a reasonable doubt jury instruction was proper. Use of prior testimony for unavailable witnesses was not error, and there was no double jeopardy violation by the successive prosecutions. The evidence was sufficient to support the murder conviction, and the death sentence was proportional to the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

The court likewise upheld the postconviction court's denial of relief, and denied his petition for habeas corpus relief, based on his ineffective assistance of counsel claims upon finding that most were procedurally barred or that he insufficiently pled any error regarding those claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the postconviction court's denial of relief and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Ronald V. Swanson, Judge -- Case No. 2004-CF-001184.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder while using, carrying, or possessing a weapon; robbery with a deadly weapon; and burglary of a dwelling with assault and battery. The Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida) sentenced defendant to death for murder and consecutive life sentences for the robbery and burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Among other things, the supreme court concluded the trial court did not err in declining to strike the jury venire after a juror saw defendant in shackles, as the juror was excused for cause and the trial court ordered that precautions be implemented to prevent the jury from seeing the shackles. Next, the supreme court found an expert's presence during the penalty phase harmless, as, inter alia, he did not refute the factual testimony of the witnesses and admitted that he had observed the testimony of other witnesses. Finding of the avoid arrest aggravator was supported by, inter alia, the fact that the last of the attacks on the victim occurred when the victim was physically incapacitated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Ventura v. State


No. SC08-60


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 194; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 131; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 71



January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ventura v. Fla., 174 L. Ed. 2d 562, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 4728 (U.S., June 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, R. Michael Hutcheson, Judge -- Case No. 86-2822-CFAES.
Ventura v. State, 673 So. 2d 479, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 9 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the summary denial entered by the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) of the inmate's successive post-conviction motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 challenging the mode of his eventual execution, which was to be by lethal injection. The inmate also filed a pro se all-writs petition under art. V, § 3(b)(7), Fla. Const. seeking the removal of his appointed counsel.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted in 1988 of first degree murder. While the inmate claimed that his successive motion for postconviction relief were upon newly discovered evidence, the trial court summarily denied the motion without an evidentiary hearing because he failed to comply with Rule 3.851(e)(2)(C) by failing to attach copies of the documents, such as Florida's 2006 lethal injection protocol, upon which his claim relied. The court affirmed based on the inmate's procedural error that rendered his motion legally insufficient. However, the court addressed the effect of Baze v. Rees, 128 S. Ct. 1520 (2008) on the validity of Florida's lethal injection protocol under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Art. I, § 17, Fla. Const. Because the United States Supreme Court had not adopted a majority standard for determined the constitutionality of a mode of execution, the court had no reliable means of determining the narrowest grounds presented in Baze but concluded that the protocol would pass muster under any of the risk-based standards considered by the Baze Court. The court denied the all-writs petition as the appointed counsel filed the reply brief timely under Fla. R. App. P. 9.420(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary denial of the inmate's successive postconviction petition. The court also denied the inmate's all-writs petition. The court reiterated that nothing in Baze v. Rees, 128 S. Ct. 1520 (2008), affected the validity of the court's opinions upholding Florida's current lethal injection protocol.

Heath v. State


No. SC07-771


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 1017; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 134; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 95



January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Heath v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 318 (Fla., Feb. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Robert P. Cates, Judge -- Case No. 01-1989-CF-3026-A.
Heath v. State, 648 So. 2d 660, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1552 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's convictions and death sentence for first-degree murder and other crimes were affirmed, he moved the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County (Florida) for postconviction relief, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said recanted testimony entitled him to relief. The supreme court held the recanting testimony was unreliable because (1) it was inconsistent with medical testimony, (2) it was internally inconsistent, (3) the witness had a motive to change his trial testimony, and (4) the witness's claim that the transcript of his trial testimony was altered was not credible. The testimony would not probably produce an acquittal or conviction on a lesser charge because it still allowed conviction as a principal of premeditated or first-degree felony murder, nor would it probably have produced a life sentence recommendation, as it did not disprove aggravators of (1) a prior violent felony conviction, or (2) committing the murder during an armed robbery, and it showed two other statutory aggravators. Counsel's assistance was not ineffective because (1) voluntary intoxication was considered and rejected as inconsistent with a stronger alibi defense, (2) presenting defendant's antisocial personality disorder diagnosis would have harmed his penalty phase case, and (3) no substance abuse diagnosis supported a diminished capacity claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, William Douglas Baird, Judge -- Case No. 521983CF000630XXXXNO.
Walton v. State, 847 So. 2d 438, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 902 (Fla., 2003)
Lightbourne v. McCollum, 969 So. 2d 326, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2255 (Fla., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of the Sixth Judicial Circuit (Florida) which summarily denied his successive motion to vacate three convictions of first-degree murder and corresponding death sentences under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He filed a successive motion for postconviction relief based on the discussion of inconsistent prosecutorial theories. The trial court also denied a public records request.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of the murder of three people during a robbery. The appellate court held the record demonstrated that the claim regarding inconsistent theories was procedurally barred and meritless as a new fundamental constitutional right was not recognized that applied retroactively. Thus, the affidavits did not constitute newly discovered evidence that would probably produce a different outcome. There was no reasonable probability that the nondisclosure of an informant's status would have resulted in a different outcome.


OUTCOME: The denial of the postconviction motion was affirmed.

Wheeler v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 27, 2009.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, T. Michael Johnson, Judge -- Case No. 2005-CF-377-01.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) of first-degree murder of deputy one, and attempted first-degree murder and aggravated battery with a firearm of deputies two and three, and his sentences, including a death sentence for the first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that a special heat of passion instruction was properly denied. The standard instructions properly advised the jury on premeditation. App. P. 9.142(a)(6).


OUTCOME: The conviction for first-degree murder and the death sentence were affirmed. The convictions for attempted murder and aggravated battery with a firearm and the sentences imposed for those offenses were also affirmed.

Advisory Opinion to the AG re: Standards for Establishing Legislative District Boundaries


No. SC08-986, No. SC08-1149


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 175; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 135; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 64



January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 21, 2009.
Companion case at Advisory Opinion to the AG re: Standards for Establishing Legislative District Boundaries, 2 So. 3d 161, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 130 (Fla., Jan. 29, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the jurisdiction rendered under Art. IV, § 10 and Art. V, § 3(b)(10), Fla. Const., the Court set forth its opinion with regard to the validity of two initiative petitions sponsored by petitioner, a political committee. Respondent, the Florida Legislative, set forth various arguments against the constitutional amendments.


OVERVIEW: The amendments at issue addressed legislative and congressional boundaries. The court noted that the two amendments and their respective ballot titles and summaries were nearly identical except for references to legislative versus congressional boundaries. The Legislature, in opposition, asserted that the proposed amendments violated the single-subject requirement of Art. XI, § 3, Fla. Const., and were misleading in various ways. The court held that the proposed amendments meet the legal requirements of Art. XI, § 3 and that the ballot titles and summaries complied with § 101.161(1), Fla. Stat. (2008). The court held that the proposed amendments encompassed a single subject, did not engage in logrolling, and did not substantially alter the functions of multiple branches of government. The court held that the proposed amendments addressed a single function of a single branch of government, namely establishing additional guidelines for the Legislature to apply when it redistricts legislative and congressional boundaries. None of the Legislature's contentions that the proposed amendments were misleading were found to have any merit.


OUTCOME: The Court approved the amendments for placement on the ballot.

Taylor v. State


No. SC06-615, No. SC07-1168


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 986; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 132; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 161



January 29, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Michael McCarthy, Judge -- Case No. 88-15525 And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Taylor v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1108 (Fla., June 19, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) which denied his motion to vacate his conviction of murder and sentence of death and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. On appeal from the denial of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 relief, he argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his claims of newly discovered evidence, and ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner raised multiple claims concerning an expert's trial testimony concerning the extensive injuries suffered by the victim. The trial court found the prisoner's allegations of recantation by the expert as to the victim's sexual injuries to be an inaccurate characterization of the expert's testimony. Thus, the prisoner failed to show that the expert's postconviction testimony qualified as newly discovered evidence. Even if an expert's alleged change in testimony were considered sufficient to call into question the sexual battery conviction, it would not be sufficient to outweigh the evidence that the prisoner committed premeditated murder or to cast doubt on his conviction for first-degree murder based upon premeditation. The record did not support the prisoner's allegation that the expert's testimony was false as it did not materially change. Neither the State nor its actors suppressed evidence. The trial court did not err in holding the prisoner had not demonstrated deficiency of his trial counsel in regard to counsel's investigation of any mental health issues. Counsel was not ineffective in any other regard. Thus, the prisoner was not entitled to postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Peterson v. State


No. SC06-252


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 146; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 141; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 74



January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 7, 2009.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Peterson v. Florida, 558 U.S. 885, 130 S. Ct. 208, 175 L. Ed. 2d 144, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 6004 (2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Peterson v. State, 154 So. 3d 275, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2063 (Fla., 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Linda R. Allan, Judge -- Case No. CRC 00-05107 CFANO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In connection with a fatal shooting during a robbery, the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder on a jury's finding of guilty, conducted a one-day penalty phase hearing, and sentenced defendant to death on the jury's recommendation. Defendant appealed, alleging violations of § 921.141(a)(6), Fla. Stat. and challenging the constitutionality of the capital sentencing process under Ring.


OVERVIEW: The court found that collateral crime evidence was admissible under § 921.141(a)(6) because it was probative of material issues and its probative value was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice. The court rejected the challenge to the constitutionality of Florida's lethal injection process. Defendant pointed to no new evidence supporting the argument that the process caused undue pain. The death sentence was proportionate because (1) the robbery aggravator was based on convictions of 13 other violent felonies and defendant's being on life parole at the time of the murder; (2) this case's facts were comparable to other murders during robberies where the death sentence was proportionate; and (3) limited mental impairment, consisting of a low to normal IQ and some difficulty in school, was not sufficiently weighty to compel a life sentence. Defendant was not entitled to a new penalty phase; the trial court did not rely on arguably improper lack of remorse evidence. The Ring claim was procedurally barred and meritless. There was insufficient evidence of premeditation, but the first-degree murder conviction was supported by substantial felony murder evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the first-degree murder conviction and the sentence of death.

Parker v. State


No. SC06-2176


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 974; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 39; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 37



January 22, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2009.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Leroy Harold Moe, Judge -- Case No. 89-8897 CF10A.
Parker v. State, 904 So. 2d 370, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 547 (Fla., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) that denied his motion to vacate a first-degree murder conviction and the death sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He had alleged ineffective assistance of counsel at the guilt and penalty phases of trial and the denial of a full and fair evidentiary hearing due to judicial bias and evidence rulings relating to his ineffectiveness claim.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant had not met his burden under Strickland as to the guilt phase, he was not entitled to relief under § 38.10, Fla. Stat., and Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.330(d), and there was no abuse of discretion in excluding witnesses whose testimony was not relevant on remand. However, defendant met both Strickland prongs as to the penalty phase. Counsel did not establish mitigation even though there was a wealth of witnesses who were not interviewed and documents that were not sought that could have fleshed out and established mitigating circumstances. Counsel only presented defendant's childhood and background information through the hearsay testimony of the public defender investigators--not from first-hand sources. Uncontroverted evidence that he had a type of neuropsychological impairment that affected his executive brain functions was available, but was not presented, at the penalty phase and would have qualified as nonstatutory mitigation. Had the facts been fleshed out or properly presented, a finding of no mitigation would not have been supported by the record. Defendant was prejudiced by the deficient performance and was entitled to a new penalty phase hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's guilt phase and evidentiary hearing claims, but reversed the penalty phase claims and remanded the case for a new penalty phase proceeding.

Nixon v. State


No. SC07-953


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 137; 2009 Fla. LEXIS 37; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 44



January 22, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, Jonathan Eric Sjostrom, Judge -- Case No. 84-2324.
Nixon v. State, 572 So. 2d 1336, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1675 (Fla., 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged, convicted, and sentenced to death for murder. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal, and the U.S. Supreme court denied certiorari review. The Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 and 3.203 motion for post conviction relief without conducting an evidentiary hearing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his conviction and death sentence violated the holding in Atkins, that U.S. Const. amend. VIII barred the execution of the mentally retarded, and that § 921.137, Fla. Stat. (2002), as interpreted in Cherry, violated the federal and state constitutions. The court disagreed. Once defendant's IQ was found to be above 70, the trial court did not have to consider other statutory factors. Defendant had a full and fair opportunity to present relevant evidence and to challenge the state-appointed psychiatrist's opinions. The trial court correctly followed § 921.137(1), Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203, and caselaw; carefully evaluated the testimony of the two experts, finding one expert's testimony to be more credible than the other; and concluded that defendant was not mentally retarded. Resolving all evidentiary conflicts and all reasonable inferences in favor of the trial court's decision, the court found that there was competent, substantial evidence to support the determination; further, the § 921.137 definition of mental retardation was constitutional, and the Equal Protection Clause did not require an extension of Atkins' interpretation of § 921.137 to the mentally ill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and its finding that defendant was not mentally retarded.

Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County


No. SC07-2200, No. SC07-2201


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


3 So. 3d 309; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2431; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 1002



December 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 249 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Brevard County v. Phantom of Brevard, Inc., 2009 Fla. LEXIS 247 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Brevard County). Fifth District - Case No. 5D06-3408.
Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 966 So. 2d 423, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13431 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both petitioner corporation and respondent county sought review of the decision in Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 966 So. 2d 423 (Fla. 5th DCA 2007), due to an alleged conflict with the decision in Phantom of Clearwater, Inc. v. Pinellas County, 894 So. 2d 1011 (Fla. 2d DCA 2005), related to whether substantially similar county ordinance provisions related to the regulation of fireworks conflict with ch. 791, Fla. Stat. (2006).


OVERVIEW: The corporation had claimed that Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance No. 05-60, as amended by Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance No. 06-18 (2006), was unconstitutional. While the Fifth District Court of Appeals had determined that ch. 791 did not expressly or impliedly preempt the regulation of fireworks, Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance No. 05-60, § 10, requiring evidence of financial responsibility by sellers of fireworks, was found to be in direct conflict with ch. 791. That determination conflicted with a prior decision by the Second District Court of Appeals. In resolving the conflict, the court agreed with the Second District. Pursuant to art. VIII, § 1(g), Fla. Const. the county had broad authority to enact ordinances that were not inconsistent with state law. The ordinance at issue was not inconsistent because § 791.03 only provided that the county had to require at least a $500 bond from licensees. Thus, the county chose to legislate in an area where the state chose to remain silent. Any business that sold fireworks in the county could comply with the county's additional insurance requirement without violating any provision of ch. 791.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision in Phantom of Brevard to the extent it was inconsistent with the instant opinion and approved the decision in Phantom of Clearwater on the conflict issue.

Jones v. State


No. SC06-474, No. SC07-729


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


998 So. 2d 573; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2434; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 8

Jones v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1565 (Fla., Sept. 4, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death, filed a motion for postconviction relief, which was denied by the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida). Defendant appealed. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In relation to a Brady claim, the court held that it was unreasonable to expect the prosecutor to become informed of and disclose the fact of a witness's arrest in the less than 24-hour period between the arrest and defendant's sentencing hearing. This was a strategic decision made after considering alternative witnesses. Furthermore, the testimony presented at the evidentiary hearing was cumulative, and it would have only added to the nonstatutory mitigation found by the trial court. Finally, the standard penalty phase instructions fully advised the jury of the importance of its role, correctly stated the law, did not denigrate the jury's role, and did not violate Caldwell.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and denied defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

310 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wickham v. State


No. SC05-1012, No. SC07-1137


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


998 So. 2d 593; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2430; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



December 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Wickham v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 888 (Fla., May 2, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, Kathleen F. Dekker, Judge -- Case No. 87-3970.
Wickham v. State, 593 So. 2d 191, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2122 (Fla., 1991)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Later, the inmate filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion for postconviction relief against appellee State. The Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) denied the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the postconviction court erred by denying his motion to disqualify all Second Circuit judges from deciding his Rule 3.851 motion. The appellate court agreed. In his Rule 3.851 motion, the inmate raised numerous ineffective assistance of counsel claims against his former trial counsel. His former trial counsel, however, had become a judge on the Second Circuit shortly after the inmate's trial. He served as a circuit court judge for almost eight years and was chief judge of the Second Circuit for three years. Currently, former defense counsel was an appellate judge on the Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, and heard appeals from, among other circuits, the Second Circuit. After former defense counsel's appointment to the appellate bench, his wife also joined the Second Circuit as a judge. Under these circumstances, it was reasonable for the inmate to fear that a Second Circuit judge hearing former defense counsel's testimony in determining the inmate's ineffective assistance of counsel claims would be biased in favor of former defense counsel and against the inmate. Thus, the inmate's motion to disqualify was based on a well-grounded fear.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's motion for disqualification was reversed and the case was remanded for a new evidentiary hearing. On remand, the Chief Judge of the Second Judicial Circuit was directed to request a temporary assignment of a judge from outside the Second Circuit to preside over the inmate's new evidentiary hearing.

 

311 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Jackson-Shaw Co. v. Jacksonville Aviation Auth.


No. SC07-2235


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


8 So. 3d 1076; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2398; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 972



December 18, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 07-10521.
Jackson-Shaw Co. v. Jacksonville Aviation Auth., 508 F.3d 653, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 27240 (11th Cir. Fla., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from a federal district court, the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit certified two questions. It asked the present court to determine whether an aviation authority had become a joint owner with a private entity or whether it had given, lent, or used its credit to aid a private entity in violation of Art. VII, § 10, Fla. Const.


OVERVIEW: The agreement was for a private commercial development company's long-term use of vacant land owned by the authority. The court held that the agreement did not violate the constitutional prohibition against joint ownership. Although an option to ground lease required the authority to construct a road extension, it had already been planned and budgeted, so the authority was not using public funds to create a prohibited joint ownership. The authority was also obligated to provide land for wetlands mitigation, but this provision did not make the parties to the agreement joint owners. Furthermore, the agreement did not meet all of the elements of the test for a joint venture. Next, the authority was not impermissibly pledging its credit to aid the company. The constitutional prohibition contemplated not just the use of public funds but the imposition of a new financial liability and a direct or indirect obligation to pay a debt of a third party. Under this standard, the authority had not given, lent, or used its credit to aid the company. Thus, the transaction needed to only serve a public purpose, which was fulfilled to the extent that the revenue might ultimately provide tax relief.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions in the negative and returned the case to the Eleventh Circuit.


 

312 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Tennis v. State


No. SC06-730


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


997 So. 2d 375; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2380; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 954



December 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Tennis v. State, 84 So. 3d 328, 2012 Fla. App. LEXIS 4013 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at Tennis v. State, 2013 Fla. App. LEXIS 14456 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Susan Lebow, Judge -- Case No. 03-11459CF-10B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) of first-degree murder. The trial court imposed a sentence of death upon defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During a hearing at which the trial court addressed defendant's motion to dismiss counsel, defendant stated, "I refuse to go to trial with him. I would like to go pro se instead of having two prosecutors against me, I'll do it myself. Even though I don't know what I'm doing, I will have a better fighting chance." He followed this pronouncement with two separate pro se motions requesting self-representation. On appeal, the court found that defendant's statement at the hearing coupled with his pro se motions was an unequivocal and clear request for self-representation, to which defendant had a right pursuant to the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments. The trial court's failure to hold a hearing to determine whether defendant could represent himself was per se reversible error. Although the State of Florida alternatively argued that the request was part of an ongoing attempt by defendant to delay and frustrate the proceedings, that did not mean that the trial court could fail to hold a hearing after the unequivocal request for self-representation. Further, the trial court did not make findings that defendant's motive in filing the motions was to delay his trial.


OUTCOME: The conviction for first-degree felony murder was reversed, the sentence of death was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

313 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Poole v. State


No. SC05-1770


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


997 So. 2d 382; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2386; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 957



December 11, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Dale Durrance, Judge -- Case No. CF01-7078A-XX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Polk County convicted defendant of attempted first-degree murder, armed burglary, armed robbery, sexual battery, and first-degree murder. Defendant appealed his conviction and his sentence of death for the first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed error in denying his motion for mistrial when the prosecutor repeatedly commented in closing argument during the guilt phase on defendant's failure to testify at trial and silence after his arrest. The comment on the failure to testify was an erroneous comment on silence that was protected under Art. I, § 9, Fla. Const.; however there was no abuse in discretion in denying the mistrial motion. Given the evidence linking defendant to the crimes, the error was not so prejudicial as to vitiate the entire trial. The trial court erred in overruling an objection to the State's questions as to unproven prior arrests and content of a tattoo. These errors were not harmless and required a new penalty phase proceeding. The questions suggested that defendant was a career felon in numerous states and created a risk that the jury would give undue weight to such information in recommending a death sentence. The tattoo questions were inadmissible nonstatutory aggravation under § 921.141, Fla. Stat. (2007). While the lack of remorse questions did not individually amount to fundamental error, the cumulative effect of the errors deprived defendant of a fair penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the case for a new penalty phase proceeding.


 

314 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pearce


No. SC07-201


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


994 So. 2d 1094; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2088; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 905



November 13, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 5, 2008.
Related proceeding at Pearce v. Tucker, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 43 (Fla., Jan. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Lynn Tepper, Judge -- Case No. 99-3110CFAES.
Pearce v. State, 880 So. 2d 561, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 975 (Fla., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida) granting appellee inmate's postconviction motion to vacate a conviction of first degree murder and death sentence and ordering a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that the trial court erred when it found that defense counsel rendered ineffective assistance in failing to file a motion in limine to exclude evidence that the inmate forced the attempted murder victim to perform a sexual act and for failing to object to other statements as to the uncharged sexual battery. The supreme court concluded that the inmate had not shown prejudice. The sexual assault did not become the feature of the trial and was simply one act in a series that led to the offenses. In addition, it was clear that the inmate was the mastermind or dominating force behind the murder and attempted murder. The State also asserted that the trial court erred in granting the inmate a new penalty phase based on the ineffective assistance of counsel. The supreme court disagreed, finding that the inmate's waiver of the presentation of mitigating evidence was not knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently made, and that the inmate suffered prejudice based on the invalid waiver. The supreme court found that defense counsel did not spend sufficient time to prepare for mitigation prior to the waiver and there was evidence that should have been presented.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting the inmate a new trial was reversed, but the order granting the inmate a new penalty phase was affirmed. The case was remanded for a new sentencing proceeding before a jury.

Tompkins v. State


No. SC08-992, No. SC08-1979, No. SC08-2000


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


994 So. 2d 1072; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2055; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 897



November 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Tompkins v. Florida, 129 S. Ct. 1305, 173 L. Ed. 2d 482, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1008 (U.S., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Appeals from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Daniel Howard Sleet, Judge - Case No. 84-CF-010538 And an Original Proceeding -- All Writs.
Tompkins v. State, 502 So. 2d 415, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 3020 (Fla., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a prisoner under sentence of death and under an active death warrant, appealed from orders of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) denying motions to vacate his sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The prisoner also petitioned to invoke the court's authority to issue all writs necessary to complete the exercise of its jurisdiction, or alternatively to issue a writ of habeas corpus, or both.


OVERVIEW: The challenge to the lethal injection protocol satisfied the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851(d)(2) exception; it was based on an allegedly botched execution. However, summary denial of claims that lethal injection violated the Eighth Amendment was proper because the new process was not cruel and inhuman punishment. The American Bar Association report on Florida's death penalty system was not newly discovered evidence. There was no error in summarily denying the claim that a governor violated § 922.06(2), Fla. Stat. (2004), in resetting an execution date beyond the statute's 10-day period; the prisoner had no enforceable rights under the statute. Further, 23 years on death row did not violate the Eighth Amendment; the prisoner contributed to the delay by filing five postconviction motions. An affidavit was not new, reliable evidence establishing that the prisoner was factually innocent. The prisoner was not deprived of his rights under chapter 119, Fla. Stat. and Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.852, when the trial court granted objections to a public records requests; the records sought were not relevant. A Giglio claim failed because allegedly false testimony did not satisfy Giglio's third element.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary denial of the fourth and fifth successive motions for postconviction relief and the petition for all writs jurisdiction, or alternatively for a writ of habeas corpus, or both.

 

316 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lynch v. State


No. SC06-2233, No. SC07-1246


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 47; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2052; 34 Fla. L. Weekly S 179; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 880



November 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by Lynch v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 152 (Fla., Jan. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, O. H. Eaton, Jr., Judge - Case No. 99-0881-CFA And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Lynch v. State, 841 So. 2d 362, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 4 (Fla., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged an amended order of the Circuit Court of the Eighteenth Judicial Circuit (Florida) denying his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 postconviction motion to vacate his murder, burglary, and kidnapping convictions and corresponding sentences of death and life imprisonment. Among other allegations, the inmate alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. The inmate also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Counsel's competing factual proffer that provided sufficient factual support for each conviction was not deficient, given overwhelming guilt evidence. The unintentional killing of a minor during an intentional, premeditated killing of her mother rendered the minor's killing a murder in the first degree and a capital felony. The armed-burglary and kidnapping felonies also rendered the minor's killing first-degree felony murder. The doctrine of transferred intent converted the minor's killing into first-degree capital murder. Any prejudice due to counsel's off-the-cuff proffer was de minimis and would not have altered the guilty plea decision. The proffer was submitted to soften the facts for the penalty phase. The inmate was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to object to the admission of a murder-suicide letter the inmate sent to his wife; the letter would have been admitted through other witnesses. Because no valid defenses existed, an asserted ignorance of unsupported defenses did not affect the decision to waive a penalty-phase jury. The death sentences were legally sound. Habeas relief was not available for procedurally barred or meritless claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the amended order of the postconviction court and denied each of the inmate's claims. The court denied the inmate's habeas petition.

Lowe v. State


No. SC05-633, No. SC05-2333


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2 So. 3d 21; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2053; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 871



November 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 20, 2008. Released for Publication January 27, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Lowe v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 159 (Fla., Jan. 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Robert A. Hawley, Judge - Case No. 90-658 And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Lowe v. State, 650 So. 2d 969, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1840 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County (Florida), granting in part and denying in part his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. The State cross-appealed, challenging the trial court's order granting defendant a new penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: Counsel was not ineffective for failing to present testimony of two witnesses that a third witness admitted to killing the victim; there was no reasonable probability an acquittal would have resulted, given the physical and circumstantial evidence of defendant's involvement. Although impeaching a witness' credibility with an affidavit could have called into question the witness' truthfulness, the failure to impeach did not undermine confidence in the outcome of the guilt phase proceeding. Defendant was not entitled to habeas relief; counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise meritless claims. Defendant was entitled to a new penalty-phase hearing; counsel failed to exercise diligence to discover evidence that a witness confessed to the crime. Although evidence proved that defendant was involved, there was no evidence conclusively showing that defendant was the perpetrator who shot and killed the victim; defendant's fingerprints were found at the scene but not on the gun used to kill the victim. Fla. Stat. § 921.141 was constitutional, and prior juvenile convictions were properly used to support the prior violent felony aggravator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order upholding defendant's first-degree murder conviction and granting a new penalty phase. The court denied defendant's petition for habeas relief. The court denied the State's cross-appeal.

Anderson v. Gannett Co.


No. SC06-2174


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


994 So. 2d 1048; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2009; 36 Media L. Rep. 2553; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 856



October 23, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Escambia County). First District - Case No. 1D05-2179.
Gannett Co. v. Anderson, 947 So. 2d 1, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17451 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed a judgment in favor of petitioner on the basis that a two-year statute of limitations for defamation applied to a false light cause of action. The appellate court certified conflict with Heekin v. CBS Broadcasting, Inc., 789 So. 2d 355 (Fla. 2d DCA 2001), which held that the four-year statute of limitations for unspecified torts applied.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court certified the following question: Is an action for invasion of privacy based on the false light theory governed by the two-year statute of limitations that applies to defamation claims or by the four-year statute that applies to unspecified tort claims? Upon consideration, the court declined to answer the certified question but approved the decision reversing the judgment in favor of petitioner. Based on a decision by the court after the appellate court's decision, it had been determined that Florida did not recognize the tort of false light invasion of privacy because the benefit of recognizing the tort was outweighed by the danger in unreasonably impeding constitutionally protected speech. Thus, the analysis of the applicable statute of limitations was unnecessary and moot. While petitioner argued that the court could not retroactively abolish the cause of action, the court had previously determined that the tort never existed at common law and any prior statements concerning false light were dicta. Based on that determination, the court disapproved of Heekin, which had assumed the existence of a cause of action and discussed the elements.


OUTCOME: The court declined to answer the certified question. The court approved the result of the appellate court's decision but not the reasoning to the extent that a cause of action for false light existed. The court disapproved of Heekin to the extent it assumed the existence of a cause of action for false light.

 

319 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Murray v. Mariner Health


No. SC07-244


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


994 So. 2d 1051; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2011; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 845



October 23, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D06-475.
Murray v. Mariners Health/Ace USA, 946 So. 2d 38, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20070 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION:  The state supreme court quashed the appellate court's decision and directed that the case be remanded to the Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) for entry of an attorney fee award that the JCC previously calculated would be a reasonable fee. It also found that the employee was entitled to an award of reasonable appellate attorney fees to be determined by the JCC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed an attorney fee award made by the Judge of Compensation Claims in favor of petitioner employee. In so ruling, it found that an award of reasonable attorney fees under § 440.34(1), Fla. Stat. (2003) in a workers' compensation case had to be made under the formula in § 400.34(3), Fla. Stat. (2003). The state supreme court then certified the decision for review as one of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a certified nursing assistant, suffered an injury while helping to lift a patient. She petitioned for workers' compensation benefits, which included a request for attorney fees. Respondents, an employer and insurer, responded by denying that benefits were owed. The Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) found the employee's testimony to be credible and awarded her a certain sum in benefits. The JCC then found that the employee's counsel expended eighty hours of time on the case but determined that the attorney fee award pursuant to § 440.34(3), Fla. Stat. (2003), was governed by the statutory formula of § 440.34(1), Fla. Stat. (2003). The JCC the found that those provisions dictated an unreasonable attorney fee award of $ 684.84, equating to an hourly rate of $ 8.11, despite testimony that a normal rate was $ 200 per hour. The appellate court affirmed the fee award. The state supreme court found that because the statutory provisions read together were ambiguous given that they did not always result a reasonable fee award, a reasonable fee award had to be determined in a workers' compensation case by applying the factors in R. Regulating Fla. Bar 4-1.5(b).


OUTCOME: The state supreme court quashed the appellate court's decision and directed that the case be remanded to the Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) for entry of an attorney fee award that the JCC previously calculated would be a reasonable fee. It also found that the employee was entitled to an award of reasonable appellate attorney fees to be determined by the JCC.

Williamson v. State


No. SC07-564, No. SC07-1787


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


994 So. 2d 1000; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1915; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 815



October 8, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Williamson v. State, 123 So. 3d 1060, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 885 (Fla., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Richard D. Eade, Judge -- Case No. 92-15642 CFA. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Williamson v. State, 681 So. 2d 688, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1629 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate under the sentence of death for, inter alia, committing first-degree murder, appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) which summarily denied his postconviction motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. He also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant had argued, inter alia, that trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: The postconviction trial court denied all of defendant's claims without holding an evidentiary hearing. The appellate court noted a comment by the prosecutor did not constitute an improper golden rule argument because it does not ask the jurors to place themselves in the victim's position. Defendant had not alleged how he was prejudiced in his trial defense by the admission of this document. The postconviction court summarily denied defendant's claim pertaining to the lack of any voir dire. The appellate court disagreed that the claim was insufficiently pled as defendant asserted that his trial counsel did not request a Frye hearing as to the expert and the testimony required a Frye hearing. Defendant did not need to provide specific factual allegations as to what his trial counsel should have elicited from the expert. The expert's testimony was the kind of testimony which required a Frye evaluation by the trial judge. Since appellate counsel did not raise a Gray claim as to defendant's convictions for attempted first-degree murder, appellate counsel was ineffective as the convictions would have been reversed. However, no new penalty-phase was required.


OUTCOME: The trial court's rulings were affirmed as to all issues raised in the postconviction motion except those issues alleging that defendant's counsel was ineffective in failing to request a Frye hearing before the opinion testimony of the State's expert was admitted into evidence. On that issue, the matter was reversed and remanded for an evidentiary hearing. Defendant's convictions and sentences for attempted first-degree murder were vacated.

 

322 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Walton County v. Stop the Beach Renourishment, Inc.


No. SC06-1447, No. SC06-1449


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


998 So. 2d 1102; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1646; 38 ELR 20254; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 761



September 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Walton County v. Stop the Beach Renourishment, Inc., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2483 (Fla., Dec. 18, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Stop the Beach Renourishment, Inc. v. Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 129 S. Ct. 2792, 174 L. Ed. 2d 290, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 4458 (U.S., 2009)
Affirmed by Stop the Beach Renourishment v. Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 2010 U.S. LEXIS 4971 (U.S., June 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D05-4086. (Walton County).
Save Our Beaches v. Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 27 So. 3d 48, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6244 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two applications, petitioners, a county, a city, a state department of environmental protection, and others, sought review of a First District Court of Appeals (Florida) decision finding the Beach and Shore Preservation Act, §§ 161.011-161.45, Fla. Stat. (2005) unconstitutional. The rephrased certified question asked was whether, on its face, the Act unconstitutionally deprived upland owners of littoral rights without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: After damage by hurricanes and tropical storms, beaches within the county were identified as critically-eroded beaches, and the county sought to restore the beaches through renourishment. Once a permit was issued for the project, respondent, a not-for-profit association consisting of six beachfront property owners, challenged the issuance of the permit and raised constitutional challenges. The appellate court found the Act unconstitutional. The court answered the certified question in the negative and quashed the appellate court's decision. The Act was facially constitutional under the doctrine of avulsion as the boundary between public lands and privately owned uplands remained the mean high water line (MHWL) as it existed before the avulsive event, such as a hurricane. Thus, if the shoreline was lost due to avulsive event, the public (in this case, the county) had the right to restore its shoreline up to the MHWL under § 161.161(5). The littoral right of accretion was not applicable as, inter alia, §§ 161.088, 161.101(1), Fla. Stat. did not apply to de minimis additions or losses of land. The littoral right of access was explicitly preserved under the Act in § 161.201.


OUTCOME: The court answered the rephrased certified question in the negative and quashed the decision of the appellate court.

An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Rogers Padgett, Judge -- Case No. 04-CF-000774.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder and one count of armed carjacking. It then sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with killing a husband and wife after responding to their advertised attempts to sell a pickup truck. Sims v. State


No. SC05-400


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


998 So. 2d 494; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1628; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 698



September 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 22, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Sims v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2479 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fifth District - Case No. 5D02-2401 and 5D02-2448. (St. Johns County).
Sims v. State, 869 So. 2d 45, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2943 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's imposition of victim-injury points in a case where defendant was convicted of leaving the scene of an accident resulting in death in violation of § 316.027(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2001). After the state supreme court denied defendant's motion to invoke discretionary review, it granted his motion for reinstatement to review the appellate court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a vehicle that struck the victim, who was intoxicated and lying in the road. Defendant then drove away. He was charged with violating § 316.027(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2001), leaving the scene of an accident resulting in death. A medical examiner testified that the victim's death was "instantaneous" upon impact. Defendant was convicted. At sentencing, the State successfully argued for adding victim-injury points, which increased his sentence. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant was not informed by his state-appointed appellate counsel about the appellate court's decision until it was too late to file a notice to invoke jurisdiction under Fla. R. App. 9.120(b). The state supreme court then granted defendant's motion for reinstatement. It found that it could treat his belated notice as timely filed because his appellate counsel rendered ineffective assistance. It also found that because § 921.0021(7)(a), Fla. Stat. (2001) defined "victim injury" as injury suffered as a direct result of an offense, the victim-injury points could not be imposed in defendant's case because the victim's death was not directly caused by defendant leaving the scene of the accident.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court quashed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case to the appellate court for further proceedings.


 

325 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Wickham v. State


No. SC05-1012


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2008 Fla. LEXIS 1617; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 711



September 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 23, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, Kathleen F. Dekker, Judge -- Case No. 87-3970.
Wickham v. State, 593 So. 2d 191, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2122 (Fla., 1991)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, which denied his post-judgment motion to vacate his conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant unsuccessfully sought to disqualify the postconviction judge under § 38.10, Fla. Stat. (2001) and Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.160. The court concluded that the postconviction court erred by denying this motion because defendant demonstrated a well-founded fear of judicial bias. In his motion for postjudgment relief, defendant raised numerous ineffective assistance of counsel claims against his trial counsel, an attorney who ran for a circuit court judgeship while defendant's case was still pending and who became a judge on the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit. After the judge's appointment to the bench, his wife also joined the Second Circuit as a judge. Under these extraordinary circumstances, it was reasonable for defendant to fear that an appellate judge hearing the judge's testimony in determining defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim would be biased against defendant. On remand, if any witness invoked the Fifth Amendment privilege to avoid testifying, the postconviction court must determine whether that witness was entitled to the privilege.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new evidentiary hearing.


 

326 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Maas v. Olive


No. SC06-835, No. SC06-1263


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 196; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1623; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 694



September 25, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Appeals, one Circuit Court and one Certified Judgment of Trial Courts in and for Leon County, Terry Powell Lewis, Judge - Case Nos. 2003-CA-000291 and 1D06-2091.
Dep't of Children & Families v. Alvarado, 946 So. 2d 130, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 483 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sued appellee state official, seeking, inter alia, a declaration that § 27.7002, Fla. Stat. (2007) violated the courts' inherent authority under art. V, Fla. Const. and the separation of powers under art. II, Fla. Const. After the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) granted the attorney summary judgment, the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the cross appeals as matters of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Under the appellate court's prior decision in the case, the attorney had standing to obtain a declaratory judgment of his rights as he was appointed as registry counsel for a death-sentenced inmate in postconviction proceedings. The prior decision did not foreclose the instant complaint as § 27.7002, Fla. Stat. (2007) was enacted after the prior decision was rendered. Thus, the complaint presented a justiciable controversy. The circuit court construed § 27.7002(5) and (6), Fla. Stat. (2007) to permit compensation above the statutory fee schedule in appropriate cases and to permit attorneys to request such compensation when justified by unusual or extraordinary circumstances, noting that the provisions had to be so construed in order to preserve the statute's constitutionality. The appellate court agreed because interpreting the statute to mean that fee caps could not be exceeded in any circumstances rendered it unconstitutional. The statute had to be interpreted and applied to ensure effective and competent representation in complex and unusual capital postconviction proceedings in order to afford death row inmates meaningful access to counsel in their collateral proceedings.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order granting the attorney summary judgment was affirmed.


 

327 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Power v. State


No. SC07-1139


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 218; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1638; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 717



September 25, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Alice Blackwell White, Judge -- Case No. CR89-1798.
Power v. State, 886 So. 2d 952, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 662 (Fla., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. Appellant had been convicted of, inter alia, first degree murder, sexual battery, and kidnapping of a child under the age of 13 and had been sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The instant motion raised constitutional challenges to the state's death penalty scheme; the motion was summarily denied in its entirety. On appeal, the court affirmed. While appellant argued that § 922.105, Fla. Stat. (2006) violated the separation of powers doctrine by giving the state department of corrections (DOC) unfettered discretion to create a lethal injection protocol, the court had previously rejected such an argument. The state's lethal injection procedures did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII based on precedent holding that additional procedural safeguards in 2007 by the DOC addressed prior deficiencies. Claiming that American Bar Association (ABA) Resolution 122A constituted newly discovered evidence, appellant argued that he was exempt from execution based on severe mental illness; however, the Resolution did not contain anything that would cause the court to recede from prior decisions upholding the constitutionality of the death penalty. The claim was untimely, and on the merits, mental illness had not been recognized as a per se bar to execution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Decision reached on appeal by, Sub nomine at Victorino v. State, 23 So. 3d 87, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1954 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, William A. Parsons, Judge -- Case No. 2004-01380CFAWS.
Salas v. State, 972 So. 2d 941, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 19780 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of six counts of first-degree murder. The Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) imposed a death sentence for each conviction. Defendant challenged his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly denied a motion to suppress statements made to law enforcement officers where defendant failed to show, inter alia, that he was in custody prior to being read his Miranda rights. The motion to suppress the physical evidence seized from defendant's temporary residence was properly denied where the warrant was sufficiently precise to include the seizure of his shoe laces, particularly as stains were observed on them. Crim. P. 3.152(b)(2) where defendant failed to identify codefendant statements that would have been inadmissible had he been tried alone. The claims as to the jury instructions and the sentences also failed.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Fla. Bar v. Sibley


No. SC06-1387


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


995 So. 2d 346; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1620; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 734



September 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Fla. Bar v. Sibley, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2268 (Fla., Nov. 14, 2008)
Stay denied by Sibley v. Fla. Bar, 555 U.S. 1151, 129 S. Ct. 1054, 173 L. Ed. 2d 467, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 963 (Jan. 26, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sibley v. Fla. Bar, 555 U.S. 1188, 129 S. Ct. 1348, 173 L. Ed. 2d 615, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1292 (Feb. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Fla. Bar v. Sibley, 979 So. 2d 221, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 485 (Fla., Mar. 7, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney filed post-discipline motions. The motions challenged the authority and power of some of the court justices to act as constitutional judicial officers.


OVERVIEW: The attorney contended that the referee who presided in his Bar discipline case and all but one of the justices did not have authority to act because they had allegedly failed to properly execute loyalty oaths to serve as constitutional judicial officers with their respective courts. The attorney relied upon § 876.05, Fla. Stat. The court found that the attorney's arguments and positions were both inaccurate and legally insufficient. Each of the justices on the court had taken the oath of office as prescribed by the Florida Constitution. Further all of the justices had executed judicial office loyalty oaths and oaths of office at the time of appointment and for each retention election thereafter. All of the justices appointed in 1998 or earlier executed written, notarized oaths of office that complied with § 876.05. The court also found that the referee who presided over the attorney's case complied with the constitutional requisites before assuming the duties of his office. Further, the Florida Constitution established the requisite oath for the judicial officers, not § 876.05. If there were any actual defect in the oath, it would be cleared by the de facto officer doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court denied the attorney's post-discipline motions to vacate the decision.

Stein v. State


No. SC06-1505


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


995 So. 2d 329; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1627; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 736



September 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stein v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2267 (Fla., Nov. 19, 2008)
Decision reached on appeal by Stein v. State, 91 So. 3d 784, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 824 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, David C. Wiggins, Judge -- Case No. 91-1505-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The inmate had been convicted of two counts or murder and one count of armed robbery, and sentenced to death for each murder and life for the armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found no merit in the inmate's claim that the trial judge erred in granting the inmate's motion for disqualification, as the mere presence of a sentencing order in the State's file, without more, did not give rise to a well-founded fear that defendant would not receive a fair trial. The supreme court also concluded that trial counsel was not ineffective at the guilt phase for conceding guilt, as it was a strategic decision made in an effort to obtain credibility for seeking a "jury pardon," and the inmate, after having discussed the strategy with defense counsel, consented to the strategy. The inmate's claim that defense counsel was ineffective at the penalty phase also failed, as counsel investigated mitigating evidence, but found witnesses who could do more damage than help. Finally, the supreme court concluded that the inmate was not entitled to a new trial based on newly discovered evidence, the life sentence imposed on codefendant, because the inmate did not establish that codefendant was the dominating force and there was substantial evidence that the inmate was the triggerman and thus, the more culpable one.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the postconviction court was affirmed.
