Strand v. Escambia County


No. SC06-1894


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 150; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1604; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 680



September 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Strand v. Escambia County, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2259 (Fla., Nov. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County - Bond Validations, Michael G. Allen, Judge - Case No. 2006-CA-881.
Strand v. Escambia County, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1745 (Fla., Sept. 28, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant intervenor challenged a final judgment validating a proposed bond issue from the Circuit Court of the First Judicial Circuit, in and for Escambia County, Florida. Appellees were Escambia County, Florida, etc., et al.


OVERVIEW: The intervenor raised three issues: (A) whether the circuit court abused its discretion in denying his motion for continuance, (B) whether the circuit court's final judgment was supported by competent, substantial evidence, and (C) whether the bonds required a referendum pursuant to art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const. On the first issue, given the adequacy of the notice provided and the circuit court's accommodation, the circuit court did not abuse its discretion. With regard to the second issue, the intervenor argued that the circuit court's adoption of the County's proposed final judgment was an improper delegation of authority. This contention was without merit because the intervenor was afforded a meaningful opportunity to review the County's proposed final judgment, make objections, and make his own proposals. Next, the court stated that the findings in the Ordinance and Resolution were not shown to have been clearly erroneous. Finally, the third issue was controlled by the court's decision in Penn, in which the court previously affirmed the Circuit Court's validation of bonds issued under a similar tax ordinance and resolution and issuance structure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final judgment of validation of the Escambia County Circuit Court.

 

334 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



City of Parker v. State


No. SC07-1400


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 171; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1613; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 671



September 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County -- Bond Validations. Dedee S. Costello, Judge -- Case No. 07-000889-CA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida) which invalidated tax-increment-financed bonds proposed for issuance by the city pursuant to the Community Redevelopment Act. However, the trial court found no merit to appellee county's challenges to the city's finding of blight, to the city's finding of conformity, and to the constitutionality of tax increment financing. The county cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a bond ordinance which authorized it to issue bonds for the purpose of financing capital projects identified in a redevelopment area. Absent its approval of supplemental ordinances, the tax increment revenues deposited into the trust fund were the only source of revenues pledged to repay the bonds. After receiving notice of the city's intention, the county sought to enjoin the city from enforcing its Community Redevelopment Act resolutions and ordinances. The appellate court held the plain language of the Community Redevelopment Act did not require it to levy ad valorem taxes in order to issue the proposed tax-increment-financed bonds. Te general statement in § 163.358, Fla. Stat., the Community Redevelopment Act, listed the discrete steps a county or municipality had to undertake to employ tax increment financing, and no step required that the city levy ad valorem taxes. The appellate found that the Community Redevelopment Act did not require the city to levy ad valorem taxes in order to issue the proposed tax-increment-financed bonds. The trial court also correctly concluded that there was substantial evidence to support the city's legislative finding of blight.


OUTCOME: The trial court's conclusion that the city could not issue the proposed bonds because it did not levy ad valorem taxes was reversed. The trial court's conclusions regarding the finding of blight, the finding of conformity, and the constitutionality of tax increment financing was affirmed.

Sexton v. State


No. SC07-286


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


997 So. 2d 1073; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1610; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 686



September 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Sexton v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2403 (Fla., Dec. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Joseph Rogers Padgett, Judge -- Case No. 94-1299.
Sexton v. State, 775 So. 2d 923, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1993 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of first-degree murder, sought postconviction review after his conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) denied relief after the evidentiary hearing. It found, inter alia, that penalty phase counsel performed a reasonable investigation into defendant's background to discover potential mitigation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for the killing of his son-inlaw. The victim was murdered by defendant's mentally challenged 22-year-old son, who strangled him to death under defendant's direction. In sentencing defendant to death, the trial court found three aggravating circumstances, including that the murder was committed for the purpose of avoiding a lawful arrest. Defendant primarily criticized his trial counsel for a so-called "rifle" approach, which highlighted strong mental mitigation, rather than a "shotgun" approach that would include any and all factors discovered by counsel that might conceivably be considered mitigating. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that defendant failed to demonstrate that counsel was deficient in his mitigation investigation or presentation. Counsel presented the information he was able to obtain, given the reticence of family members and his own client to report any unfavorable family history and the inability to obtain certain records. If counsel had put on additional mental health evidence, it would have opened the door to further possibly damaging evidence. The remaining examples of ineffective counsel were also unavailing.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

336 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bay County v. Town of Cedar Grove


No. SC07-1572, No. SC07-1574


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 164; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1612; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 678



September 18, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County -- Bond Validations. Dedee S. Costello, Judge -- Case No. 07-1771-CA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee town filed complaints in the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida), for validation of bond proposals. Appellant county intervened in the proceedings. Appellee, the State of Florida, required strict proof of the matters alleged but did not otherwise object to validation. After conducting a consolidated hearing, the circuit court entered final judgments validating the bond proposals. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town proposed two tax-increment-financed bonds pursuant to the Florida Community Redevelopment Act, pt. III of ch. 163, Fla. Stat. (2006). The county contended that § 163.346, Fla. Stat. (2006), required two public readings for resolutions adopted by the town pursuant to the Act. In addition, the county argued that the proposed tax-increment-financed bonds violated the referendum requirement of art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const. On appeal, the court found that, because § 163.346, Fla. Stat., incorporated only the public notice requirements of §§ 166.041(3)(a) and 125.66(2), Fla. Stat. (2006), § 163.346 did not impose a two-reading requirement for resolutions adopted pursuant to the Act. As a result, the town was not required to conduct two readings at two public meetings when enacting its redevelopment resolutions. In addition, the proposed bonds did not violate art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const. because the proposed bonds did not pledge the taxing power of any government entity. The bondholders had no right, if the trust funds were insufficient to meet the bond obligations, to compel the levy of ad valorem taxation. Consequently, the proposed bonds were constitutional without a referendum.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Fla. Dep't of State v. Slough

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Department of State, sought review in the Florida Court of Appeals of a decision of the trial courts in and for Leon County, (Florida), which entered a summary judgment in favor of appellees and ordered a proposed amendment 5 removed from the November 2008 ballot. The appellate court certified the matter to the court for immediate resolution.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Taxation and Budget Reform Commission proposed an amendment (Amendment 5) to the Florida Constitution that would impact and change several aspects of Florida's taxation and financial structure. Jones v. State


No. SC06-474, No. SC07-729


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2008 Fla. LEXIS 1565; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 622



September 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 23, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by Jones v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2426 (Fla., Dec. 23, 2008)
Substituted opinion at Jones v. State, 998 So. 2d 573, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2434 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, William L. Gary, Judge - Case No. 91-1932-CF.
Jones v. State, 648 So. 2d 669, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1588 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 after his conviction of first-degree murder and the imposition of a death sentence. Appellant also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Testimony from a witness who was appellant's cellmate in a medical cell indicated that appellant met the victim at a liquor store and subsequently tried to take the victim's money after they went to a pond. During a struggle, appellant allegedly drowned the victim. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of postconviction relief and denied the petition for habeas corpus. No Brady violation occurred based on an alleged failure to disclose evidence of an agreement with the witness as the witness, a detective, and the prosecutor all denied that any promises to benefit the witness were made. As no promise had been made, any testimony as to the witness's release from jail was not false; thus, no Giglio violation occurred. While trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate evidence of mental health mitigation based on an available report of a forensic psychologist that appellant suffered from mental illness, appellant was not prejudiced as substantial aggravators (prior felony conviction and heinous, atrocious, or cruel) were presented and other conflicting evidence indicated that appellant was not mentally ill but suffered from an antisocial personality disorder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

340 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Lawnwood Med. Ctr. v. Seeger


No. SC07-1300


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


990 So. 2d 503; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1458; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 590



August 28, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. (Leon County). First District - Case No. 1D06-2016.
Lawnwood Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Seeger, 959 So. 2d 1222, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 9569 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation brought an action seeking to have the St. Lucie County Hospital Governance Law (HGL), ch. 2003-372, Laws of Fla., declared constitutional. Appellee president of the corporation's medical staff opposed the petition. Both parties moved for summary judgment, and the trial court held that the HGL violated Art. III, § 11(a)(12), Fla. Const. The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, affirmed. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court found, inter alia, that the HGL altered many of the rights and obligations specified in the contract between the corporation's medical staff and its board of trustees, constituting an impermissible privilege. The appellate court found, among other things, that the HGL provided the hospital with a complete override of medical staff bylaws. Moreover, Ch. 2003-372, § 5, at 448, Laws of Fla. granted the corporation's board of trustees the right and power to unilaterally amend the medical staff bylaws, something it could not do before enactment of the HGL. The HGL altered the framework for governing, and the medical staff's important role in it pursuant to the bylaws, in a manner favorable to the board, and essentially gave the board plenary power to take independent action in these areas. These facets of the HGL granted the corporation a "right" and placed it in an advantageous position, one that it did not possess before the law was enacted. The HGL granted the corporation rights, benefits, or advantages and thus, a "privilege" in contravention of Art. III, § 11(a)(12), Fla. Const. The unconstitutional provisions were not severable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Morton v. State, 789 So. 2d 324, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1250 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida), which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion to vacate his death sentences for two first-degree murder convictions. Appellant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: During the course of committing a burglary with two others, appellant shot one victim and attempted to shoot and stab the other victim. Appellant filed a motion for postconviction relief, claiming, inter alia, ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed and also denied the request for a writ of habeas corpus. Even if counsel's performance had been deficient, appellant was not prejudiced as substantial aggravators were found as the trial court concluded that the first victim's death was cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) and the second victim's death was heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief. The court also denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

(2007); (2) counsel made an informed decision not to present any witnesses during the guilt phase of the trial; (3) counsel timely requested a Richardson hearing after a witness changed his testimony; (4) counsel's decision to seek a mistrial rather than a Richardson hearing when a witness alluded to the inmate being in a gang was a reasonable one; (5) the inmate's Brady violation claim failed because the information he claimed was improperly withheld either did not exist prior to trial or was not exculpatory in nature; (6) R. 344 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Liner v. Workers Temp. Staffing, Inc.


No. SC07-1470


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


990 So. 2d 473; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1380; 156 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,651; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 583



July 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 28, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. (Broward County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D05-4729.
Liner v. Workers Temp. Staffing, Inc., 962 So. 2d 344, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10387 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant day laborer appealed from the Fourth District Court of Appeal, Florida, which had declared the Florida Labor Pool Act (2004) invalid, and thus, defendant labor hall was not liable to the laborer on an alleged violation of Fla. Stat. § 448.24(1)(b) (2004) for overcharging day laborers for transportation to various worksites.


OVERVIEW: Reaching the constitutionality issue had been unnecessary. The actual damages claimed was minimal compared to Fla. Stat. § 448.25(1) (2004)'s statutory damages. Thus, the Act was penal in nature, to be construed in favor of the labor hall. Fla. Stat. § 448.24(1)(b) (2004)'s plain language established that the Legislature intended for "to or from the designated worksite," in the first clause, to modify the entire second clause, which included the more general "geographic area." Reasonable testimony had shown that transportation in the area was predicated upon a tri-county basis published by a regional transportation authority. The "geographic area" was based upon the public-transportation system in place for a particular area. "Public transportation" was not limited to bus travel in the area. The cost associated with traveling from a bus stop to the worksite, and its return at the end of the day had to be taken into account in determining a reasonable transportation charge. The labor hall's charge of $ 1.50 for site-to-site transportation was a "reasonable amount." Given the rates for taxi service, $ 1.50 did not exceed the cost of public transportation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed with regard to the holding that the Act was unconstitutional, but the labor hall was not liable for the alleged violation.


 

345 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wyche v. State


No. SC05-1509


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


987 So. 2d 23; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1229; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 509



July 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wyche v. Florida, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8954 (U.S., Dec. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. First District - Case No. 1D03-5211. (Columbia County)
Wyche v. State, 906 So. 2d 1142, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9491 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress and granted the State's motion for denial of the motion, defendant was tried and convicted of burglary, grand theft, and criminal mischief. The Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, affirmed the convictions, and certified conflict with another district court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was in custody on another matter, an investigator asked him for a saliva sample, stating that he was suspected of committing a supermarket burglary. In fact, the investigator had manufactured the fictitious supermarket burglary in order to obtain defendant's consent to take swabs for a sexual-assault case. Defendant was exonerated in the sexual-assault case, but the saliva was used to convict defendant in the current case. The issue was whether defendant's consent was involuntary. The appellate court found, among other things, that defendant was aware that the officer wanted the DNA sample in order to investigate a crime, and the officer did not misrepresent the fact that he had no search warrant. The officer did not indicate that defendant had no choice regarding whether to provide a DNA sample. The custodial setting of defendant's consent and the investigator's failure to inform defendant of the actual purpose of the search were not factors so controlling as to overpower defendant's will. Defendant was not deluded as to the import of his consent. However, the appellate court distinguished rather than disapproved the other case believed to have been in conflict.


OUTCOME: The appellate court approved the decision of the intermediate appellate court to affirm the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress the saliva swabs. The case believed to have been in conflict was distinguished rather than disapproved.

 

346 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Kasischke v. State


No. SC07-128


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


991 So. 2d 803; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1241; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 481



July 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Kasischke v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1719 (Fla., Sept. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Dade County). Third District - Case No. 3D04-2149.
Kasischke v. State, 946 So. 2d 1155, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21282 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION:  The appellate court's opinion was quashed, and the matter was remanded to the appellate court with instructions to return it to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sex offender pled guilty to lewd or lascivious battery and exhibition on a child under age 16 and was sentenced to, inter alia, community control and probation. His community control was ordered revoked when pornography was found in his home. He appealed, and the Third District Court of Appeals (Florida) affirmed, so he sought further review, alleging a direct conflict with the decision of another appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court's decision that defendant could not, under former § 948.03(5)(a)(7), Fla. Stat. (1999) (now § 948.30(1)(g), Fla. Stat. (2007)), possess any pornography as a condition of his community control conflicted with another court's decision that such pornography had to be relevant to an offender's deviant behavior. The supreme court held the statute could be reasonably construed in at least four ways. It could not be interpreted in a manner that rendered some of its language superfluous, and neither the bill title nor a staff analysis clarified it. The doctrine of the last antecedent did not show the phrase "that are relevant to the offender's deviant behavior pattern" qualified the phrase "sexually stimulating visual or auditory material." Given the statute's ambiguity, the rule of lenity in § 775.021(1), Fla. Stat. (2007), requiring that any ambiguity be resolved in defendant's favor, had to be applied, so "relevant to the offender's deviant behavior pattern" qualified all pornography defendant was barred from possessing, and he violated the statute only if material found in his home was relevant to his "deviant behavior pattern," which had not been addressed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's opinion was quashed, and the matter was remanded to the appellate court with instructions to return it to the trial court for further proceedings.

Lescher v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles


No. SC07-32


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


985 So. 2d 1078; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1221; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 434



July 3, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Palm Beach County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D06-2291.
Lescher v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 946 So. 2d 1140, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21284 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver sought review of a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed that the permanent revocation of his driver license by respondent, the Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles, and the elimination of hardship eligibility pursuant to §§ 322.28(2)(e) and 322.271(4), Fla. Stat. (2000; 2003), was not an ex post facto law. A question of great public importance was certified on the issue.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted of DUI on four occasions. Pursuant to § 322.28(2)(e), his license was permanently revoked. Although there was a provision that allowed for license eligibility upon a showing of hardship at the time that the driver's license was revoked, that provision was eliminated in an amendment pursuant to § 322.271(4). The driver's petition for a hardship license was denied, and his requests for a writ of certiorari were denied by the trial court and the court of appeals upon the determination that there was no ex post facto violation. However, a question of great public importance on the issue was certified to the court for review. The court held that the Ex Post Facto Clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Art. I, § 10, Fla. Const., were not violated by the statutory scheme, including the amendment. The court analyzed the matter under the seven-factor ex post facto test and found that the license revocation and hardship eligibility elimination were not criminal provisions, as they were part of a regulatory scheme to protect the public.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question by holding that there was no ex post facto violation, and in so doing, it approved the decision of the court of appeals.

Hudson v. State


No. SC06-748


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


992 So. 2d 96; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1217; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 465



July 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 25, 2008.
As Revised September 25, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Hudson v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1622 (Fla., Sept. 25, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hudson v. Fla., 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1286 (U.S., Feb. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Paul L. Backman, Judge -- Case No. 01-17757-CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) of first-degree murder and armed kidnapping and was sentenced to death and a consecutive life sentence. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a rival drug dealer. The supreme court held the victim's phone call was an excited utterance because a gunman's announced intent to kill him, described in the call, was sufficiently startling. Defendant opened the door to hearsay by volunteering hearsay to answer a proper question, which could be clarified with the entire statement. A comment that he would not further implicate a person who ordered the murder did not comment on his right to remain silent because he did not invoke the right. His proposal to modify the standard heinous, atrocious and cruel aggravator instruction was denied because it was covered by the standard instruction, which told the jury to focus on his acts' effect on the victim. Comments on circumstances leading up to the murder were not fundamental error because they related to the victim's perception of and reaction to his impending death. Testimony that the victim knew he would die wrongly exceeded what the witness saw but was harmlessly brief and based on testimony from which the inference could be made. Evidence supported the heinous, atrocious and cruel and cold, calculated and premeditated aggravators.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

351 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. House of Representatives v. Crist


No. SC07-2154


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


990 So. 2d 1035; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1220; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 437



July 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication September 11, 2008.
Reported at Fla. House of Representatives v. Crist, 999 So. 2d 601, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2512 (Fla., 2008)
Rehearing denied by Fla. House of Representatives v. Crist, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1689 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Seminole Tribe v. Fla. House of Representatives, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1696 (U.S., Mar. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding -- Quo Warranto
Seminole Tribe v. Florida, 517 U.S. 44, 116 S. Ct. 1114, 134 L. Ed. 2d 252, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 2165 (1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Florida House of Representatives and its Speaker, filed a petition for a writ of quo warranto that disputed respondent Florida Governor's (FG) authority to bind the State to a gambling "compact" with the Seminole Indian Tribe of Florida. The compact significantly expanded casino gambling on tribal lands in return for substantial remuneration to the State under the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 2701-2721.


OVERVIEW: The Indian Tribe signed the gambling "compact" with the FG, which regulated "gaming." The Florida Legislature did not authorize the FG to negotiate the compact before it was signed, and it did not ratify it thereafter. Rather, petitioners brought their action. The court initially determined that it had jurisdiction over the writ petition pursuant to Art. V, § 3(b)(8), Fla. Const., based on the importance and immediacy of the issue. The court reviewed various exercises of authority with respect to compacts. The court held that the Legislature had the power under the residual authority power to execute the compact at issue. Further, the court determined that the "necessary business" clause of Art. IV, § 1(a), Fla. Const., did not authorize the FG to execute the compact because it was contrary to the expressed public policy of Florida or was prohibited under Florida law. Lastly, the court concluded that the compact violated the separation of powers under Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const., as it violated Florida's public policy about the types of gambling that was allowed. Such was the type of action particularly within the Legislature's power.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition but withheld issuance of the writ of quo warranto.


 

352 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. House of Representatives v. Crist


No. SC07-2154


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


999 So. 2d 601; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2512



July 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication September 11, 2008.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Seminole Tribe v. Fla. House of Representatives, 129 S. Ct. 1526, 173 L. Ed. 2d 657, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1696 (U.S., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding -- Quo Warranto
Fla. House of Representatives v. Crist, 990 So. 2d 1035, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1220 (Fla., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner House of Representatives filed a petition for a writ of quo warranto against respondent Governor; the House claimed that the Governor lacked authority to bind the state to a compact allowing Class III gaming on Indian lands, pursuant to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 2701-2721 (2000) (IGRA).


OVERVIEW: After almost 16 years of sporadic negotiations with four governors, the Seminole Indian Tribe of Florida signed a gambling "compact" with the Governor. The compact authorized the Tribe to conduct "covered gaming," which included some Class III gaming, such as banked card games, that was prohibited under §§ 849.08, 849.086(12)(a), (15)(a), Fla. Stat. The state supreme court held that the Governor did not have the constitutional authority to bind the state to a gaming compact that clearly departed from the state's public policy by legalizing types of gaming that were illegal everywhere else in the state. Because the compact changed the state's public policy as expressed in the criminal law, it violated the separation of powers clause in Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const. IGRA did not grant the Governor, or any state actor, any powers beyond those provided by the state's constitution and laws. By authorizing the Tribe to conduct banked card games that were illegal throughout Florida--and thus illegal for the Tribe--the compact violated Florida law.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, but issuance of the writ was withheld.


 

353 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist. v. Echeverri


No. SC07-1556


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


991 So. 2d 793; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1222; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 445



July 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist. v. Echeverri, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1693 (Fla., Sept. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Clay County). First District - Case No. 1D06-2026 and 1D06-2158.
Zingale v. Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist., 960 So. 2d 20, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7005 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner community development sought review of a decision from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) which, inter alia, held that respondent county property appraiser had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 189.403(1), Fla. Stat. (1999), as an affirmative defense (AD). A direct conflict between that decision and one from the Second District Court of Appeal was certified for the court's review.


OVERVIEW: The development filed three actions against respondents, a county and/or state officials, alleging that pursuant to § 189.403(1), it should have been treated as a municipality and granted exemptions for ad valorem tax purposes. The development alternatively asserted constitutional rights violations. The appraiser asserted by way of AD that § 189.403(2) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the development's motions to strike the AD upon finding that the appraiser lacked standing to raise that issue. The trial court thereafter determined that the development was entitled to the requested tax exemptions. The court of appeals held, inter alia, that the appraiser had standing to raise the AD, and the matter was remanded for consideration thereof. On certification of a conflict with a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal, the court reviewed the history of a property appraiser's standing. It held that an appraiser lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of a statute as an AD in a tax suit by a taxpayer. In so holding, the court disapproved the holding of Fuchs v. Robbins, 818 So.2d 460 (Fla. 2002), which had been relied on by the court of appeals.


OUTCOME: The court resolved the conflict by holding that a property appraiser lacked standing in his official capacity to raise the constitutionality of a statute as an AD in a tax suit by a taxpayer. Accordingly, the court approved the holding of the Second District Court of Appeals and quashed the appellate court's decision in the instant action.

 

354 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Schwab v. State


No. SC08-1199


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


995 So. 2d 922; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1113; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 431



June 27, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Schwab Mark D. v. Fla., 128 S. Ct. 2996, 171 L. Ed. 2d 911, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5284 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Charles M. Holcomb, Judge - Case No. 05-1991-7249-AXXX.
Schwab v. State, 982 So. 2d 1158, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 55 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder, sexual battery of a child, and kidnapping, and was sentenced to death. He filed a third successive motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, which the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's PCR motion was similar to his prior motions, which also challenged Florida's lethal injection protocol. The PCR court noted that a defendant could not succeed on an Eighth Amendment objection to a method of execution unless he could proffer a feasible, readily implemented procedure that would, in fact, significantly reduce a severe risk of pain, The inmate's suggestions for additional training of prison personnel and a reduction in the amount of sodium pentathol did not meet this test. The inmate did not show that Florida's protocol for lethal injection significantly differed from Kentucky's, which had been approved by the U.S. Supreme Court, or that Florida's protocol created a demonstrated risk of severe pain. The high court adopted the PCR court's reasoning.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

355 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. SC06-615, No. SC07-1168


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2008 Fla. LEXIS 1108; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 410



June 19, 2008, Decided


NOTICE:

NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing denied by Taylor v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 139 (Fla., Jan. 29, 2009)
Substituted opinion at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Taylor v. State, 3 So. 3d 986, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 132 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Michael McCarthy, Judge -- Case No. 88-15525.
Taylor v. State, 638 So. 2d 30, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 650 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State charged appellant inmate with first-degree murder and sexual battery. He was convicted of both charges and was sentenced to death. Pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, he moved to vacate his murder conviction and death sentence. After holding an evidentiary hearing, the Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motion. The inmate appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued newly discovered evidence entitled him to a new trial. The high court disagreed. A medical examiner's testimony at the postconviction hearing that there was a one-in-a-million possibility the victim's vaginal injuries were caused by a kick was not a recantation of his trial testimony that the injuries were caused by insertion of an object into her vagina, and thus was not "new evidence." As the examiner's trial testimony was not false, there was no Giglio violation, and as it was essentially unchanged, the State did not suppress evidence in violation of Brady. Trial counsel was not deficient for failure to discover such evidence, or in preparing defendant to testify. The inmate received a competent mental health evaluation at trial, and did not prove counsel's investigation of this issue was deficient. Counsel was not deficient in investigating mitigating factors or in not calling the victim's daughter as a witness. A PET Scan was not newly discovered evidence entitling the inmate to relief, as two experts testified the scan did not indicate brain damage. The inmate's constitutional claims, not having been preserved on direct appeal, were procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmate's postconviction motion and denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.

 

356 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Collins


No. SC05-108


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


985 So. 2d 985; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1064; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 373



June 5, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Lee County). Second District - Case No. 2D02-3655.
Collins v. State, 893 So. 2d 592, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19512 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to robbery. The trial court sentenced him as a habitual felony offender to 20 years in prison. He appealed. The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed, holding the State presented insufficient evidence establishing the predicate convictions, and could not present additional evidence on remand. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: At sentencing, the State presented evidence of prior felony convictions. Defense counsel objected, arguing that the evidence failed to show the prior convictions were "separately sentenced," as required by § 775.084(5), Fla. Stat. (2001), of the habitual offender statute. The trial court overruled the objection. The intermediate appellate court held that the documents presented to the trial court failed to preclude the possibility that all of defendant's prior felony offenses were originally sentenced on the same date. It prohibited the State from correcting the error on remand by producing additional evidence. The high court held that this prohibition conflicted with rulings of the First, Fourth, and Fifth District Courts of Appeal (Florida), and that the latter rulings were correct. As resentencing was de novo, the State could produce new evidence to prove defendant's habitual offender status, and his Double Jeopardy Clause rights were not thereby violated. Shull v. Dugger did not apply to habitual offender sentencing. The due process inquiry was whether the new sentence was vindictive; the presumption of vindictiveness would arise only if a more severe sentence was imposed.


OUTCOME: The high court approved the decision of the intermediate appellate court reversing defendant's sentence, but quashed the decision to the extent it precluded the State from introducing additional evidence on remand.


 

357 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Davis v. State


No. SC06-1444


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


990 So. 2d 459; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1063; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 381



June 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 4, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Davis v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1722 (Fla., Sept. 4, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Davis v. Sec'y Dep't of Corr., 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 101364 (M.D. Fla., Oct. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Emmett Lamar Battles, Judge -- Case No. 98-CF-11873.
Davis v. State, 859 So. 2d 465, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1539 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. He filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, claiming, inter alia, that his guilt-phase and penalty-phase counsel were ineffective. After an evidentiary hearing, the Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: After consuming LSD, the inmate choked the victim, injected her with bleach, and stabbed her. The high court held that counsel was not deficient for failing to call experts at a suppression hearing to testify that the inmate's sleep deprivation and his being under the influence of LSD made his confession involuntary, as the Rule 3.851 testimony did not support these claims, and suppression of the confession was unlikely to have changed the outcome. As police did not use the "question first, warn later" method of questioning in a calculated way to undermine the Miranda warning, the inmate's Siefert claim failed. His Giglio claim failed as he did not show an officer's testimony was false and the prosecutor knew it. Not calling an expert to substantiate the inmate's voluntary intoxication defense was not ineffective assistance, as the expert testified at the Rule 3.851 hearing that LSD ingestion would not have negated the inmate's ability to plan. Penalty phase counsel was not deficient for failing to adduce mitigation testimony from an expert that could have done more harm than good, in preparing the expert, or for failing to rebut the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

358 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Jackson v. State


No. SC07-659


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


983 So. 2d 562; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 938; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 357



May 29, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Polk County). Second District - Case No. 2D05-4095.
Jackson v. State, 952 So. 2d 613, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4662 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State prosecuted petitioner inmate, and she was convicted of aggravated battery with a weapon. The inmate appealed on grounds that the trial court erred in hearing testimony from the victim for purposes of sentencing without defense counsel being present in the courtroom. The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed, concluding that this "sentencing error" was not preserved. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate did not preserve by contemporaneous objection her claim of a deprivation of counsel during part of a victim impact statement. The intermediate appellate court held that this was a claim of sentencing error and therefore should have been preserved for appeal as required by Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(e) by filing a motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b). The high court disagreed. A claim of partial deprivation of counsel during a sentencing hearing was a due process violation, not a "sentencing error" as contemplated by Rule 3.800(b), and therefore no motion under Rule 3.800(b) had to be filed. The unpreserved claim was therefore reviewable on appeal for fundamental error. The high court held that the temporary absence of counsel during a portion of the victim's testimony was not fundamental error. Counsel participated during a portion of the victim's testimony, and when counsel joined the hearing, the trial judge summarized the substance of the testimony counsel had not heard. At that point, counsel had the opportunity to question the victim (who was still on the stand). Thus, counsel's absence did not go to the foundation or merits of the case.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed, but its reasoning--that the "sentencing error" was not preserved--was not. Counsel's temporary absence was not a sentencing error, but an unpreserved due process violation that did not amount to fundamental error.


 

359 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


G.S. v. T.B.


No. SC07-2370


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


985 So. 2d 978; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1243; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 325



May 22, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 30, 2008.
Rehearing denied by G.S. v. T.B., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1288 (Fla., June 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D06-5264. (Duval County).
G.S. v. T.B., 969 So. 2d 1049, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14239 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) had certified a question as to the denial of a petition for adoption by petitioners, the maternal grandfather and his wife: did the trial court abuse its discretion granted by ch. 63, Fla. Stat., when it denied the petition, after determining petitioners to be fit prospective parents, on the basis that the denial was in the children's best interest for ensuring the paternal grandparents' involvement?


OVERVIEW: The children's mother had died shortly after the younger child's birth. The father died shortly thereafter in an automobile accident. The children then moved into petitioners' home. After petitioners sought to adopt the children, respondents filed a petition to have the paternal grandmother appointed as guardian. While the evidence indicated that petitioners were fit prospective parents, the trial court awarded guardianship of the children's persons to petitioners and guardianship of the children's property to respondents. The appellate court affirmed and certified a question, which the court answered in the affirmative. Because the State had a compelling interest in providing stable and permanent homes for adoptive children under § 63.022(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005), the issue before the trial court was whether the adoption by petitioners was in the children's best interests without consideration of some other form of custody such as guardianship. The split guardianship was the antithesis of the right to permanence and stability as, inter alia, guardianships required continuing judicial involvement under § 744.3675, Fla. Stat. (2005).


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative and quashed the decision of the appellate court and directed that the case be remanded to the trial court with directions that the petition for adoption be granted.

Hitchcock v. State


No. SC03-2203, No. SC04-1286


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


991 So. 2d 337; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 917; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 343



May 22, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 17, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Hitchcock v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1707 (Fla., Sept. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Reginald Karl Whitehead, Judge -- Case No. 48-1976-CF-001942-O And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Hitchcock v. State, 755 So. 2d 638, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 626 (Fla., Mar. 23, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate moved the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, after his third resentencing. The trial court denied the motion and the inmate appealed. The inmate also petitioned the Florida Supreme Court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied as procedurally barred the inmate's guilt phase claims and denied his resentencing claims on their merits. The supreme court held witnesses who said the inmate's now deceased brother admitted committing the murder were not credible, so the inmate was not entitled to a new trial. Not disclosing a hair analyst's poor evaluation did not violate Brady or Giglio because (1) nothing showed the analyst mishandled hairs in the inmate's case, (2) the hairs were destroyed, (3) excluding the analyst's testimony would not likely produce an acquittal, (4) the evaluation did not exist at trial, and (5) nothing showed the analyst falsely testified. Resentencing counsel was not ineffective for not objecting to the victim's sister's testimony because it was admissible to show an enumerated felony was committed during the murder and a heinous, atrocious and cruel murder. Resentencing counsel was not ineffective for not asking an expert if the inmate had (1) an extreme mental or emotional disturbance or (2) a substantial impairment of his capacity to appreciate his conduct's criminality or to conform it to the law given mitigation presented and aggravators proved.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, and the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Owen v. State


No. SC06-2104, No. SC07-650


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


986 So. 2d 534; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 809; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 569



May 8, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised July 10, 2008. Released for Publication July 10, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Owen v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1323 (Fla., July 10, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Owen v. Sec'y for the Dep't of Corr., 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 10484 (11th Cir. Fla., May 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Krista Marx, Judge - Case No. 84-4014CF A02 And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Owen v. State, 862 So. 2d 687, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1778 (Fla., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted sexual battery, and burglary; he was sentenced to death. He filed a motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, which the Palm Beach County Circuit Court (Florida) denied. He appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging, inter alia, ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed the PCR court erred by summarily denying certain claims. The high court disagreed, finding them all meritless. Counsel was not ineffective for not moving to suppress the inmate's confession under § 90.410, Fla. Stat. (1999), as his own testimony showed he did not have a reasonable belief he was negotiating a plea when he confessed. As an expert's testimony about the inmate's psychological impairment was inadmissible to support an insanity defense, and would have harmed the defense, counsel was not deficient in failing to present it. He did not establish a Brady violation, as he knew about his counselor's notes, which he claimed the State suppressed, and they were not material. He did not show counsel was deficient for not removing three jurors, as there was no showing they were biased. He did not show counsel was deficient during the penalty phase for not presenting evidence of his substance abuse, as such evidence likely would not have changed the sentence. The jury was properly instructed on mitigation. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise certain issues on direct appeal because they probably would have been found to be without merit.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the motion court's order and denied the inmate's habeas petition.


 

362 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lebron v. State


No. SC06-138


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


982 So. 2d 649; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 756; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 294



May 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Lebron v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 376 (Fla., Jan. 30, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County, Belvin Perry, Jr., Chief Judge - Case No. CR96-2147.
Lebron v. State, 894 So. 2d 849, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 5 (Fla., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and robbery with a firearm and was sentenced to death. His death sentences were twice overturned on appeal. After the second reversal and remand, the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County, Florida, sentenced defendant to death after conducting a Spencer hearing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the sentencing order, the trial court relied on information that was not presented during the third penalty-phase proceeding. The high court held that this was error, since a resentencing proceeding was de novo and began with a "clean slate''; it thus gave no weight to such evidence. The trial court properly rejected the age mitigator, as there was no evidence defendant was not functioning as a typical 21-year-old at the time of the crime. Giving little mitigation weight to the fact that the mother was a drug addict while pregnant with defendant, and used drugs when he was a child, was proper, as there was no evidence this had any impact on him. In view of the meager evidence that defendant was physically or psychologically abused, the trial court properly gave these factors little weight as mitigation. Any error from the use of special-verdict forms for aggravators and mitigators was harmless. The death sentence was proportionate to other cases in which one had been imposed, in view of defendant's three prior violent felonies, and the fact that the murder was committed while defendant was robbing the victim. The jury instructions and method of execution were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The death sentence was affirmed.

 

363 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Belvin


No. SC06-593


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


986 So. 2d 516; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 758; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 279



May 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 8, 2008.
Rehearing denied by State v. Belvin, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1301 (Fla., July 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Palm Beach County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D04-4235.
Belvin v. State, 922 So. 2d 1046, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3305 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of driving under the influence (DUI). He appealed. The intermediate court of appeal affirmed. He sought certiorari review. The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that admission of certain portions of a breath test affidavit violated defendant's constitutional right to confrontation under Crawford, remanded the case for a new trial, and certified a question to the high court for its review.


OVERVIEW: The breath test technician who administered the breath test to defendant and prepared a breath test affidavit under § 316.1934(5), Fla. Stat. (2007), did not testify. The affidavit was admitted over defendant's objections. The high court held that the breath test affidavit was "testimonial" for purposes of Crawford because it was created to prove a critical element in the DUI criminal prosecution, not during an ongoing emergency or contemporaneously with the crime. As it was undisputed that the technician had left the State to avoid a criminal charge, the State met its burden to show she was unavailable at trial. Defendant did not waive his opportunity to cross-examine the technician by failing to depose her under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.220(h)(1)(D). Therefore, as he had no prior opportunity for cross-examination, admission of the affidavit violated his Sixth Amendment Confrontation Clause rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the second intermediate appellate court was affirmed, and its certified question was answered as follows: Admission of those portions of the breath test affidavit pertaining to the breath test operator's procedures and observations in administering the breath test constituted testimonial evidence and violated the Sixth Amendment's Confrontation Clause as interpreted by Crawford.

Woodel v. State


No. SC05-1336


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


985 So. 2d 524; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 754; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 290



May 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 11, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Woodel v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1299 (Fla., June 26, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Woodel v. Florida, 555 U.S. 1036, 129 S. Ct. 607, 172 L. Ed. 2d 465, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8491 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Woodel, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1808 (Fla., June 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Susan W. Roberts, Judge - Case No. CF97-00047A-XX.
Woodel v. State, 804 So. 2d 316, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2308 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Polk County Circuit Court (Florida) of two murders and other crimes. After his two death sentences were reversed and the case was remanded, he was sentenced to death for one murder, and to life imprisonment for the other. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to killing an elderly couple. After a second sentencing hearing, the trial court followed the jurors' recommendation. Defendant argued that dismissing two jurors for cause because they were not proficient in English violated his right to a jury composed of a fair cross-section of the community. The high court held that exclusion of the jurors was valid as a "public necessity" under § 40.013(6), Fla. Stat. (2005), because Florida case law banned interpreters from jury rooms during deliberations. Further, defendant failed to show that the class of Hispanics not proficient in English was a distinctive group in the community. An informant's testimony that defendant admitted fondling the wife was relevant to the nature of the crime and was thus admissible under § 921.141(1), Fla. Stat. (2005). Evidence that the 74-year-old wife had not regained the strength in an arm she had broken supported the aggravating factor that the victim was particularly vulnerable due to advanced age or disability. The death sentence was proportional to other similar crimes. Florida's execution protocol, including a three-drug cocktail, did not violate the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The sentences were affirmed.

 

365 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Massey v. David


No. SC07-776


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


979 So. 2d 931; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 552; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 229



April 3, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. (Alachua County). First District - Case No. 1D06-3657.
Massey v. David, 953 So. 2d 599, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3653 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former client sued appellee attorney for malpractice. A jury found the attorney negligent but awarded the client no damages; the trial court awarded the attorney expert witness fees. The client appealed the fee award on grounds the attorney had not complied with § 57.071(2), Fla. Stat. (1999). The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed, finding that § 57.071(2) was unconstitutional. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney represented the client in a personal injury case. Pursuant to their retainer agreement, they submitted their dispute about settlement to arbitration. The arbitrator decided the client should accept the settlement. The attorney filed a motion to approve settlement with the trial court. The trial court granted the attorney's motion and directed the client to sign the settlement; the client refused, discharged the attorney, and hired other counsel. The trial court appointed a guardian ad litem to sign the release on behalf of the client; it divided the contingency fees between the attorney and new counsel. This suit followed. The client argued that the intermediate appellate court erred in finding § 57.071(2), which provided a time limit for filing a written report, unconstitutional. The high court disagreed. As it was § 92.231(2), Fla. Stat. (2007), that created the right to tax expert witness fees as costs, § 57.071(2), Fla. Stat., was exclusively procedural in nature. It thus impermissibly encroached on the high court's rulemaking authority conferred by Art. V, § 2(a), Fla. Const., thereby violating the separation of powers provision, Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

366 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Phillips v. State


No. SC06-2554


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


984 So. 2d 503; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 442; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 219



March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 12, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Phillips v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1172 (Fla., June 12, 2008)
Motion denied by Phillips v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1806 (Fla., Sept. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Israel U. Reyes, Judge - Case No. 83-435.
Phillips v. State, 705 So. 2d 1320, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1458 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an inmate sentenced to death in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), challenged an order denying his successive motion to vacate his judgment and sentence and an order concluding that he was not mentally retarded under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203.


OVERVIEW: The inmate challenged the circuit court's determination that he was not mentally retarded in accordance with the three prongs of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203 and § 921.137(1), Fla. Stat. (2006). The supreme court found the majority of his IQ scores exceeded that required under § 921.137. Moreover, the trial court questioned the validity of the only IQ score falling within the statutory range for mental retardation. Therefore, evidence supported the finding that the inmate did not meet the first prong of the mental retardation definition. The evidence also supported the trial court's conclusion that the inmate failed to prove the second prong--impairments in adaptive functioning. Aside from personal independence, the inmate demonstrated that he was healthy, well-nourished, well-groomed, and exhibited good hygiene. Likewise, there was no evidence of deficits of adaptive behavior in regards to home living, use of community resources, or leisure. The inmate did not meet the third prong, onset of significantly subaverage general intellectual functioning with deficits in adaptive behavior before age 18. Anecdotes about the inmate's childhood were insufficient to meet this definition.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying the inmate's Rule 3.851 motion and concluding that he was not mentally retarded was affirmed.


 

367 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Bevel v. State


No. SC05-2213


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


983 So. 2d 505; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 443; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 202



March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 23, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Bevel v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 998 (Fla., May 23, 2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at Bevel v. State, 139 So. 3d 884, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1285 (Fla., Apr. 14, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by Bevel v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1314 (Fla., June 15, 2017)
Review dismissed by, As moot Bevel v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1478 (Fla., July 10, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Lawrence Page Haddock, Judge -- Case No. 16-2004-CF-4525-AXXX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directly appealed his convictions in the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) of two counts of first-degree murder and one count of attempted first-degree murder and sentences of death.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that defendant murdered two victims and attempted to murder a third; thus, the prior violent felony aggravator, § 921.141(5)(b), Fla. Stat. (2005) was applicable to each count based upon the contemporaneous murder and attempted murder convictions. In light of the totality of the circumstances, including a very weighty prior violent felony aggravator based on a first-degree murder conviction, an attempted first-degree murder conviction, a prior robbery involving the use of a firearm occurring just one year before the murders, and minimal nonstatutory mitigation, death was a proportionate punishment as to the murder of one victim. If the death penalty was proportionate for the first-degree murder of that victim, then a fortiori it was a proportionate punishment for the first-degree murder of the second victim, because the trial court found an additional aggravating circumstance, murder to avoid arrest, applicable to the second victim. Although defendant's full-scale IQ was low, there was competent, substantial evidence that he understood his Miranda rights and voluntarily waived them. Accordingly, the denial of his motion to suppress was appropriate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree murder convictions and his sentences of death were affirmed.

Israel v. State


No. SC05-1739, No. SC06-653


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


985 So. 2d 510; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 441; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 211



March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 26, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Israel v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1275 (Fla., June 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County, Kim C. Hammond, Judge -- Case No. CR93-1684 And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Israel v. State, 837 So. 2d 381, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2664 (Fla., Dec. 19, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sexually assaulted and murdered an elderly woman; he was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. He filed a motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851; the Putnam County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motion. He appealed this ruling and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued counsel was ineffective during the penalty phase closing argument. The high court held that while the argument was brief, counsel made a strategic decision not to focus on the inmate's substance abuse or to present possibly damaging testimony from family members. Though counsel's failure to file a sentencing memorandum may have been deficient, there was no prejudice, as the trial court independently identified and weighed the mitigating and aggravating factors. Counsel was not ineffective in presenting mitigating evidence; the inmate did not produce any mitigating evidence at the PCR hearing that was not presented at trial. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for not challenging the constitutionality of R. Regulating Fla. Bar 3.575, as the inmate did not allege trial counsel was denied a post-trial juror interview under Rule 3.575. The inmate's claims that Florida's death penalty statute violated Apprendi and Ring failed, as those cases did not apply retroactively. His claim his incompetence precluded his execution under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811 was not ripe for review as he had been not been found incompetent. Execution by lethal injection was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the PCR court's denial of postconviction relief and denied the inmate's petition for habeas relief.


 

369 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Crist v. Fla. Ass'n of Crim. Def. Lawyers, Inc.


No. SC08-02


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


978 So. 2d 134; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 377; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 172



March 13, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal of Judgment of the Circuit Court, in and for Leon County, P. Kevin Davey, Judge, Case No. 2007-CA-002898 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D07-6544.
Crist v. Fla. Ass'n of Crim. Def. Lawyers, 975 So. 2d 428, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 63 (Fla., Jan. 15, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a state association of criminal defense lawyers, sued appellants, the Florida Governor and others, alleging ch. 2007, § 62, Laws of Fla. (the Act), violated art. V, § 18, Fla. Const. The trial court granted the association's petition for a writ of quo warranto; appellants sought review. The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the order as one requiring immediate resolution by the high court, which accepted jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The Act created five Florida Offices of Criminal Conflict and Civil Regional Counsel (OCCCRC) to handle representation in criminal cases where a public defender had a conflict. The association filed a petition for writ of quo warranto, asserting that the Governor exceeded his constitutional authority by appointing the regional counsel for the OCCCRC, and that the Act violated art. V, § 18, Fla. Const., which required that the public defender in each circuit be elected. The high court disagreed. The Act supplanted the prior system of private registry counsel and did not establish de facto public defenders in violation of the Florida Constitution. The OCCCRC did not perform the duties of, compete with, or displace the public defenders. Defendants were guaranteed the right to effective assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment and art. I, § 16, Fla. Const; that right encompassed the right to representation free from actual conflict. The mere creation of the OCCCRC did not adversely impact either the independent judgment of the appointed attorneys or the right of defendants to effective representation under the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the trial court's order and held that the Act did not violate the Florida Constitution by allowing for the appointment and confirmation of the five regional counsel.

Rhodes v. State


No. SC04-31


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


986 So. 2d 501; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 375; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 190



March 13, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised July 3, 2008. Released for Publication July 11, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Rhodes v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1214 (Fla., July 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, W. Douglas Baird, Judge - Case No. CRC84-03982 CFANO-D.
Rhodes v. State, 638 So. 2d 920, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 651 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. He filed a motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, which the Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of strangling a woman. At the PCR hearing, an FBI agent admitted, after checking his bench notes, that hair found in the victim's hand, which he identified at trial as the victim's, was in fact not suitable for testing. The inmate alleged this was exculpatory evidence the State withheld in violation of Brady and the State knowingly presented false evidence in violation of Giglio. The appellate court held that while the agent's trial testimony about the hair was false, as the evidence was neither intentionally withheld nor exculpatory, there was no Brady or Giglio violation. The inmate claimed his sentencing counsel was deficient for failing to call family members and a nurse to testify as to his childhood abuse, since this would have resulted in substantial mitigation and a life sentence. The appellate court disagreed. Defense counsel submitted ample testimony about such abuse. He made a strategic choice not to call certain witnesses, and the testimony the inmate referred to would have been cumulative to that provided by other witnesses. Moreover, such mitigation was overcome by aggravating factors. His other claims were unpreserved or without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fla. Hosp. Waterman, Inc. v. Buster


No. SC06-688, No. SC06-912


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


984 So. 2d 478; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 371; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 154



March 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 25, 2008.
Released for Publication June 10, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Fla. Hosp. Waterman, Inc. v. Buster, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 889 (Fla., May 12, 2008)
Rehearing denied by Notami Hosp. of Fla., Inc. v. Bowen, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1775 (Fla., June 10, 2008)
On remand at Fla. Hosp. Waterman, Inc. v. Buster, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 10251 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., July 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Lake County). Fifth District - Case No. 5D05-2195 And an Appeal from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 1D05-4149.
Notami Hosp. of Fla. v. Bowen, 927 So. 2d 139, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5760 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)
Fla. Hosp. Waterman, Inc. v. Buster, 932 So. 2d 344, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3452 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two malpractice cases, trial courts granted respondents, patients one and two, discovery from petitioners, hospitals one and two. The hospitals appealed. The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that to the extent § 381.028, Fla. Stat., limited art. X, § 25, Fla. Const., it was unconstitutional. The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that art. X, § 25, Fla. Const., did not apply to existing records. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Patients' Right-to-Know About Adverse Medical Incidents Act, § 381.028, Fla. Stat. (2005), implemented Amendment 7, art. X, § 25, Fla. Const., which gave the public access to information about adverse medical incidents involving health care providers. Patient one sought discovery of documents relating to the investigation of the adverse medical incident at issue. Patient two sought discovery of documents relating to the retention or termination of a doctor. Each hospital objected, claiming such information was confidential under statutes predating Amendment 7. The high court agreed with the intermediate appellate courts that Amendment 7 was self-executing. As the statutory guarantee of confidentiality previously afforded reports of adverse medical incidents created by and for peer review committees did not give health care providers a vested right in such confidentiality, application of Amendment 7 to records existing before its passage was constitutional. Section 381.028(2), (3)(j), (5), (6), and (7)(a), Fla. Stat., were unconstitutional, as they curtailed rights granted by Amendment 7; however, they could be severed, leaving the remainder of the statute enforceable.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the first intermediate appellate court's decision that patient one was entitled to discovery from hospital one under Amendment 7, and that § 381.028, Fla. Stat., was unconstitutional in part. As to the denial of patient two's discovery request, the high court reversed the second intermediate appellate court's ruling that Amendment 7 could not be applied retroactively and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Larzelere


No. SC05-611, No. SC06-148


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


979 So. 2d 195; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 273; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 136



February 28, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 5, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, John W. Watson, III, Judge - Case No. 91-2561-CF-A-ES And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Larzelere v. State, 676 So. 2d 394, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 523 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee inmate filed a motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 to vacate her sentence and conviction. The Volusia County Circuit Court (Florida) vacated her death sentence and ordered a new sentencing proceeding. Appellant State sought review; the inmate cross-appealed the denial of her motion to vacate her first-degree murder conviction and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate induced her son to murder her husband, in part so she could collect life insurance. The trial court granted the inmate resentencing due to her counsel's ineffectiveness during the guilt phase. The supreme court agreed that counsel was ineffective; had he conducted a reasonable investigation, he would have learned that the inmate had been sexually abused by her father and physically abused by an ex-husband. Her waiver of mitigation evidence was not knowingly and intelligently made, as she lacked adequate advice; had counsel properly investigated, he would have learned of the abuse and consulted a mental health expert. At the postconviction hearing, such an expert opined that the inmate suffered from multiple mental disorders; this mitigation evidence could have saved her from the death penalty. Counsel was not ineffective during the guilt phase for failing to call expert witnesses in the fields of mental health, concrete, handwriting, and insurance. As to the inmate's habeas petition, her appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to argue that a jury instruction given by the trial court was improper, as such an argument would have lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's order and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.
