Martinez v. State


No. SC06-1597


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


981 So. 2d 449; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 224; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 125



February 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 29, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Martinez v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 805 (Fla., Apr. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. (Dade County). Third District - Case No. 3D04-1521.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted first-degree premeditated murder; he appealed the conviction. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed. It ruled that a self-defense instruction, to which defendant had not objected, was erroneous, but did not constitute fundamental error. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed his girlfriend multiple times in the face, arm, chest, and back. He claimed she had attacked him with scissors. The self-defense instruction stated that the use of force likely to cause death or great bodily harm was not justifiable if defendant was attempting to commit, committing, or escaping after the commission of an attempted murder and/or aggravated battery. The high court held this instruction was erroneous, as there was no independent forcible felony other than the one which defendant claimed he committed in self-defense. However, the erroneous instruction did not deprive defendant of a fair trial and, therefore, fundamental error did not occur. First, his claim of self-defense--that he was fighting for his life--was so weak as to defy credulity, in view of the victim's serious injuries and the 1/4 inch cut he sustained to his pinky finger. Second, self-defense was not his sole defense; he also argued that he was intoxicated and acted in a drunken frenzy rather than with premeditation. The high court disapproved of those decisions that held that an erroneous reading of the forcible-felony instruction always constituted fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bowles v. State


No. SC05-2264, No. SC06-1666


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


979 So. 2d 182; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 214; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 121



February 14, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 3, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Bowles v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 687 (Fla., Apr. 3, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Bowles v. Sec'y for the Dep't of Corr., 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 12695 (11th Cir. Fla., June 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Jack Marvin Schemer, Judge - Case No. 94-12188-CFA And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Bowles v. State, 804 So. 2d 1173, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2007 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate pled guilty to premeditated first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. Pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, he petitioned the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) to vacate his death sentence. The postconviction court denied relief. The inmate petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate dropped a concrete block on the victim's head and strangled him to death. He claimed his trial counsel were ineffective for failing to present an expert to testify to mental mitigation. The appellate court held that the decision not to call the psychologist was a reasonable strategic decision, as her testimony could have opened the door to other damaging testimony. Due to negative aspects of her opinion, it was also a reasonable strategic decision to not present her testimony at the Spencer hearing. Based on the inmate's confession, counsel were not ineffective in not calling an expert to refute the opinion of the State's expert as to the heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC) aggravator. The inmate presented no factual basis under Rule 3.851(e)(1) for his claim counsel were deficient in presenting mental mitigation. His Apprendi, Ring, and Crawford claims were meritless. As the inmate did not show a reasonable probability that the prosecutor's comments affected the verdict, and as photos of the victim were properly admitted to support the applicability of the HAC aggravator, appellate counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise meritless claims based on these issues.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the postconviction court and denied relief on all asserted claims.

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


980 So. 2d 473; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 179; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 102



February 14, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 16, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Carter v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 682 (Fla., Apr. 16, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Carter v. Florida, 555 U.S. 947, 129 S. Ct. 400, 172 L. Ed. 2d 292, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7464 (Oct. 14, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Carter v. State, 175 So. 3d 761, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1434 (Fla., July 2, 2015)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Lance M. Day, Judge - Case No. 04-730 CFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of premeditated and felony murder (with burglary as the predicate felony) for each of three killings. The Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) followed the jury's recommendation and imposed death sentences for two of the murders and life in prison for the third. Defendant appealed his convictions and death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to his girlfriend's home and fatally shot her, her new boyfriend, and her minor child. He claimed that the child was shot accidentally, and that before the shootings, he had taken antidepressant pills and drank several glasses of whiskey. The high court rejected his claim that § 775.051, Fla. Stat. (2002), which barred the defense of voluntary intoxication, was unconstitutional. (2002), as to the adults and not as to the child, as the adults were the victims defendant originally targeted. The State's promise to Mexico not to execute defendant was conditioned on Mexico's sending him to Florida, which it did not do. As the jury unanimously convicted defendant of three murders, which was basis for the trial court's finding of the prior violent felony conviction aggravator, there was no Ring violation. The death sentences were proportionate.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentences.

Doorbal v. State, 837 So. 2d 940, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 107 (Fla., Jan. 30, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which denied the inmate's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion to vacate his convictions on two counts of first-degree murder and his sentences of death. The inmate also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus. Green v. State


No. SC05-2265, No. SC06-1533


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


975 So. 2d 1090; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 137



January 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Green v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 177 (Fla., Jan. 31, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Bruce W. Jacobus, Judge - Case No. 89-4942-CFA And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Green v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1898 (Fla., Oct. 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. He filed a motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The Brevard County Circuit Court (Florida) upheld the inmate's conviction but granted him a new penalty phase. The inmate appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellee State cross-appealed, challenging the order granting the inmate a new penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: The inmate robbed and murdered a man. The high court held that his newly discovered evidence claim failed, as the recantations of three of the State's witnesses did not create a reasonable probability of acquittal on retrial. His claim of a Brady violation failed, as he did not prove materiality. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to obtain a file from his predecessor, impeach a witness, or challenge a juror. The trial court properly denied relief with regard to dog tracking evidence. Fla. R. Bar 4-3.5(d)(4), which barred defense counsel from interviewing jurors, was constitutional. Summary denial of the inmate's claims of juror misconduct and counsel's failure to challenge cross-race identification was proper. As his New York youthful offender robbery adjudication was not a conviction, it did not satisfy the "prior violent felony conviction aggravator," § 921.141(5)(b), Fla. Stat. (1987). Counsel's ineffectiveness in not discovering this entitled the inmate to a new penalty phase. As to his habeas petition, a proportionality reevaluation was not warranted; lethal injection was not cruel and unusual punishment; and his claim of incompetency to be executed was not ripe.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the trial court's order upholding the inmate's first-degree murder conviction and granting a new penalty phase. It denied the inmate's petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Pooler v. State


No. SC05-2191


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


980 So. 2d 460; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 136; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 81



January 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 17, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Pooler v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 749 (Fla., Apr. 17, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pooler v. Florida, 555 U.S. 911, 129 S. Ct. 255, 172 L. Ed. 2d 192, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6029 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Jorge Labarga Judge - Case No. 95-1117CFA02.
Pooler v. State, 704 So. 2d 1375, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1854 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised two issues on appeal: that trial counsel provided constitutionally ineffective assistance (U.S. Const. amend. VI), and that the trial court erred in summarily denying his postconviction claims. The supreme court disagreed. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to investigate and present a voluntary intoxication defense. None of the evidence established appellant was intoxicated at the time of the murder, and the testimony of a detective established that he was not intoxicated just a few hours before the murder. Counsel was also not ineffective for failing to investigate and present evidence of appellant's history of alcohol abuse and dependency in support of the impaired capacity mitigator. Neither appellant nor his family indicated to counsel that appellant had a substance abuse problem or that he had been drinking at the time of the shooting. The trial court did not err in summarily denying appellant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failure to object to the introduction of gruesome photographs. Counsel challenged the admission of the photographs by written motion when they were offered into evidence by the State.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order denying appellant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed.


 

381 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



James v. State


No. SC06-426


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


974 So. 2d 365; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 53; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 67



January 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 21, 2008.
Rehearing denied by James v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2013 (Fla., Oct. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, O. H. Eaton, Jr., Judge - Case No. 93-3237-CFA.
James v. State, 695 So. 2d 1229, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 559 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida), which denied the inmate's motion for reappointment of Capital Collateral Regional Counsel and reinstatement of a motion to vacate a sentence of death under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether the trial court properly denied reappointment of collateral counsel for the inmate to resume postconviction proceedings after the inmate had discharged his original collateral counsel and dismissed his postconviction proceedings more than two and a half years prior to his motion. The supreme court affirmed. The inmate had the right initially to waive his right to counsel on his postconviction claims so long as the waiver was made voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently. The record established that when the inmate sought to waive counsel, the waiver was being made in such a manner. After waiving counsel, the inmate had sought a dismissal of the postconviction proceedings, fully aware of the fact that doing so would result in a waiver of any legal barriers to the State's ability to carry out the death sentence. The fact that the inmate later changed his mind was not a sufficient basis for setting aside the previous waiver.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's order.

Ward v. State


No. SC06-1764


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


986 So. 2d 479; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 39; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 564



January 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised July 3, 2008. Released for Publication July 11, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Ward v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1213 (Fla., July 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case No. 3D05-1277. (Dade County).
Ward v. State, 936 So. 2d 1143, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13682 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought to commit petitioner offender as a sexually violent predator under the Jimmy Ryce Act. The trial court granted the petition; petitioner appealed. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) denied relief, but certified this question: could one not in custody on January 1, 1999, be committed under the Act if he was sentenced to total confinement after January 1, 1999, but the qualifying conviction occurred before that date?


OVERVIEW: In 1976, petitioner was convicted of two counts of rape and imprisoned; he was released in 1993. In 2004, he was sentenced to three years for burglary; no sexual offense was involved in that charge. The State then moved to civilly commit him under Florida's Jimmy Ryce Act, §§ 394.910-.931, Fla. Stat. (2004). The trial court ruled that one incarcerated after the effective date of the Act (January 1, 1999) for an offense not defined as a sexually violent offense, but who had been convicted previously of a sexually violent offense and had been released at the end of his sentence before January 1, 1999, was subject to civil commitment under the Act. Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition. The intermediate appellate court ruled that a person was subject to the Act whatever the reason for his or her qualifying confinement. The high court rejected petitioner's argument that to be subject to the Act his current conviction had to be for a sexual offense. Under its plain language, the Act applied to all persons who were then incarcerated--regardless of the nature of the crime for which they were imprisoned--and who at some point in the past had been convicted of a sexually violent offense.


OUTCOME: The high court answered the certified question in the affirmative, lifted the stay on petitioner's commitment proceedings in the trial court, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


 

383 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Raborn v. Menotte


No. SC06-2461


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


974 So. 2d 328; 2008 Fla. LEXIS 3; 33 Fla. L. Weekly S 21



January 10, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 05-16260-DD.
Raborn v. Menotte (In re Raborn), 470 F.3d 1319, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 29217 (11th Cir. Fla., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A federal district court agreed with appellee bankruptcy trustee that a farm deeded in trust was owned by appellant beneficiary/debtor in fee simple. The U.S. Court of Appeals for Eleventh Circuit certified these questions: (1) whether under former § 689.07(1), Fla. Stat., a deed to a trustee of an unrecorded trust conveyed only legal title to the property to the grantee as trustee; (2) whether an amendment to § 689.07(1) applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: The grantors recorded a deed to a trustee of a trust identified in the deed by name and date; the deed referred to the unrecorded trust agreement, the settlors, and beneficiaries. The beneficiary/debtor, who was also the trustee of the trust, filed bankruptcy. The district court held that under § 689.07(1) (2001), the deed conveyed fee simple title to the beneficiary/debtor individually, rather than conveying mere legal title to him in his capacity as trustee of the trust. Then, § 689.07 was amended to provide that language in a deed identifying the trust by either name or date would cause a conveyance to be in trust; the amendment applied retroactively. On a second appeal from the bankruptcy court, the district court held that the deed did not reflect a "contrary intention" of the grantors to convey the property in trust, and that retroactive application of the amendment would be unconstitutional. The state's high court held that as the deed clearly expressed that the grantors intended to deed their farm to the beneficiary/debtor in trust, the deed fell under the "contrary intention" exception in former § 689.07(1); thus, the beneficiary/debtor held mere legal title as trustee.


OUTCOME: The instant court answered the first certified question in the affirmative. Under former § 689.07(1), Fla. Stat. (2001), the deed conveyed mere legal title to the beneficiary/debtor as trustee grantee. Having answered this first question, it declined to answer the second certified question as it was moot.


 

384 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Chames v. DeMayo


No. SC06-1671, No. SC06-2187


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


972 So. 2d 850; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2393; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 820



December 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Chames v. DeMayo, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 50 (Fla., Jan. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. (Dade County). Third District - Case No. 3D04-117.
DeMayo v. Chames, 934 So. 2d 548, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 9714 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION:  The court reaffirmed its previous holdings that a waiver of the homestead exemption in an unsecured agreement was unenforceable. It approved the decision below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an attorney and her law firm, obtained a lien and final judgment against respondent former client, who had waived his homestead exemption in a retainer agreement. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that the client's waiver of the homestead exemption of Art. X, § 4(a), Fla. Const. was invalid. On appeal, the court considered the certified question of whether the exemption from forced sale of a homestead could be waived.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that in previous decisions, it had held that a waiver of the homestead exemption in an unsecured agreement was unenforceable. It declined to depart from that precedent. A 1985 amendment replacing the phrase "the head of a family" with "a natural person" did not change the purpose of the exemption from one protecting the family into a personal right that could be waived. As for the attorney's argument that the court's position conflicted with the law in other states, given the variety of state homestead provisions, comparisons to other jurisdictions were difficult and generally of limited value. Furthermore, the court's review did not reveal a shift toward permitting a waiver of the homestead or personal property exemptions in an executory contract. Finally, the court's previous decisions did not contradict the trend toward allowing waivers of constitutional rights, but were consistent with holdings that such waivers had to be knowing, intelligent, and voluntary. Waivers of the homestead exemption could be accomplished by mortgage, sale, or gift under Art. X, § 4(c), Fla. Const.; it was a general waiver in an otherwise unsecured instrument that was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court reaffirmed its previous holdings that a waiver of the homestead exemption in an unsecured agreement was unenforceable. It approved the decision below.

Merck v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


975 So. 2d 1054; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2271; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 789



December 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 11, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Merck v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 269 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Merck v. Florida, 555 U.S. 840, 129 S. Ct. 73, 172 L. Ed. 2d 66, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7203 (Oct. 6, 2008)
Writ denied by Merck v. State, 60 So. 3d 387, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 783 (Fla., Mar. 31, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Merck v. State, 124 So. 3d 785, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 88 (Fla., 2013)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Merck v. Sec'y, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 152243 (M.D. Fla., Oct. 27, 2014)
Appeal dismissed by, Without prejudice Merck v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 31 (Fla., Jan. 8, 2016)
Post-conviction proceeding at Merck v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 1479 (Fla., May 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Brandt C. Downey, III, Judge - Case No. CRC 91-16659 CFANO.
Merck v. State, 763 So. 2d 295, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1447 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a second remand for resentencing, the Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) sentenced defendant to death, finding two aggravating factors, one statutory mitigating factor, and three nonstatutory mitigating factors. Defendant again appealed, raising claims relating to the exclusion of evidence, improper remarks by the State during the penalty phase, the weight given to the mitigating factors, and to the sentence itself.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of defendant's claims and the evidence, his death sentence was again upheld. First, the relevant case law supported the exclusion of proffered expert testimony regarding Florida's parole procedures and defendant's likelihood of being paroled. Second, the alleged excluded testimony regarding the circumstances of the murder was presented to the jury, with the exception of testimony that was not proffered. Thus, absent a proffer, a claim regarding the testimony was denied. Third, neither the mercy comments, "golden rule" arguments, nor the State's denigration of defendant's mitigation strategy amounted to reversible or fundamental error which denied defendant a fair penalty hearing. Fourth, the trial judge's rejection of two of defendant's proposed mitigating factors was supported by competent, substantial evidence. Moreover, the assignments of weight to the established mitigating factors did not appear unreasonable or arbitrary. Fifth, given the totality of the evidence, the sentence was proportionate. And, finally, as the instant court has previously rejected claims that Florida's capital sentencing scheme is unconstitutional, no relief was granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Overton v. State


No. SC04-2071, No. SC05-964, No. SC06-237


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


976 So. 2d 536; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2204; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 775



November 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Overton v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 505 (Fla., Feb. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Appeals from the Circuit Court in and for Monroe County, Mark H. Jones, Judge - Case No. CFP-96-30167 And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Overton v. State, 801 So. 2d 877, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1808 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appeals from the Circuit Court in and for Monroe County (Florida), appellant sought review of the denial of his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, and appealed the trial court's denial of his second motion for postconviction DNA testing under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853. Finally, he petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that appellant's claims with regard to his failure to receive a full and fair evidentiary hearing at the postconviction stage were without merit. With regard to the questioning by the trial court, there was no bias displayed by the trial court in favor of either the State or appellant, and the trial court elicited information that was clearly helpful to him, including information relating to defense counsel's investigation of an alibi defense. The trial court did not err in the partial denial of a Rule 3.853 motion which requested DNA testing of hairs attached to tape used to bind a victim. Evidence that the hairs came from someone other than appellant or the victims would fail to prove or disprove any theory in the case because it was impossible to establish when or how the hairs could have become attached to the tape. As to the habeas corpus claim, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to present on appeal the improper denial of a motion to change venue, as the pre-trial publicity was factual rather than inflammatory, and most of the prospective jurors assured the trial court that they could be impartial despite any extrinsic knowledge.


OUTCOME: Both the trial court's denial of appellant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion for postconviction relief and the denial of his second Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853 motion for postconviction DNA testing were affirmed. His petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Stephens v. State


No. SC05-1301, No. SC06-1729


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


975 So. 2d 405; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2171; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 735



November 15, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stephens v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 175 (Fla., Feb. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Jack Marvin Schemer, Judge - Case No. 97-9232-CF And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Stephens v. State, 787 So. 2d 747, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 520 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) to armed kidnapping, armed robbery, and related crimes and was convicted of first degree murder and armed robbery. He was sentenced to death and consecutive and concurrent life sentences. His convictions and sentence were affirmed, and the trial court denied his motion to vacate his death sentence. He appealed and filed a habeas corpus petition in the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said counsel did not present available mitigation evidence. The supreme court held the strategic choice to use lay testimony on good aspects of defendant's life, rather than contradictory expert testimony, was not ineffective. Not trying to lessen an aggravating prior conviction's weight was not ineffective when counsel thought this could backfire. Defendant did not show he was ineffectively advised to plead guilty, as he did not show he would have insisted on a trial, or that his pleas were involuntary, nor did he show a defense to the charges would succeed. Counsel was deficient for not attending depositions and pleading defendant guilty to armed kidnapping, but no prejudice was shown. Counsel's representation of defendant's codefendant in a burglary used as an aggravator against defendant created no conflict of interest. Defendant was not entitled to a writ of habeas corpus because (1) appellate counsel's ineffectiveness was not shown, and (2) instructions on the heinous, atrocious, or cruel, pecuniary gain, "in the course of a felony" or "victim under 12 years of age" aggravators were not improper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, and defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Lawrence v. State


No. SC06-352, No. SC06-1152


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 294; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2012; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 699



November 1, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul Rasmussen, Judge - Case No. 57-98-270-CFA-B And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Lawrence v. State, 846 So. 2d 440, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 386 (Fla., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida), which denied his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. The inmate also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The 18-year-old inmate went with the inmate and the co-defendant into the woods, where they drank alcoholic beverages, had sex with her, and then fatally shot her. Thereafter, they cut her body, took photos, and buried her. The inmate eventually confessed, and he was convicted and sentenced to death. His direct appeal resulted in an affirmance, and his postconviction relief motion was denied. The inmate's claim of ineffectiveness of trial counsel during the guilt phase failed, as the evidence did not support his claim that his counsel failed to adequately advise him of an available defense, and counsel's decision not to seek suppression was a strategic one. Claims of ineffectiveness during the penalty phase failed, as they were based on tactical decisions and there was no cause for counsel to have requested a competency evaluation at that time. There were no cumulative errors, and claims raised in the habeas corpus matter were procedurally barred or previously denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order which denied the inmate's postconviction relief motion, and the court also denied the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Lightbourne v. McCollum


No. SC06-2391


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 326; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2255; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 687



November 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication November 7, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Lightbourne v. McCollum, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2125 (Fla., Nov. 7, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lightbourne v. McCollum, 128 S. Ct. 2485, 171 L. Ed. 2d 777, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4194 (U.S., 2008)
Related proceeding at Walton v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 136 (Fla., Jan. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lightbourne v. State, 956 So. 2d 456, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 724 (Fla., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a death row inmate and other such inmates, filed an all writs petition which challenged the constitutionality of Florida's lethal injection (LI) procedures under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Art. I, § 17, Fla. Const. The named inmate appealed from an order of a circuit court (Florida), which denied his challenge to the LI procedure as well as other claims arising from his criminal matter. The court heard both matters together.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's direct appeal from his conviction and sentence, and his postconviction relief motions, were denied. After another inmate's execution by LI took an unusually long time, the all writs petition was filed. An investigation led to revisions by the Department of Corrections in its LI procedures, and the trial court thereafter denied the inmate's constitutional challenge in a previously pending matter. On appeal of that ruling and pursuant to the all writs petition, the court found that the inmate was not denied a full and fair hearing, as he was given ample time to raise issues regarding the other inmate's execution and the revised LI procedures. Although the trial court erred in excluding two memoranda, as neither was privileged under § 119.071(d)1, Fla. Stat. (2006), and any privilege was waived, the court indicated that it would consider them in ruling on the LI issue. The court noted that based on the chemicals used, the training and certification, and the assessment of consciousness, the LI method of execution based on the revised procedure was not constitutionally violative. The inmate did not show a substantial, foreseeable, or unnecessary risk of pain in the process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that denied the inmate's requested relief, and it denied the all writs petition.

Schwab v. State


No. SC07-1603


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 318; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2011; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 697



November 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 7, 2007.
Stay denied by Schwab v. State, 973 So. 2d 427, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2013 (Fla., 2007)
Stay granted by Schwab v. Florida, 128 S. Ct. 644, 169 L. Ed. 2d 416, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12320 (U.S., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Schwab v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 55 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Schwab v. Florida, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4273 (U.S., May 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Charles M. Holcomb, Judge - Case No. 05-1991-7249-AXXX.
Schwab v. State, 814 So. 2d 402, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 537 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and other crimes and was sentenced to death. His second motion for postconviction relief alleged (1) execution by lethal injection violated the Eighth Amendment, and (2) newly discovered evidence about his brain impairment made his death sentence constitutionally unreliable. Appellee State opposed the motion, and the Brevard County Circuit Court (Florida) denied it. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate kidnapped, sexually battered, and murdered an 11-year-old boy. The high court held that as the inmate's Eighth Amendment claim was based on facts that occurred during a recent lethal injection in which complications arose, the claim was not, as the State argued, procedurally barred. After that execution, the high court had ordered a lower court to determine the validity of execution by lethal injection. The postconviction court erred in not taking judicial notice of that case under § 90.202(6), Fla. Stat. (2006), but the error was harmless, because it considered all of the evidence presented in that case when reviewing the Eighth Amendment challenge. In view of the amended protocols adopted for administering lethal injections, this method of execution did not violate the Eighth Amendment. The inmate's claim of newly discovered evidence regarding his neurological impairment was procedurally barred, as he could have, but did not, present evidence of his alleged brain damage in his initial postconviction proceeding. Further, new research studies were not "newly discovered evidence," and they did not support his claim that brain damage caused him to commit the crimes.


OUTCOME: The order denying postconviction relief was affirmed.

Barnhill v. State


No. SC06-275, No. SC06-1803


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


971 So. 2d 106; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1954; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 671



October 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 13, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Barnhill v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2463 (Fla., Dec. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Kenneth R. Lester, Jr., Judge - Case No. 95-2932-CFA. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Barnhill v. State, 834 So. 2d 836, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1959 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had pled no contest, appealed the denial of his motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 by the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida). He also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant argued that trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance by, inter alia, failing to move to withdraw defendant's guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed the 84-year-old victim and then stole his money, wallet, keys, and car. Defendant's motion to suppress a statement to police and evidence obtained during his arrest was denied. Defendant pled no contest over counsel's objections. The record reflects counsel was not deficient by failing to file a motion to withdraw the guilty plea based on a strategic decision. When counsel noticed defendant's changed mental state, they immediately advised the court and medical assistance was provided. Because a statement made by the judge would not have led a reasonable person to believe he or she would not receive a fair trial, counsel was not ineffective for failing to move to disqualify the judge. The record supported the court's findings that counsel adequately investigated and prepared mitigating evidence for the penalty phase. The testimony that was presented at the postconviction hearing was cumulative to and corroborated the evidence that was presented at the penalty phase, and the fact that there were other witnesses available who could have testified concerning defendant's upbringing and his mental health did not demonstrate that counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied. Defendant's claim for relief as to lethal injection was denied without prejudice to pursue any available remedies he might have in the appropriate trial court.

 

395 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Sigler


No. SC04-1934


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 835; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1893; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 607



October 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 18, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. (Broward County). Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-4799.
Sigler v. State, 881 So. 2d 14, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10485 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was acquitted of first-degree murder and convicted of second-degree murder. The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed; it directed entry of judgment for third-degree murder. The trial court complied; the State and defendant appealed. The intermediate appellate court reversed its prior ruling, finding that its application of § 924.34, Fla. Stat. (2001), was contrary to the right to a jury trial. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a prison escapee, was a passenger in a car that was fleeing police. The driver hit another car, killing its driver. The intermediate appellate court, finding no evidence the driver had evil intent directed at the victim, held the depraved mind second-degree murder conviction lacked evidentiary support. Under § 924.34, it directed entry of judgment on the lesser-included offense of third-degree murder, as the underlying crime supporting this charge was harboring an escapee, defendant was a perpetrator of that crime, and thus a principal in a homicide committed to further a common criminal plan. In reversing itself, it held that § 924.34 violated the Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial under Apprendi and Blakely to the extent it was read as allowing an appellate court, not a jury, to make a finding as to an element of the offense. The high court agreed. In convicting defendant of depraved mind second-degree murder, the jury had not found that he committed a felony, an essential element of third-degree murder. But if all of the elements of a lesser offense had been determined by the jury, appellate courts could properly direct a judgment for that offense under § 924.34.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court for resolution by a jury of the issue of whether defendant was guilty of third-degree murder.

Green v. State


No. SC05-2265, No. SC06-1533


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2007 Fla. LEXIS 1898; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 619

Substituted opinion at Green v. State, 975 So. 2d 1090, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 137 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Bruce W. Jacobus, Judge - Case No. 89-4942-CFA And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Green v. State, 641 So. 2d 391, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1003 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Brevard County Circuit Court (Florida) granted defendant's motion to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence, in part, specifically, granting him a new penalty phase hearing. He thus appealed from that part of the order which denied his remaining claims for relief, and the State cross-appealed, challenging the grant of a new penalty phase hearing. Defendant also filed a petition for habeas relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his remaining postconviction claims, but upon review, the instant court found that such were properly denied. But, defendant was properly granted a new sentencing phase hearing based on his trial counsel's deficient performance by failing to investigate a juvenile New York robbery case, as a youthful offender adjudication was not a "conviction" and, therefore, could not satisfy the prior violent felony conviction aggravator under Florida's death penalty statute. Additionally, the New York case file contained some potentially mitigating information and could have been used to clear up the confusion over whether defendant was convicted of armed robbery or simple robbery. Finally, defendant was not entitled to habeas relief, as: (1) he could not use his petition as an additional appeal of issues that could have been or were raised on appeal or in other postconviction motions; (2) he failed to support his claim for an additional proportionality review of his sentence with newly discovered evidence; (3) death by lethal injection did not amount to cruel and unusual punishment; and (4) his claim of incompetency at the time of execution was unripe.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction was upheld and the trial court's order granting a new penalty phase was affirmed. But, the trial court properly denied his remaining post-conviction claims. Finally, defendant's request for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

397 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Frances v. State


No. SC05-892


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


970 So. 2d 806; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1897; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 613



October 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Frances v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2452 (Fla., Dec. 6, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Frances v. Florida, 553 U.S. 1039, 128 S. Ct. 2441, 171 L. Ed. 2d 241, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3946 (May 12, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Frances v. State, 143 So. 3d 340, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1315 (Fla., Apr. 17, 2014)
Related proceeding at, Dismissed by State v. Frances, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1140 (Fla., May 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, John H. Adams, Sr., Judge - Case No. 00CF-16204.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder, robbery, and two counts of petit theft. The Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) sentenced defendant death for both murders and a consecutive 15 years for robbery and 60 days for the petit thefts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly restricted his presentation of evidence relevant to his relative culpability and what sentence he should receive. The supreme court found no abuse of discretion, noting that, inter alia, some of the evidence was presented through the testimony or videotaped depositions of the individuals with first-hand knowledge of the information. Defendant also argued that the trial court improperly found the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravating circumstance (HAC), excluded mitigating evidence, and concluded that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating ones. The supreme court disagreed, noting that, inter alia, the HAC finding was supported by evidence that the strangled victims would have been conscious and aware of what was happening to them for at least one or two minutes, and that one victim was attacked in her own home by people she knew. The lack of criminal history factor was also considered, but discounted because defendant helped his brother with disposing of a body in another murder. Finally, the court declined to find the death sentenced disproportionate or the capital sentencing statute unconstitutional under Ring.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


 

398 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Grim v. State


No. SC06-122, No. SC06-1575


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


971 So. 2d 85; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1842; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 593



October 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Grim v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2462 (Fla., Dec. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul Rasmussen, Judge - Case No. 98-510-CFA And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Grim v. State, 841 So. 2d 455, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 384 (Fla., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Santa Rosa County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief in a case where defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and sexual battery upon a person 12-years-old or older with the use of a deadly weapon, and defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed the denial of that motion and filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus with the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen with the victim early one morning. The victim's bookkeeper then could not locate the victim that same morning. Police searched defendant's house, but saw no signs of a struggle. That afternoon witnesses saw defendant in a store at the foot of a bridge. One witness saw his car parked on the bridge with the doors and the trunk open. The victim was soon found floating in a nearby bay. The victim had suffered blunt force trauma and 11 stab wounds to the chest. Evidence at defendant's residence tied him to the killing. He was tried and found guilty of first-degree murder and a sexual battery count. He told his attorneys not to present mitigating evidence. The trial court found he did so freely, knowingly, and voluntarily. Special counsel presented mitigation evidence. Defendant was sentenced to death; his convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. The state supreme court then found that no error occurred when the trial court denied his postconviction relief motion because defendant did not show a Brady violation, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, any other ground meriting relief, or that he was entitled to a writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the motion for postconviction was affirmed, and the state supreme court denied his habeas corpus petition.

 

399 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Insko v. State


No. SC06-1619


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 992; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1676; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 559



September 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 26, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Insko v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2262 (Fla., Nov. 26, 2007)
Related proceeding at Insko v. State (In re Insko), 29 So. 3d 1127, 2010 Fla. App. LEXIS 2721 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 2D05-1221. (Hillsborough County).
Insko v. State, 933 So. 2d 679, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11820 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the judgment of the Hillsborough County Circuit Court, and held that under § 800.04(6)(a)(2) and (b), Fla. Stat. (2001), a defendant's age was a sentencing enhancement, as opposed to an element of the crime, but certified a question relevant to the same as one of great public importance. Thus, the matter came before the instant court for review.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of the question presented, the instant court found that the age of a defendant was not a sentencing enhancement, but an element of the crime. Specifically, the age of a defendant under § 800.04(6) was necessary to the provision criminalizing the conduct and ascribing the degree of the crime. It was therefore an element of second- and third-degree felony lewd or lascivious conduct. The State's contention that the age of the defendant was not an element in § 800.04(6), Fla. Stat. (2001) failed to recognize the integral role the fact played in defining the crime. Further, unless a defendant who committed the crime of lewd or lascivious conduct was at least eighteen years old at the time of the offense, he could not be convicted of a second-degree felony. But, despite this, because defendant failed to object to preserve any error, he waived any claim to relief.


OUTCOME: In answering the certified question, the age of a defendant was an element of the crime. But, the Second District's affirmance of the circuit court's judgment was approved, as defendant waived any claim for relief long before retrial.


 

400 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox


No. SC06-2494


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 815; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1678; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 564



September 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D05-4111. (Santa Rosa County).
Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox, 943 So. 2d 823, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17891 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION:  The decision of the First District was quashed and the case was remanded for further proceedings. Moreover, the decision of the Fourth District in Mierzwa was disapproved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under § 627.702(1), Fla. Stat. (2004), the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) found petitioner insurer liable to respondent insured for the the face amount of the policy covering the insured's property, no matter what other facts are involved as to the cost of repairs or replacement. The insurer thus sought further review, and a question relative to the issue of their liability was certified as one of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether § 627.702, Fla. Stat. (2004) required an insurer to pay the face amount of a policy to an owner of a building deemed a total loss when the building was damaged in part by a covered peril, but was significantly damaged by an excluded peril. On review, the insurer was not contesting the value of the property, but whether it was liable for the entire loss when the covered peril alone did not cause a total loss, but was only responsible for a relatively small amount of the damage. Contrary to the First District, the instant court held that the insurer was only liable for that part of a covered peril for which a premium was paid. Moreover, the instant court did not find that the plain language of the statute intended that if a covered peril caused part of a total loss, that the insurer was mandated to pay for the total loss.


OUTCOME: The decision of the First District was quashed and the case was remanded for further proceedings. Moreover, the decision of the Fourth District in Mierzwa was disapproved.
